Instance variable and local variable: 
Instance Variables : 
1. Such variables which are directly created within a class outside any block 
or method. 
2. For every object separated copy of instance variables will be created. 
3. Memory for these variables would be given on the heap area, so jvm would 
perform 
initialisation with default values. 
4. Variables whose value changes from Object to object (i.e for every new 
object new 
memory map on heap and new values it will hold) 
public class Student{ 
private String sname; 
private int sid; /// Instance varibales 
private int sage; 
public Student(String sname,int sid,int sage){ 
this.sname=sname; this.sid=sid; this.sage=sage; 
} 
} 
Note : If we make instance variable as final, then compulsorily we should 
perform 
initialisation explicitly jvm wont provide default values. (bcz final variables 
act constant - 
watch the class lecture on final keyword) 
Whether we use or not otherwise we get compile time error. 
Instance Variable: When we declared the variable inside the class and above 
the method the variable is called instance variable. 
EX: 
Class ABC 
{ 
} 
int a =10 
If we doesn’t assign any 
value in to the Instance 
variable default it will 
take 0 Zero 
Local variables : 
1. Variables which are a part of method signature, method body and those 
variables are 
called as "Local variables". (for the first time we declare within a method or 
any 
block) 
2. Variables which are created by the programmer to meet the temporary 
requirements 
are called "local variables". 
3. Memory for those variables will be given on the stack memory,jvm will 
not initialise 
any value for those variables, compulsorily the user should initialise the 
value. 
eg:: class Test{ 
public static void main(String... args){ 
int i; // local variable 
System.out.println("Hello"); 
} 
} 
Note : If the local variables are final then we should initialise before we 
use.(final keyword 
topic done during Inheritance concept kindly watch) 
The only modifier applicable for local variables is final,if we use any other 
modifier 
it would result in a compile time error. 
Local Variable:  When we declare the Variable inside the class and in side 
method is class Local variable.

flow

Delegation:  
Delegation is simply passing a duty off to someone/something else.  
Delegation can be an alternative to inheritance. 
Delegation means that you use an object of another class as an instance variable, 
and forward messages to the instance. 
Exp: 1 
class Calculator11 
{ 
 public int add(int num1,int num2) 
 { 
  int result = num1 +num2; 
  return result; 
 } 
} 
public class Delegation  
{ 
   public static void main(String[] args)  
   { 
    int num1 = 35; 
    int num2 = 15; 
    Calculator11 cal = new Calculator11(); 
    int result = cal.add(num1,num2);  
//Delegation 
    System.out.println(result); 
   } 
} 
Exp:2 
class RealPrinter  
{ 
    // the "delegate" 
   int print() 
    { 
       int a,b,c; 
       a=30; b=20; 
       c= a+b; 
       return c; 
    } 
} 
class Printer { 
    // the "delegator" 
    RealPrinter p = new RealPrinter(); 
    // create the delegate 
    void print() 
    {   
      int c = p.print(); // delegation 
      System.out.println(c); 
    } 
} 
public class Del_2 { 
    // To the outside world it looks like Printer 
actually prints. 
public static void main(String[] args) 
    { 
        Printer printer = new Printer(); 
        printer.print(); 
    } 
} 
Method Over Loading (Compile Time Polymorphism): Method Over Loading 
(Compile Time Polymorphism) is defined as the use of the same method name 
with different parameters values. 
Exp 1: 
  class Calculation 
{ 
 // Adding two Numbers 
 public int add(int num1,int num2) 
 { 
  int result = num1+num2; 
  return result; 
 } 
 //Adding three Numbers and doing average 
 public int add(int a,int b,int c) 
 { 
  int result = (a+b+c/3); 
  return result; 
 } 
    public void add() 
 { 
  int n; 
  int i =0;int j=0;n=9; 
  while(i<n) 
  { 
    for(j=0;j<n;j++) 
   { 
    if(i==0||j==0||i==(n-1)||j==(n-1)||i==j||i+j==(n-1)) 
    { 
     System.out.print("*"); 
    } 
    else 
    { 
     System.out.print(" "); 
    } 
    } 
   i++; 
   System.out.println(); 
  } 
 } 
    public String add(String str1,String str2) 
    { 
     String c = str1.concat(str2); 
     return c; 
    } 
}

{ 
  public static void main(String[] args)  
  { 
 Calculation cal = new Calculation(); 
 cal.add();

 int Avg = cal.add(10, 20, 30); 
 String Res = cal.add("Sai "," Teja"); 
 System.out.println(A1); 
 System.out.println(Avg); 
 System.out.println(Res); 
  } 
}

Scanner Class : 
The Scanner class is used to get user input, and it is found in the java.util package. 
To use the Scanner class, create an object of the class and use any of the available 
methods found in the Scanner class documentation. In our example, we will use 
the nextLine() method, which is used to read Strings:

Array: Arrays are used to store multiple values in a single variable, instead of 
declaring separate variables for each value. 
Array is index based Ds to Store large amount of Homogenous Data 
To declare an array, define the variable type with square brackets [ ]. 
In Java Array is Treated as Object. 
Advantage: 
Creation is simple and retrieving and managing data is simple 
Ex: 
int a[ ] = new int [10];

1 Dimensional array: 
1.In Java, an array is a container object that holds a fixed number of values of a 
single type. The length of an array is established when the array is created. After 
creation, its length is fixed. 
Here's an example of how you can create and initialize an array of integers in 
Java: 
int[] arr = new int[5];  // creates an array with a length of 5 
arr[0] = 1;  // assign the value 1 to the first element of the array 
arr[1] = 2;  // assign the value 2 to the second element of the array 
arr[2] = 3;  // assign the value 3 to the third element of the array 
arr[3] = 4;  // assign the value 4 to the fourth element of the array 
Memory Allocation: 
Assigned      
value 
arr[4] = 5;  // assign the value 5 to the fifth element of the array 
0              
1          
1  
2 
2   
3   
4 
3 
4   
5 
Index 
Value 
2. You can also use the shortcut syntax to create and initialize an array in one line: 
int[] arr = {1, 2, 3, 4, 5};    // creates an array and initializes its elements with the 
given values 
3. Arrays in Java are indexed, which means you can access the elements of an 
array by their position in the array. The index of the first element is 0, the index 
of the second element is 1, and so on. 
You can access the elements of an array using the array access operator ([]). For 
example: 
int firstElement = arr[0];  // gets the value of the first element (1) 
int secondElement = arr[1];  // gets the value of the second element (2) 
4. You can also use a loop to iterate over the elements of an array: 
This will print the elements of the array to the console, one element per line. 
Ex: Code 
for (int i = 0; i < arr.length; i++)  
{ 
  int element = arr[i]; 
  System.out.println(element); 
} 
import java.util.Scanner; 
public class LaunchAr { 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 { 
          int []a=new int[5]; 
          System.out.println(a.length); 
          Scanner scan=new Scanner(System.in); 
          for(int i=0; i<a.length;i++) 
          { 
 System.out.println("Please enter the marks of Student " + i); 
           a[i]=scan.nextInt(); 
          } 
       System.out.println("the marks of students are as follows"); 
              for(int i=0;i<a.length;i++) 
              { 
               System.out.print(a[i] +" "); 
              } 
 } 
} 
2-D Array: A two-dimensional (2D) array is an array of arrays. It is a type of 
array that contains a set of elements arranged in rows and columns, and can be 
thought of as a grid of elements. In Java, a 2D array is implemented as an array 
of arrays.  
Memory Allocation Map Example: 
To declare a 2D array in Java, you can use the following syntax: 
type[][] arrayName; 
For example, the following code declares a 2D array of integers: 
int[][] myArray; 
You can also declare and create a 2D array in a single statement: 
int[][] myArray = new int[3][3];

import java.util.Scanner; 
public class Array_2D_Code_2  
{ 
  public static void main(String[] args)  
  { 
     Scanner s = new Scanner(System.in); 
     int ary[][] = new int[3][4]; 
     for(int i=0;i<ary.length;i++) 
     { 
       for(int j=0;j<ary[i].length;j++) 
  { 
  System.out.println("Enter the marks of class "+i+" Student "+j); 
  ary[i][j]=s.nextInt(); 
       } 
     } 
  System.out.println("The marks of the Students are"); 
  for(int i=0;i<ary.length;i++) 
  { 
   for(int j=0;j<ary[i].length;j++) 
   { 
    System.out.print(ary[i][j]+" "); 
   } 
   System.out.println(); 
       } 
   } 
}

import java.util.*; 
public class Array_2D_Code1  
{ 
    public static void main(String[] args)  
    { 
 Scanner s = new Scanner(System.in); 
 System.out.println("Enter the number Class"); 
 int nof_cls = s.nextInt(); 
 System.out.println("Enter the number of Students"); 
 int nof_studs = s.nextInt(); 
 int arr[][] = new int[nof_cls][nof_studs];  
 for(int i=0;i<arr.length;i++) 
 { 
   for(int j=0;j<arr[i].length;j++) 
   { 
     System.out.println("Enter marks of class "+i + " Student "+j); 
     arr[i][j]=s.nextInt(); 
   } 
 } 
 System.out.println("Enter the Marks of the Students"); 
 for(int i=0;i<arr.length;i++) 
 { 
    for(int j=0;j<arr[i].length;j++) 
    { 
       System.out.print(arr[i][j]+"  "); 
    } 
   System.out.println(); 
 } 
   } 
} 
Jagged Array: 
A jagged array is an array of arrays, and therefore its elements are reference types 
and are initialized to null. Each element of a jagged array can be an array of a 
different length. 
Here is an example of how to declare and initialize a jagged array: 
Memory Allocation Map Example: 
int[][] jaggedArray = new int[3][ ]; 
jaggedArray[0] = new int[5]; 
jaggedArray[1] = new int[3]; 
jaggedArray[2] = new int[2];

Code Example: 
package Jagged_Array; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
public class Jagged_Array_1  
{ 
   public static void main(String[] args)  
   { 
  Scanner s = new Scanner(System.in); 
  int ary[][] = new int[3][]; 
  ary[0]= new int[3]; 
  ary[1]= new int[2]; 
  ary[2]= new int[4]; 
  for(int i=0;i<ary.length;i++) 
  { 
    for(int j=0;j<ary[i].length;j++) 
    { 
      System.out.println("Enter the marks of class "+i+" Student "+j); 
      ary[i][j]=s.nextInt(); 
    } 
  } 
  System.out.println("The marks of the Students are"); 
  for(int i=0;i<ary.length;i++) 
  { 
   for(int j=0;j<ary[i].length;j++) 
   { 
    System.out.print(ary[i][j]+" "); 
   } 
   System.out.println(); 
       } 
   } 
} 
3D Array: A three-dimensional (3D) array is an array of arrays of arrays. It is a 
type of array that contains a set of elements arranged in a grid of rows and 
columns, with an additional layer of depth. In Java, a 3D array is implemented as 
an array of 2D arrays. 
To declare a 3D array in Java, you can use the following syntax: 
Memory Allocation Map: 
type[ ][ ][ ] arrayName; 
For example, the following code declares a 3D array of integers: 
int [ ][ ][ ] myArray; 
you can also declare and create a 3D array in a single statement: 
int[ ][ ][ ] myArray = new int[3][3][3]; 
Exp_Code_1: 
Wap to copy one array to another array: 
package Array_3D; 
import java.util.Scanner;      /// Example Code: 
public class Arr_3D_Code  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 { 
  Scanner S = new Scanner(System.in); 
  int arr[][][] = new int[3][2][3]; 
  for(int i=0;i<arr.length;i++) 
  { 
    for(int j=0;j<arr[i].length;j++) 
    { 
     for(int k=0;k<arr[i][j].length;k++) 
     { 
System.out.println("Enter marks of School "+ i +" class "+ j+" Student "+ k); 
     arr[i][j][k]= S.nextInt(); 
    } 
   } 
  } 
  for(int i=0;i<arr.length;i++) 
  { 
   for(int j=0;j<arr[i].length;j++) 
   { 
    for(int k=0;k<arr[i][j].length;k++) 
    { 
     System.out.print(arr[i][j][k]+" "); 
    } 
         System.out.println(); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
} 
public class Wap_arr  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) 
 { 
  int arr[] = {11,25,45,2,13,17}; 
  int brr[] = new int[arr.length]; 
  for(int i=0;i<arr.length;i++) 
  { 
   brr[i] = arr[i]; 
   System.out.print(brr[i]+" "); 
  } 
  System.out.println(); 
 } 
} 
Creating an array by Using Class: 
Exp Code_1: 
class ara 
{ 
 String name; 
 int R_num; 
 public String payru(String name1) 
 { 
  name = name1; 
  return name; 
 } 
 public int r_No(int Rno) 
 { 
  R_num = Rno; 
  return R_num; 
 } 
} 
public class Arra_code_2  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 { 
     ara ar[] = new ara[3]; 
     ar[0] = new ara(); 
     ar[1]= new ara(); 
     ar[2] = new ara(); 
     ar[0].payru("Teja"); 
    ar[1].payru("Nani"); 
    ar[2].payru("Sai"); 
     ar[0].r_No(301); 
    ar[1].r_No(302); 
    ar[2].r_No(303);  
     for( ara ae : ar) 
     { 
      System.out.println("The name of the Student is -
>"+ae.name+"<--and Roll number = "+ae.R_num); 
     } 
 } 
} 
For Each Loop: 
 It starts with the keyword for like a normal for-loop. 
 Instead of declaring and initializing a loop counter variable, you declare a 
variable that is the same type as the base type of the array, followed by a colon, 
which is then followed by the array name. 
 In the loop body, you can use the loop variable you created rather than using 
an indexed array element.  
 It’s commonly used to iterate over an array or a Collections class (eg, 
ArrayList) 
is equivalent to: 
Syntax: 
for (type var : array) 
{ 
} 
statements using var; 
for (int i=0; i<arr.length; i++) 
{ 
} 
type var = arr[i]; 
it fetch the data from starting 
index. we don’t have control to 
fetch from specific index  
 Example: 
For Each loop For 2D Array: 
public class For_each_2D_arr  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) 
 { 
  int arr[][]= {{1,6,7,8,9},{6,4,8,7,3}}; 
  for(int ae[]:arr) 
  { 
   for(int ar: ae) 
   { 
    System.out.print(ar+" "); 
   } 
   System.out.println(); 
  } 
 } 
}

13th Aug Live Class Strings in Java part 1 
String in Java: 
String refers to a collection of characters enclosed within double quotes( “ ”). 
String refers to an Object in java present in a package called java.lang.String. 
eg:: String s= "sachin"; 
System.out.println(s);//sachin 
String s =new String("sachin"); 
System.out.println(s);//sachin 
Two types of String: 
1- Immutable String (String class) 
2- Mutable String (StringBuilder, StringBuffer) 
● In java String object is by default immutable (String class if you store), meaning 
once 
“the object is created we cannot change the value of the object, if we try to 
change”. 
then those changes will be reflected on the new object not on the existing object. 
Ways to compare String ; 
equals(): Compare the content of String Object 
== : Compare references of String Objects. 
equalsIgnoreCase(): Compares values of String ignoring case sensitivity. 
compareTo(); compare value of string lexicographically 
● Memory in case of String will be allocated in Heap and within heap there is 
String 
Constant pool. If we are creating a String object without a new keyword things 
get 
resolved during compile time and Memory created in the String Constant pool. 
● Meaning : Direct literals are always placed in SCP,Because of runtime 
operation if 
object is required to create compulsorily that object should be placed on the 
Heap(Using new keyword or using any method like concate() ) ,but not on SCP. 
(Watch the class recording for understanding of same) 
Note:: 
● Before allocating memory in String Constant Pool(SCP) 1st jvm will check is 
any 
object is already created with required content or not. 
● If it is already available then it will reuse the existing object instead of creating 
the 
new Object. 
● If it is not available only then a new object will be created, so we say in SCP 
there is 
no chance of existing 2 objects with the same content. 
● In SCP duplicates are not permitted. 
● Garbage Collector cannot access SCP Area, Even though Object does not have 
any 
reference still object is not eligible for GC. 
● All SCP objects will be destroyed only at the time of JVM ShutDown. 
Note : 
● In our program if any String object is required to be used repeatedly then it is 
not 
recommended to create multiple objects with the same content it reduces 
performance of the system and affects memory utilisation. 
● We can create only one copy and we can reuse the same object for every 
requirement. This approach improves performance and memory utilisation we 
can achieve this by using "scp". (Adv of SCP) 
Summary: 
String: The String class in Java represents strings and provides methods for 
manipulating strings, such as concatenating, comparing, and finding the length of 
a string. Strings are immutable in Java, meaning that once a string is created, it 
cannot be changed. If you need to modify a string, you can create a new string 
with the desired modifications. Some examples of commonly used methods of 
the String class include length (), charAt(), substring(), concat(), and equals().

Different Ways to compare String Values: 
1.(==) Equals to Operator: Using the "==" operator: This compares the memory 
addresses of the two strings, not the actual content. It will return true if both 
variables point to the same string object in memory, otherwise, it will return false. 
String str1 = "hello"; 
String str2 = "hello"; 
System.out.println(str1 == str2); //true

} 
}

2. equals() method: Using the equals() method: This compares the actual content 
of the two strings. It will return true if both strings have the same characters in 
the same order, otherwise, it will return false. 
String str1 = "hello"; 
String str2 = "hello"; 
System.out.println(str1.equals(str2)); //true 
Exp_Code2: 
3. equalsIgnoreCase() method: Using the equalsIgnoreCase() method: This 
compares the actual content of the two strings, ignoring the case of the characters. 
It will return true if both strings have the same characters in the same order, 
ignoring case, otherwise, it will return false.

4.compareTo() method: This compares the two strings lexicographically, based 
on the Unicode value of each character in the strings. It returns 0 if the strings are 
equal, a positive integer if the first string is greater than the second string, and a 
negative integer if the first string is less than the second string. 
String str1 = "hello"; 
String str2 = "HELLO"; 
System.out.println(str1.compareTo(str2)); //32

Methods in String Class: 
1.concat () method: The concat() method in Java is used to concatenate two 
strings. It appends one string to the end of another and returns a new string that 
represents the concatenated result. 
String str1 = "Hello"; 
String str2 = " World"; 
String str3 = str1.concat(str2); 
System.out.println(str3); // "Hello World" 
You can also use the + operator to concatenate strings: 
String str1 = "Hello"; 
String str2 = " World"; 
String str3 = str1 + str2; 
System.out.println(str3); // "Hello World" 
Note: it's important to note that the “concat() method creates a new string 
object, it doesn't modify the original strings”, so it's a bit less efficient than 
using the + operator. 
It's also important to keep in mind that the concat() method doesn't add a space 
between the two strings, you need to add it manually or use the + operator to 
concatenate with a space. 
Memory map: 
String str1 = "Hello"; 
String constant pool 
String str1 = str1.concat(“World”); 
“Hello”; 
“HelloWorld”; 
String str2 = str1.concat(“Teja”); 
“HelloTeja”

2.toLowerCase(): This method returns a new string with all characters converted 
to lowercase. 
String str = "Hello World"; 
String lowerCase = str.toLowerCase(); 
System.out.println(lowerCase); // "hello world" 
3. toUpperCase(): This method returns a new string with all characters converted 
to uppercase. 
String str = "Hello World"; 
String upperCase = str.toUpperCase(); 
System.out.println(upperCase); // "HELLO WORLD" 
4. charAt(int index): This method returns the character at the specified index in 
the string. 
String str = "Hello"; 
char c = str.charAt(1); 
System.out.println(c); // 'e' 
5. substring(int beginIndex, int endIndex): This method returns a new string 
that is a substring of the original string, starting at the specified beginIndex and 
ending at the specified end Index. 
String str = "Hello World"; 
String subStr = str.substring(6, 11); 
System.out.println(subStr); // "World" 
6. length(): This method returns the number of characters in the string. 
String str = "Hello"; 
int length = str.length(); 
System.out.println(length); // 5 
7. indexOf(int ch): This method returns the index of the first occurrence of the 
specified character in the string. 
String str = "Hello World"; 
int index = str.indexOf('o'); 
System.out.println(index); // 4 
8. replace(char oldChar, char newChar): This method returns a new string in 
which all occurrences of the specified old character are replaced with the 
specified new character. 
String str = "Hello World"; 
String newStr = str.replace('o', 'a'); 
System.out.println(newStr); // "Halla Werala" 
9. trim(): This method returns a new string with leading and trailing whitespace 
removed. 
String str = " Hello World "; 
String trimStr = str.trim(); 
System.out.println(trimStr); // "Hello World"

14th Aug Live Class String part 2 (Mutable String ): 
Mutable String:  A mutable string is a string that can be changed after it's created. 
In Java, the String class is immutable, meaning its value cannot be changed after 
it's created. However, there are several ways to create a mutable string in Java. 
One way to create a mutable string is to use a StringBuilder or StringBuffer class, 
both of which are part of the Java Standard Library 
String Buffer:  The StringBuffer class is used to create mutable strings in a 
multithreaded environment. 
String Builder: The StringBuilder class is used to create mutable strings in a 
single-threaded environment. 
String (java. Lang): 
We classify String into 2 types 
a. Immutable 
b. Mutable(StringBuffer(1.0V),StringBuilder(1.5v)) 
Case1: 
String s=new String("sachin"); // 2 object (SCP and other one in heap Area) 
s.concat("tendulkar");// 1 object(SCP) 
System.out.println(s); 
Since String object are immutable, if we try to change the object, that change 
would not happen in the same memory 
the changes will happen in the new memory this concept we call it as 
"Immutable".

final keyword( access modifer): 
It is an access modifier which can be applied at 3 levels 
a. variable(primitive and reference) 
b. class level. 
c. method level. 
Final variable: 
If the variable is made as final then the value for those variables can't be changed, 
if we try to change it would result in "Compile Time Error”. Final variables would 
be resolved at the compile time only by the compiler. 
Eg_Code: 
public class FV_Code1  
{ 
public static void main(String[] args)  
{ 
final int a =20; 
int b=10; 
a++; // a= a+1; change for the variable:CE(compiletime error) 
b++; 
System.out.println(a); 
System.out.println(b); 
} 
} 
Out Put: 
Exception in thread "main" java.lang.Error: Unresolved compilation 
problem:  
The final local variable a cannot be assigned. It must be 
blank and not using a compound assignment 
at Final_Varible.FV_Code1.main(FV_Code1.java:9) 
final vs Immutablity : 
1. final is a keyword used in Java to indicate that the value of a variable, the 
implementation of a method, or the definition of a class cannot be changed once 
it is assigned or defined. For example, a final variable cannot be reassigned after 
its initial value is set. A final method cannot be overridden by a subclass. And a 
final class cannot be subclassed. 
2. Immutability, on the other hand, refers to the property of an object that cannot be 
modified after it is created. An immutable object is an object whose state cannot 
be changed after it is constructed. For example, a String object in Java is 
immutable because its value cannot be changed once it is created. 
3. While the final keyword can be used to achieve immutability, it is not the only 
way to achieve it. For example, an object can be made immutable by making all 
its fields private and final, and not exposing any setter methods to modify them. 
The final keyword is often used in combination with other techniques to ensure 
immutability.

Note_1: 
1. If the variable is of primitive type and if it is final then the value of the variable 
should not be changed,if we try to change it would result in "CompileTimeError". 
2. If the variable if of reference type and if it is of mutable nature then as per its 
mutable nature the object data can be changed,it would not result in 
"CompileTimeError". 
3. But if we try to reassign the reference variable with a new object address then it 
would result in "CompileTimeError". 
Note_2: 
1. final variable(valid concept) 
2. final object(not valid) 
3. immutable variable(not valid) 
4. immutable object(valid) 
primitive  
int,float,byte,short,long,double,....  
reference 
String,StringBuffer,StringBuilder,Object,....... 
String Buffer 
It is avaialble in java.lang package. 
Methods of StringBuffer 
capacity() => the default capacity of StringBuffer is 16 
if the capacity is filled internally jvm will  increase the size using the following 
formulae 
newCapacity= (currentcapcity + 1) * 2 
EG: 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer(); 
System.out.println(sb.capacity());//16 
sb.append("abcdefghijklmnop"); 
System.out.println(sb.capacity());//16 
sb.append("q"); 
System.out.println(sb.capacity()); // (16+1) * 2 
sb.append("rstuvwxyz"); 
System.out.println(sb.capacity());// 34 
EG_2: 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer(19);  //here the integer no specifies the 
capacity of StringBuffer  
System.out.println(sb.capacity()); 
EG_3: 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer("sachin"); //here the capacity will be 
(length of String + 16) 
System.out.println(sb.capacity()); 
System.out.println(sb.length()); 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer(); 
System.out.println(sb.capacity());//16 
sb.append("The value of PIE IS :: "); 
sb.append(3.1414); 
sb.append(", This is exactly ::"); 
sb.append(true); 
System.out.println(sb); 
System.out.println(sb.capacity());//70 
System.out.println(sb.length());//54 
insert(int,String)

index 
insert(int,long) 
eg: 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer("abcdefgh");

System.out.println(sb); // abxyzcdefgh9 
delete(int,int) 
deleteCharAt(int) 
eg: 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer("sachinrameshtendulkar");

the String 
eg:

ensureCapacity(int) => it is used to increase the 
capacity to the specific limit 
eg: 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer(); 
System.out.println(sb.capacity());//16 
sb.ensureCapacity(10000); 
System.out.println(sb.capacity());//10000 
METHODS IN THE STRINGBUFFER CLASS IN JAVA: 
1.append(): Adds one or more characters to the end of the string buffer. 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer("Hello"); 
sb.append(" World"); 
System.out.println(sb.toString()); // "Hello World" 
2. insert(): Inserts one or more characters into the string buffer at a specified 
index. 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer("Hello World"); 
sb.insert(5, ", "); 
System.out.println(sb.toString()); // "Hello, World" 
3. delete(): Deletes one or more characters from the string buffer. 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer("Hello World"); 
sb.delete(5, 7); 
System.out.println(sb.toString()); // "Helloorld" 
4. replace(): Replaces one or more characters in the string buffer with new 
characters. 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer("Hello World"); 
sb.replace(5, 7, ", "); 
System.out.println(sb.toString()); // "Hello, World" 
5.reverse(): Reverses the order of the characters in the string buffer. 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer("Hello World"); 
sb.reverse(); 
System.out.println(sb.toString()); // "dlroW olleH" 
6.capacity(): Returns the current capacity of the string buffer. 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer(); 
System.out.println(sb.capacity()); // 16 
7.length(): Returns the length of the string buffer. 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer("Hello World"); 
System.out.println(sb.length()); // 11 
8.toString(): Returns the contents of the string buffer as a string. 
StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer("Hello World"); 
String str = sb.toString(); // Converts String buffer to 
String. 
System.out.println(str); // "Hello World"

All the methods present are synchronized 
At a time on StringBuffer object only one 
thread can operate. 
Since only one thread operate it is 
"ThreadSafety". 
Performance is low.

All the methods present are not 
synchronized 
At a time on StringBuilder object many threads

Performance is high. 
public class Wap_String  
{ 
    public static String Wap(String str) 
    { 
     String str2 = " "; 
     for(int i=0;i<str.length();i++) 
     { 
      str2 = str2+str.charAt(i); 
     } 
     System.out.println(str2); 
     return str2; 
    } 
    public static void main(String[] args)  
    { 
  System.out.print(" Enter the String ----> "); 
  Wap("Sai Teja"); 
 } 
} 
public class Wap_String  
{ 
    public static String Wap(String str) 
    { 
     String str2 = " "; 
     for(int i=0;i<str.length();i++) 
     { 
      str2 = str2+(char)(str.charAt(i)+32); 
     } 
     System.out.println(str2); 
     return str2; 
    } 
    public static void main(String[] args)  
    { 
  System.out.print(" Enter the String ----> "); 
  Wap("SAITEJA"); 
 }

20th Aug Live Class Encapsulation and Constructor in Java: 
In Java, "Oops" typically refers to object-oriented programming (OOP) concepts 
and principles. Object-oriented programming is a programming paradigm that 
organizes code into objects, which are instances of classes that encapsulate data 
and behavior. 
Here are some important concepts in OOP in Java: 
1. Classes and Objects: A class is a blueprint or template that defines the 
properties and methods of objects. An object is an instance of a class. 
2. Inheritance: Inheritance allows classes to inherit properties and methods from 
other classes. It enables code reuse and the creation of a hierarchical class 
structure. 
3. Polymorphism: Polymorphism allows objects of different classes to be treated 
as objects of a common superclass. It allows methods to be overridden in 
subclasses to provide different implementations. 
4. Encapsulation: Encapsulation is the practice of hiding internal 
implementation details of a class and exposing a public interface for interacting 
with the class. It helps in achieving data abstraction and information hiding. 
5. Abstraction: Abstraction focuses on the essential characteristics of an object 
and hides the irrelevant details. It allows creating abstract classes and interfaces 
to define common behaviors and contracts. 
6. Modularity: Modularity refers to dividing a program into separate modules or 
components, each responsible for a specific functionality. Java uses packages 
to achieve modularity. 
7. Polymorphism: Polymorphism allows objects of different classes to be treated 
as objects of a common superclass. It allows methods to be overridden in 
subclasses to provide different implementations. 
1.Encapsulation: is one of the fundamental principles of object-oriented 
programming (OOP) and is supported in Java. It refers to the bundling of data 
and methods within a class, where the data is kept private and can only be 
accessed through public methods known as getters and setters. Encapsulation 
ensures that the internal state of an object is protected from direct access and 
manipulation by other code. 
In Java, encapsulation is achieved through the use of access modifiers. There are 
three access modifiers in Java: 
1. Public: The public access modifier allows unrestricted access to the class, its 
fields, and its methods from any other class. 
2. Private: The private access modifier restricts access to only within the same 
class. Private fields and methods can only be accessed and modified from 
within the class itself. 
3. Protected: The protected access modifier allows access to the class, its fields, 
and its methods within the same package and also in subclasses, even if they 
are in different packages. 
Example 1: 
package Encapusulation;

{ 
 private int PgNo;

 {

     {

 }

This Keyword: To refer to instance variables or methods: When there is a need 
to refer to an instance variable or method of the current object, the "this" keyword 
is used. It distinguishes between the local variable and the instance variable if 
they have the same name. 
Exp: 
Example 2:

    private int num; 
    public void setNum(int num) { 
        this.num = num; // "this.num" refers to the instance variable, while "num" refers 
to the method parameter 
    } 
}

Constructors:  
A Specialized Setter whose name is as that of class name. Constructor can be 
Invoked during object creation. 
In Java, a constructor is a special method that is used to initialize objects of a 
class. It has the same name as the class and does not have a return type, not even 
void. Constructors are called automatically when an object is created using the 
"new" keyword. 
Constructors have the following characteristics: 
Initialization: The primary purpose of a constructor is to initialize the newly 
created object. It sets the initial values of the object's instance variables or 
performs any other necessary setup. 
Same name as class: Constructors have the same name as the class they belong 
to. This allows Java to identify the constructor that should be called when creating 
an object. 
No return type: Constructors do not have a return type specified. This is different 
from regular methods, which specify a return type or use "void" if they don't 
return a value. 
Optional parameters: Constructors can have parameters that specify the initial 
values for the object's instance variables. These parameters allow for different 
ways to construct objects with different initial states. 
Default constructor: If a class does not explicitly define any constructors, Java 
provides a default constructor automatically. The default constructor takes no 
arguments and performs default initialization for instance variables (e.g., setting 
numeric variables to 0, references to null, etc.). 
Exp: 
class MyClass { 
private int num;      
 // Constructor with a parameter 
public MyClass(int value)  
{ 
num = value; // Initializes the instance variable 
} 
// Default constructor (provided by Java if no constructors are defined explicitly) 
public MyClass() { 
// Performs default initialization 
} 
} 
In the example, the first constructor MyClass(int value) takes an integer 
parameter and initializes the num instance variable with the provided value. The 
second constructor MyClass() is a default constructor that takes no parameters 
and performs default initialization. 
Constructors play a vital role in object initialization and can be used to ensure 
that objects are properly set up before they are used in the program. 
Example2: 
package Constructor;

Constructor Overloading: 
Constructor overloading is a concept in Java that allows a class to have multiple constructors with different 
parameter lists. Each constructor can provide a different way to initialize objects of the class, accommodating 
various scenarios or user requirements. 
By using constructor overloading, you can create objects with different sets of initial values without needing to 
invoke separate initialization methods. The appropriate constructor is automatically invoked based on the 
arguments provided when creating an object. 
Exp1: 
package Polymorphism_Method_OverLoading; 
class Laptop 
{ 
 private String brand; 
 private String processor; 
 private int cost; 
 private String storage; 
 public Laptop(String brand,int cost) 
 { 
  this.brand = brand; 
  this.cost = cost; 
 } 
 public Laptop(String processor, String storage) 
 { 
  this.processor = processor; 
  this.storage = storage; 
 } 
 public String getBrand()  
 { 
  return brand; 
 } 
 public String getProcessor()  
 { 
  return processor; 
 } 
 public int getCost()  
 { 
  return cost; 
 } 
 public String getStorage()  
 { 
  return storage; 
 } 
} 
public class ConsOverLoad  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 { 
  Laptop ls = new Laptop("HP", 60000); 
  Laptop lse = new Laptop("i5 12th Gen", "512 SSD"); 
  System.out.println("LapTop Specification are ---> "); 
  System.out.println(ls.getBrand()+" "+ls.getCost()); 
  System.out.println(lse.getProcessor()+" "+lse.getStorage()); 
 }

this() Method in Constructors: The syntax this() in a constructor is used to 
invoke another constructor within the same class. It is a form of constructor 
chaining, where one constructor calls another constructor to perform initialization 
tasks. This allows code reuse and helps in avoiding duplication of initialization 
logic. 
When this() is used in a constructor, it must be the first line of code in that 
constructor. It can only be used once within a constructor, and it cannot be used 
together with super() (which is used to invoke a constructor from the superclass).

package Constructor; 
class Car 
{ 
 private String brand; 
 private int cost; 
 public Car() 
 { 
  this("BMW",1000000); 
  System.out.println(brand+" "+cost); 
 } 
 public Car(String brand,int cost) 
 { 
  this.brand=brand;

  this(); 
  this.cost=cost;

  return brand;

  return cost; 
 }

Static Key word: 
It is mainly consisting of 5 types. 
1. Static variables 
2. Static methods 
3. Static initialization blocks 
4. Static nested classes: 
5. Static import 
1.Static variables: Static variables we can access in static methods, static block, 
non-static block and non-static methods.They are also called as class variables. 
When a variable is declared as static, it is associated with the class rather than 
with specific instances of the class. All instances of the class share the same copy 
of the static variable. Static variables are accessed using the class name, not 
through an instance of the class. 
class MyClass { 
} 
static int myStaticVariable = 10; 
Memory is allocated in the heap 
area for Static variables only once 
at the time of Class loading. 
Static methods: Similar to static variables, static methods belong to the class 
rather than to instances of the class. They can be called directly on the class itself, 
without the need to create an object. 
class MyClass { 
static void myStaticMethod() 
{ 
} 
// Code here 
} 
Static initialization blocks: These blocks are used to initialize static variables or 
perform any other static initialization tasks. They are executed once when the 
class is loaded into memory. 
class MyClass { 
static { 
// Static initialization code here 
} 
} 
Static nested classes: Nested classes declared as static are associated with the 
outer class itself, not with instances of the outer class. They can be accessed 
without an instance of the outer class. 
class MyClass { 
static { 
// Static initialization code here 
} 
} 
Static import: The static import statement allows you to access static members 
of a class directly without specifying the class name. 
import static java.lang.Math.PI; 
It's important to note that using static should be done with caution, as it can affect 
the object-oriented nature of Java and lead to potential issues such as shared state 
between instances and reduced flexibility. 
Exp: 
Execution will start from first “Static variables --- Static Block --- Static 
Methods” 
public class Static_varible1 
{ 
    // Static variables 
 static int a,b,c; 
 // Static Block 
 static  
 { 
  System.out.println("This is Static Block"); 
  a =2; 
  b=6; 
  c=9; 
 } 
 static void STM() 
 { 
  System.out.println(a); 
  System.out.println(b); 
  System.out.println(c); 
 } 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 { 
  System.out.println("This is main method"); 
  STM(); 
 } 
}

package Static_Varible; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
class Farmer { 
 private float pa; 
 private float td; 
 private float si; 
 private static float ri; // class variables 
 static { 
  ri = 2.5f; 
 } 
 public void acceptInput() { 
  Scanner scan = new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.println("Dear, Kindly enter loan amount needed"); 
  pa = scan.nextFloat(); 
  System.out.println("Dear, Kindly enter time needed to repay"); 
  td = scan.nextFloat(); 
 } 
 public void compute() { 
  si = (pa * td * ri) / 100; 
 } 
 public void disp() { 
  System.out.println("Simple interest is " + si); 
  float ta = pa+si; 
  System.out.println("The Total Amount To Pay  : "+ ta); 
 } 
} 
public class Static_Code3 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Farmer f1 = new Farmer(); 
  Farmer f2 = new Farmer(); 
  f1.acceptInput(); 
  f1.compute(); 
  f1.disp(); 
 System.out.println("--------------------------------------------------"); 
  f2.acceptInput(); 
  f2.compute(); 
  f2.disp(); 
 } 
}

27th Aug Live Class Inheritance: 
Inheritance : 
It is one of the pillars of Object Orientation. 
It always speaks about reusability. 
In java inheritance is achieved through the "extends" keyword. 
Inheritance is the process of one class acquiring properties(Fields) and 
behaviour(methods) 
of another class. 
It is also referred to as a writing project as a hierarchy of classes rather than a single class. 
Important points to be noted: 
● Private members of a class do not participate in Inheritance. 
● Constructor will not get inherited but it will get executed because of super() call 
present in child class Constructor. 
● Single Inheritance is allowed ( One class extending another class) 
● Multilevel Inheritance is Allowed 
● Multiple Inheritance is not permitted. It will lead to ambiguity to compiler also to the 
Diamond shape problem. 
● Cyclic Inheritance is not permitted. 
● Hierarchical Inheritance is allowed. (One class can have multiple child classes). 
Parent class== Existing class== Base class== Super class 
Child class== Derived class== Subclass 
This relationship also known as is - A relationship. 
Inherited Methods vs Overridden methods vs Specialized method 
Inherited Method : Such method which is inherited from parent class to child class 
and used as it is in child class without any modification. 
Overridden method : Such method which is inherited from parent class to child class 
and modified in child class to meet child class requirement. 
Specialized method : Such method which is present only in child class but not in 
parent class. 
Super Keyword: 
Code Exp:   
Super keyword: The super keyword is used to refer to the immediate parent class, i.e., the 
superclass, from within the context of a subclass. It is particularly useful when you want to 
access or call the members (fields, methods, or constructors) of the superclass that have been 
overridden or hidden in the subclass. 
The super keyword can be used in the following scenarios: 
Accessing superclass members: If a subclass defines a member (field or method) with the same 
name as the superclass, using super allows you to refer to the superclass's version of that 
member. 
Invoking the superclass constructor: When a subclass is constructed, the superclass's 
constructor is automatically called. By using super, you can explicitly invoke a specific 
constructor of the superclass. 
class Animal { 
    String name; 
    public Animal(String name) { 
        this.name = name; 
    } 
    public void makeSound() { 
        System.out.println("Generic animal sound"); 
    } 
} 
class Dog extends Animal { 
    public Dog(String name) { 
        super(name); // Calls the constructor of the superclass (Animal) 
    } 
   @Override 
    public void makeSound() { 
        super.makeSound(); // Calls the makeSound() method of the superclass 
(Animal) 
        System.out.println("Bark!"); 
    } 
    public void fetch() { 
        System.out.println("Fetching the ball"); 
    } 
} 
public class Super_animal_Class { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Dog dog = new Dog("Buddy"); 
        System.out.println("Name: " + dog.name); 
        dog.makeSound(); // Outputs: "Generic animal sound" followed by 
"Bark!" 
        dog.fetch(); // Outputs: "Fetching the ball" 
    } 
} 
Single Level Inheritance: 
Single-level inheritance is a type of inheritance in object-oriented programming 
where a class inherits from only one superclass (parent class). In other words, 
there is a one-to-one relationship between a subclass and its superclass. This 
means that a class can have only one immediate parent class, which it extends to 
inherit its properties and behaviours. 
Exp: 
In a single-level inheritance hierarchy, the subclass can access all the public and 
protected members (fields and methods) of its superclass. It can also override or 
extend those members if needed. However, there is no chaining of inheritance 
beyond the immediate superclass. That is, there is no grandparent class or 
multiple levels of inheritance involved. 
Multilevel heritance:  
Multilevel inheritance is a type of inheritance in object-oriented programming 
where a class inherits from another class, which in turn inherits from another 
class, forming a chain of inheritance. In other words, there is a multi-level 
relationship between classes, where each subclass inherits from its immediate 
superclass, which is also a subclass of another superclass. 
package Inheritance; 
//Superclass 
class Animals { 
 void eat() { 
     System.out.println("Animal is eating"); 
 } 
} 
//Subclass inheriting from Animal 
class Dogs extends Animals { 
 void bark() { 
     System.out.println("Dog is barking"); 
 } 
} 
//Subclass inheriting from Dog 
class Labrador extends Dogs { 
 void playFetch() {

     Labrador labrador = new Labrador();

     labrador.bark();      // Outputs: "Dog is barking" 
     labrador.playFetch(); // Outputs: "Labrador is playing 
fetch" 
 } 
}

Inherited Methods: Inherited Methods are such methods, which are inherited 
from parent class to child class we are using as it is without doing any 
modification of the method. 
Overridden Methods: Overridden methods such methods, as per our need we 
can modify those methods are called overridden methods. 
Specialization Methods: Specialization Methods such methods, we are available 
in the child class and not available in the parent class. Those methods are called 
as specialization methods. 
Example: 
Plane: 
+Fly(): Void 
+Take Off(): Void 
Cargo plane: 
+Fly(): Void 
         + Carry 
Goods():Void 
Passenger plane: 
+Fly(): Void 
          + Carry 
Passengers():Void 
Code Exp:  
package Inheritance; 
class Plane 
{ 
 public void fly() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Plane is flying"); 
 } 
 public void takeOff() /// Inherited Method 
 { 
  System.out.println("Plane is taking off"); 
 } 
} 
class CargoPlane extends Plane 
{ 
 public void fly() // Overridden Method 
 { 
  System.out.println("Cargo plane flies at lower height"); 
 } 
 public void carryGoods() // Speclization method 
 { 
  System.out.println("Cargo plane carry goods"); 
 } 
} 
class PassengerPlane extends Plane 
{ 
 public void fly() // Overridden Method 
 { 
  System.out.println("passenger plane flies at medium height"); 
 } 
 public void carryPassenger() // Speclization method 
 { 
  System.out.println("Passenger plane carry passenger"); 
 } 
} 
public class Plane_inheritance { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
       Plane cp=new CargoPlane(); /// So We can Create Object for child class by 
Using  
       cp.fly();  //           Parent Class  
       cp.takeOff(); 
       //cp.carryGoods(); 
       ((CargoPlane) cp).carryGoods(); // For Spelization Methods we need to Access 
By 
                                    // Using Down Casting   
       Plane pp=new PassengerPlane(); 
       pp.fly(); 
       pp.takeOff(); 
       ((PassengerPlane) pp).carryPassenger(); 
 } 
} 
Out put: 
Cargo plane flies at lower height 
Plane is taking off 
Cargo plane carry goods 
passenger plane flies at medium 
height 
Plane is taking off 
Upcasting in Java refers to the process of casting a reference of a subclass to a 
reference of its superclass. This type of casting is always allowed in Java and is 
considered safe, as a subclass object inherently contains all the attributes and 
behaviors of its superclass. 
Exp: 
Downcasting in Java refers to the process of casting a reference of a superclass 
to a reference of its subclass. Unlike upcasting, downcasting can potentially result 
in runtime errors if not done correctly, because the subclass may contain 
additional methods or attributes that the superclass does not have. Therefore, 
before attempting to downcast, it's important to ensure that the object being 
referenced is actually an instance of the subclass. 
Exp: 
28th Aug Live Class Polymorphism and has A relationship in Java: 
Method Over Loading (Compile Time Polymorphism): Method Over Loading 
(Compile Time Polymorphism) is defined as the use of the same method name 
with different parameters values. 
Exp 1: 
class Calculation 
{ 
 // Adding two Numbers 
 public int add(int num1,int num2) 
 { 
  int result = num1+num2; 
  return result; 
 } 
 //Adding three Numbers and doing average 
 public int add(int a,int b,int c) 
 { 
  int result = (a+b+c/3); 
  return result; 
 } 
    public void add() 
 { 
  int n; 
  int i =0;int j=0;n=9; 
  while(i<n) 
  { 
    for(j=0;j<n;j++) 
   { 
    if(i==0||j==0||i==(n-1)||j==(n-1)||i==j||i+j==(n-1)) 
    { 
     System.out.print("*"); 
    } 
    else 
    { 
     System.out.print(" "); 
    } 
    } 
   i++; 
   System.out.println(); 
  } 
 } 
    public String add(String str1,String str2) 
    { 
     String c = str1.concat(str2); 
     return c; 
    } 
} 
public class Code_M_O_1  
{ 
  public static void main(String[] args)  
  { 
 Calculation cal = new Calculation(); 
 cal.add(); 
 int A1 = cal.add(31, 19); 
 int Avg = cal.add(10, 20, 30); 
 String Res = cal.add("Sai "," Teja"); 
 System.out.println(A1); 
 System.out.println(Avg); 
 System.out.println(Res); 
  } 
}  
Constructor Overloading: 
Constructor overloading is a concept in Java that allows a class to have multiple constructors with 
different parameter lists. Each constructor can provide a different way to initialize objects of the class, 
accommodating various scenarios or user requirements. 
By using constructor overloading, you can create objects with different sets of initial values without 
needing to invoke separate initialization methods. The appropriate constructor is automatically invoked 
based on the arguments provided when creating an object. 
Exp1: 
package Polymorphism_Method_OverLoading; 
class Laptop 
{ 
 private String brand; 
 private String processor; 
 private int cost; 
 private String storage; 
 public Laptop(String brand,int cost) 
 { 
  this.brand = brand; 
  this.cost = cost; 
 } 
 public Laptop(String processor, String storage) 
 { 
  this.processor = processor; 
  this.storage = storage; 
 } 
 public String getBrand()  
 { 
  return brand; 
 } 
 public String getProcessor()  
 { 
  return processor; 
 } 
 public int getCost()  
 { 
  return cost; 
 } 
 public String getStorage()  
 { 
  return storage; 
 } 
} 
public class ConsOverLoad  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 { 
  Laptop ls = new Laptop("HP", 60000); 
  Laptop lse = new Laptop("i5 12th Gen", "512 SSD"); 
  System.out.println("LapTop Specification are ---> "); 
  System.out.println(ls.getBrand()+" "+ls.getCost()); 
  System.out.println(lse.getProcessor()+" "+lse.getStorage()); 
 }  
} 
Output:

Asus 59999 
AMD Ryszen 5600H 512Gb SSd , 
1Tb HDD 
LapTop Specification are --->  
HP 60000 
i5 12th Gen 512 SSD 
Method Overriding: 
Method overriding is a fundamental concept in object-oriented programming that 
allows a subclass to provide a specific implementation for a method that is already 
defined in its superclass. The method in the subclass has the same name, return 
type, and parameters as the method (Having the Same Parameters and same 
method name) in the superclass. Method overriding is a key component of 
achieving run-time polymorphism in Java. 
Exp1: 
package Method_Overriding; 
class Animal { 
void makeSound() { 
System.out.println("Animal makes a sound"); 
} 
} 
class Dog extends Animal { 
@Override 
void makeSound() { 
System.out.println("Dog barks"); 
} 
} 
public class Method_override1 { 
public static void main(String[] args)  
{ 
Animal myAnimal = new Dog();   
//Parent class     Child Class 
myAnimal.makeSound(); // Outputs: "Dog barks" 
} 
} 
Output: 
Dog barks

package Method_Overriding; 
class plane 
{ 
 public void fly() 
 { 
  System.out.println("plane is going fly with in a short span"); 
 } 
 public void takeoff() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Plane is going to Take off"); 
 } 
} 
class Cargo_Plane extends plane 
{ 
 public void fly()   //overriding the Method 
 { 
  System.out.println("Cargo planes are fly at short height"); 
 } 
 public void takeoff()    //overriding the Method 
 { 
  System.out.println("Cargo planes need Large Run Way to take off"); 
 } 
} 
class Fighter_Plane extends plane 
{ 
 public void fly() //overriding the Method 
 { 
  System.out.println("Fighter planes are fly at High height"); 
 } 
 public void takeoff() //overriding the Method 
 { 
  System.out.println("Fighter planes need Small Run Way to take off"); 
 } 
} 
class Passenger_plan extends plane 
{ 
 public void fly() //overriding the Method 
 { 
  System.out.println("passenger planes are fly at Medium height"); 
 } 
 public void takeoff() //overriding the Method 
 { 
  System.out.println("Cargo planes need Large/Medium Run Way to take off"); 
 } 
} 
class AirPort{ 
 public void permession(plane p) 
 { 
  p.fly(); 
  p.takeoff(); 
 } 
} 
public class Plan_Override  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
    plane cp = new Cargo_Plane();  
    plane fp = new Fighter_Plane(); 
    plane pp = new Passenger_plan(); 
    AirPort ar = new AirPort(); 
    //ar.permession(cp);ar.permession(fp);ar.permession(pp); 
    //By individual 
    plane[]pls = new plane[] {cp,fp,pp}; 
    for(plane p : pls) 
    {           
     ar.permession(p);   //By Foreachloop 
     System.out.println(); 
    } 
 } 
} 
HAS – A – Relation in JAVA: 
In Java, the has-a relationship is often referred to as composition, where one class 
contains an instance of another class as a member variable. This allows you to 
create more complex objects by combining simpler ones. Composition is one of 
the fundamental principles of object-oriented programming. 
Exp Code-1:   
package HAS_A_RELATIONSHIP; 
class Author { 
    private String name; 
    private Book book; 
    public Author(String name, Book book) { 
        this.name = name; 
        this.book = book; 
    } 
 // * @return the name 
 public String getName() { 
  return name; 
 } 
 // * @return the book 
 public Book getBook() { 
  return book; 
 } 
    // Other methods and getters/setters 
} 
class Book { 
    private String title; 
    public Book(String title) { 
        this.title = title; 
    } 
 // * @return the title 
 public String getTitle() { 
  return title; 
 } 
 // * @param title the title to set 
 public void setTitle(String title) { 
  this.title = title; 
 } 
    // Other methods and getters/setters 
} 
public class CODE_2 { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Book book = new Book("The Great Gatsby"); 
        Author author = new Author("F. Scott Fitzgerald", book); 
        System.out.println(author.getName() + " wrote the book: " + 
author.getBook().getTitle()); 
    } 
} 
Out put: 
F. Scott Fitzgerald wrote 
the book: The Great Gatsby 
Relationship in java 
==================== 
As a part of application development, we have to use few entities(class) as per 
our application requirement. 
By promoting relationship we can achieve 
a. Optimisation over our code(less lines of code) 
b. Code Reusability 
c. Execution time 
d. share ability. 
How many types of relationship exists in Java? 
we have 2 types of relationship 
a. IS-A(achieved through extends keyword) 
b. HAS-A 
What is the difference b/w IS-A relationship and HAS-A relationship? 
IS-A relationship 
=> It is able to define inheritance b/w 2 entity classes 
=> It also promotes code reusability in java application. 
HAS-A relationship 
=> It will define associations b/w 2 entities in java application. 
=> Through association b/w entities it will improve communication b/w 2 entities 
and data 
navigation b/w 2 entities. 
Associations in Java 
=================== 
In Java we have 4 types of association 
a. 1 to 1 association 
b. 1 to many association 
c. Many to One association 
d. Many to Many association. 
To achieve association b/w 2 entities we have to declare either single reference or array of 
reference variable of an entity in another entity class. 
eg: 
class Address{ 
Integer pinNo; 
Integer doorNo; 
String state; 
String city; 
String country; 
} 
class Student{ 
String name; 
Integer age; 
Integer sid; 
//HAS-A variable 
Address address;//1 to 1 Association 
//HAS-A variable 
Address[] address;//1 to Many Association 
} 
Key points of Associations 
=========================== 
Dependency Injection 
a. The process of Injecting the dependent object into target object is called 
"Dependency Injection". 
Target Object => The object which is been given to the developers for usage is called 
"Target Object". 
Dependent Object => The object which is an helper object for the target object is called 
"Dependant Object". 
eg#1 
class Address{}//Dependant Object 
class Student{}//Target Object 
How to perform Dependency Injection in Java? 
It can be done in 2 ways 
a. Constructor Injection. 
a. We can inject primitive value to object. 
b. We can inject one more object into another object. 
b. Setter Injection. 
a. We can inject primitive value to object. 
b. We can inject one more object into another object. 
Over –View: 
One-One Association 
=================== 
It is a relationship b/w 2 entities, where one entity of one class is mapped to one more entity 
of another class. 
eg: 
Employee(target object) 
| 
|HAS-A 
| 
Account(dependent object) 
refer: ONE_ONE_EXample.png 
refer: One-One-Association(Constructor Injection) 
One-One-Association(Setter Injection) 
When to use Constructor Injection and when to use Setter Injection? 
Ans. It totally depends on the project requirement 
Constructor => If the dependant object is ready at the time of target object creation 
then perform "Constructor injection". 
Setter => If the dependant object is not ready at the time of target object creation 
then perform "Setter injection". 
Employee Account HAS A 
Int employeID; 
String employeName; 
String employeeAddress; 
Account account;

String accountName; 
String accountType; 
String accountNomine;

CONSTRUCTORS 
For Has – A- Relation first we need to create a Dependent Object for usage were 
required to point the Target Object, For that I am taking the Example for 
Employee and account. Here I am taking the Account as Dependent Object and 
Employee is Target Object. 
Creating The Dependent Object – Account. 
 Creating the Target Object for Employee by Injecting the Dependent Object 
Account. 
package Account_and_Employee_Has_A_Relationship; 
public class Account  
{ 
    private int accountNumber; 
    private String account_type; 
    private String account_holder_name; 
    private String account_Nomine; 
    // Creating the Constructor for Account 
    public Account(int accountNumber,String account_type,String 
account_holder_name,String account_Nomine) 
    { 
     this.accountNumber=accountNumber; 
     this.account_type=account_type; 
     this.account_holder_name = account_holder_name; 
     this.account_Nomine = account_Nomine; 
    } 
    // Generating the Getters to Get the Value. 
 public int getAccountNumber() { 
  return accountNumber; 
 } 
 public String getAccount_type() { 
  return account_type; 
 } 
 public String getAccount_holder_name() { 
  return account_holder_name; 
 } 
 public String getAccount_Nomine() { 
  return account_Nomine; 
 } 
} 
package Account_and_Employee_Has_A_Relationship; 
public class Employee  
{ 
    private int employeeId; 
    private String employeeName; 
    private String employeAddress; 
    //HAS a Varible Injection 
    private Account account; 
 /** 
  * @param employeeId 
  * @param employeeName 
  * @param accountNUMBER      // Creating the Constructor 
  * @param employeAddress 
  * @param account 
  */ 
 public Employee(int employeeId, String employeeName, String 
employeAddress, Account account) { 
  super(); 
  this.employeeId = employeeId; 
  this.employeeName = employeeName; 
  this.employeAddress = employeAddress; 
  this.account = account; 
 } 
    public Employee display(Employee details) 
    { 
     System.out.println("*******Display the Details of the Employee******"); 
     System.out.println(); 
     System.out.println("Employee id :: "+employeeId); 
     System.out.println("Employee Name :: "+employeeName); 
     System.out.println("Empoyee Adress :: "+employeAddress); 
     System.out.println(); 
     System.out.println("*******Account Details**********"); 
     System.out.println(); 
     if(account.getAccount_holder_name().equalsIgnoreCase(employeeName)) 
     { 
      System.out.println("Account number :: 
"+account.getAccountNumber()); 
         System.out.println("Account Type :: "+account.getAccount_type()); 
         System.out.println("Account Holder Name:: 
"+account.getAccount_holder_name()); 
         System.out.println("Account Nomine :: 
"+account.getAccount_Nomine()); 
     } 
     else { 
      System.out.println("Employee Name and Account holder Name is Miss 
matching ---> Update your Name"); 
      System.out.println("Account Holder Name:: 
"+account.getAccount_holder_name()); 
   } 
     return details; 
    } 
}

One to Many Assocation 
====================== 
It is a relationship b/w 2 entities, where one entity of one class is mapped to multiple 
entities of another class. 
eg: 
Department(1) //Target Object 
| 
|HAS-A 
| 
Employee(Many)//Dependent Object

package One_TO_Many_Association; 
public class Players  
{ 
 private int playerID; 
 private String playerName; 
 private String Board; 
 private String playerAddress; 
 public Players(int playerID,String playerName,String Board,String 
playerAddress) 
 { 
  this.playerID = playerID; 
  this.playerName = playerName; 
  this.Board = Board; 
  this.playerAddress = playerAddress; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @return the playerID 
  */ 
 public int getPlayerID() { 
  return playerID; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @return the playerName 
  */ 
 public String getPlayerName() { 
  return playerName; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @return the board 
  */ 
 public String getBoard() { 
  return Board; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @return the playerAddress 
  */ 
 public String getPlayerAddress() { 
  return playerAddress; 
 } 
} 
Package One_TO_Many_Association; 
public class Franchise_Board  
{ 
 private String franchiseCode; 
 private String franchiseName; 
 private String frachiseLocation; 
 // Has A Variable, 
 Players[] players; 
 /** 
  * @param franchiseID 
  * @param franchiseName 
  * @param frachiseLocation 
  * @param players 
  */   
 //Performing the Constructor Injection. 
 public Franchise_Board(String franchiseCode, String franchiseName, String 
frachiseLocation, Players[] players) { 
  this.franchiseCode = franchiseCode; 
  this.franchiseName = franchiseName; 
  this.frachiseLocation = frachiseLocation; 
  // Has A variable injecting through Constructor. 
  this.players = players; 
 } 
@return the franchiseID 
 public String getFranchiseCode() { 
  return franchiseCode; 
 } 
@return the franchiseName 
 public String getFranchiseName() { 
  return franchiseName; 
 } 
@return the frachiseLocation 
 public String getFrachiseLocation() { 
  return frachiseLocation; 
 } 
@return the players 
 public Players[] getPlayers() { 
  return players; 
 } 
 public void details() 
 { 
  System.out.println(); 
  System.out.println("***********Frachise Details**************"); 
  System.out.println("Franchise Code :: "+franchiseCode); 
  System.out.println("Franchise Name :: "+franchiseName); 
  System.out.println("Franchise Location :: "+frachiseLocation); 
  System.out.println(); 
  System.out.println("***********Player Details**************"); 
  for(Players Player : players) 
  { 
   System.out.println("Player ID :: "+Player.getPlayerID()); 
   System.out.println("Player Name :: "+Player.getPlayerName()); 
   System.out.println("Player Board :: "+Player.getBoard()); 
  System.out.println("Player Address :: "+Player.getPlayerAddress()); 
   System.out.println(); 
  } 
 }

package STUDENT_COLLEGE; 
public class STUDENT { 
 private int studentID; 
 private String studentName; 
 private String studentBranch; 
 private String studentAddress; 
 //Generating Setters to set the Value 
 /** 
  * @param studentID the studentID to set 
  */ 
 public void setStudentID(int studentID) { 
  this.studentID = studentID; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @param studentName the studentName to set 
  */ 
 public void setStudentName(String studentName) { 
  this.studentName = studentName; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @param studentBranch the studentBranch to set 
  */ 
 public void setStudentBranch(String studentBranch) { 
  this.studentBranch = studentBranch; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @param studentAddress the studentAddress to set 
  */ 
 public void setStudentAddress(String studentAddress) { 
  this.studentAddress = studentAddress; 
 } 
 // Generating the Getters to Get the value; 
 /** 
  * @return the studentID 
  */ 
 public int getStudentID() { 
  return studentID; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @return the studentName 
  */ 
 public String getStudentName() { 
  return studentName; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @return the studentBranch 
  */ 
 public String getStudentBranch() { 
  return studentBranch; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @return the studentAddress 
  */ 
 public String getStudentAddress() { 
  return studentAddress; 
 } 
} 
package STUDENT_COLLEGE; 
public class College { 
 private int collegeid; 
 private String collegeCode; 
 private String collegeName; 
 private String collegeAddress; 
 // intilizing the HAS A Variable 
 private STUDENT students[]; 
 public void setCollegeid(int collegeid) { 
  this.collegeid = collegeid; 
 } 
 public void setCollegeCode(String collegeCode) { 
  this.collegeCode = collegeCode; 
 } 
 public void setCollegeName(String collegeName) { 
  this.collegeName = collegeName; 
 } 
 public void setCollegeAddress(String collegeAddress) { 
  this.collegeAddress = collegeAddress; 
 } 
 public void setStudents(STUDENT[] students) { 
  this.students = students; 
 } 
 public int getCollegeid() { 
  return collegeid; 
 } 
 public String getCollegeCode() { 
  return collegeCode; 
 } 
 public String getCollegeName() { 
  return collegeName; 
 } 
 public String getCollegeAddress() { 
  return collegeAddress; 
 } 
 public STUDENT[] getStudents() { 
  return students; 
 } 
 public void Details() 
 { 
  System.out.println(); 
  System.out.println("***************COLLEGE 
INFO*********************"); 
  System.out.println("COLLEGE NAME  :: "+collegeName); 
  System.out.println("COLLEGE CODE  :: "+collegeCode); 
  System.out.println("COLLEGE ID  :: "+collegeid); 
  System.out.println("COLLEGE ADDRESS  :: "+collegeAddress); 
  System.out.println("-----------------------------------------------
"); 
  System.out.println("***************STUDENTS 
INFO*********************"); 
  for(STUDENT stu : students) 
  { 
   System.out.println(); 
   System.out.println("STUDENT NAME  :: "+stu.getStudentName()); 
   System.out.println("STUDENT ID  :: "+stu.getStudentID()); 
   System.out.println("STUDENT BRANCH  :: 
"+stu.getStudentBranch()); 
   System.out.println("STUDENT NAME  :: "+stu.getStudentAddress()); 
   System.out.println(); 
  } 
 } 
}

package Studend_College_Counseling; 
public class COLLEGE { 
 private String collegeCode; 
 private String collegeName; 
 private int collegeID; 
 // Intilizeing the has varible 
 /** /// Creating the constructors 
  * @param collegeCode 
  * @param collegeName 
  * @param collegeID 
  */ 
 public COLLEGE(String collegeCode, String collegeName, int 
collegeID) { 
  this.collegeCode = collegeCode; 
  this.collegeName = collegeName; 
  this.collegeID = collegeID; 
 } 
 /** Generating the Getters 
  * @return the collegeCode 
  */ 
 public String getCollegeCode() { 
  return collegeCode; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @return the collegeName 
  */ 
 public String getCollegeName() { 
  return collegeName; 
 } 
 /** 
  * @return the collegeID 
  */ 
 public int getCollegeID() { 
  return collegeID; 
 } 
}

Many to Many Association 
======================== 
It refers to relationship b/w entites, where mulitple instance of one entity should be mapped to 
Multiple instance of another entity. 
eg: Many students have taken Many courses 
public class Course{//Many 
private Integer cid; 
private String cname; 
private Integer cost; 
} 
public class Student{//Many 
private Integer sid; 
private String sname; 
//HAS-A 
private Course[] course; 
} 
refer: Many-Many-Association(Construtor Injection) 
Many-One-Association(Construtor Injection) 
refer: Many-To-Many.png 
Many-To-One.png 
Course 2 
{Python,SQL} 
Course 3 
{html & css and Java 
Script} 
 Code Example: 
Similar procedure hear I am taking the Example for Courses and Students. Here 
I am taking the Courses as Dependent Object and Students as Target Object.(By 
Using Constructor Injection).  
package Student_and_Courses; 
public class Courses  
{ 
 private int courseID; 
 private String courseName; 
 private int coursePrice; 
 //Creating the Constructor to set the value 
 public Courses(int courseID,String courseName,int 
coursePrice) 
 { 
  this.courseID=courseID; 
  this.courseName=courseName; 
  this.coursePrice=coursePrice; 
 } 
 // Generating the Setters to Set Value 
 public int getcourseID() 
 { 
  return courseID; 
 } 
 public String getcourseName() 
 { 
  return courseName; 
 } 
 public int getcoursePrice() 
 { 
  return coursePrice; 
 } 
} 
package Student_and_Courses; 
public class Students1 { 
 private int registerID; 
 private String studentName; 
 private String phoneNumber; 
 private String studentAddress; 
 // Intilizing the Has A Variable 
 Courses []courses; 
 /** Creating the constructor to set values 
 public Students1(int registerID, String studentName, String 
phoneNumber, String studentAddress, Courses []courses) { 
  this.registerID = registerID; 
  this.studentName = studentName; 
  this.phoneNumber = phoneNumber; 
  this.studentAddress = studentAddress; 
  this.courses = courses; 
 } 
 /// generating the getters to set the values. 
 public int getRegisterID() { 
  return registerID; 
 } 
 public String getStudentName() { 
  return studentName; 
 } 
 public String getPhoneNumber() { 
  return phoneNumber; 
 } 
 public String getStudentAddress() { 
  return studentAddress; 
 } 
 public Courses[] getCourses() { 
  return courses; 
 } 
 public void courseDetails() 
 { 
  System.out.println(); 
  System.out.println("**************Student 
Details****************"); 
  System.out.println("STUDENT RegID :: "+registerID); 
  System.out.println("STUDENT Name :: "+studentName); 
  System.out.println("STUDENT Phone Number :: "+phoneNumber); 
  System.out.println("STUDENT Address :: "+studentAddress); 
  System.out.println("----------------------------------------------"); 
  System.out.println(); 
  System.out.println("**************Courses 
Details****************"); 
  for(Courses course : courses) 
  { 
   System.out.println("COURSE ID :: "+course.getcourseID()); 
   System.out.println("COURSE Name :: 
"+course.getcourseName()); 
   System.out.println("COURSE Price :: 
"+course.getcoursePrice()); 
   //System.out.println("COURSE Total 
Price"+course.getcoursePrice(); 
  } 
 } 
} 
package Student_and_Courses.TestAPP; 
import Student_and_Courses.*; 
public class Student_Courses_Test_APP  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 { 
  // Depenent Object 
  Courses java = new Courses(001,"JAVA",6000); 
  Courses python = new Courses(002,"PYTHON",5000); 
  Courses SQL = new Courses(003,"SQL",3000); 
  Courses csharp = new Courses(004,"C- Sharp",4500); 
  Courses javaScript = new Courses(005,"JAVA SCRIPT",5500); 
  Courses htmlcss = new Courses(006,"HTML & CSS",2000); 
 // Courses courses[] = new Courses[] 
{java,python,SQL,csharp,javaScript,htmlcss}; 
  Courses fullStack[] = new Courses[] {java,SQL,javaScript,htmlcss}; 
  Courses java_backend[] = new Courses[] {java,SQL}; 
  Courses dotnet_backend[] = new Courses[] {csharp,SQL}; 
  Courses dataScience[] = new Courses[] {python,SQL}; 
  Courses frontend[] = new Courses[] {htmlcss,javaScript}; 
  //Target Object 
  Students1 teja = new 
Students1(2356,"Teja","9346337502","RJY",fullStack); 
  Students1 nani = new 
Students1(1568,"Nani","8897942995","RJY",java_backend); 
  Students1 sriram = new Students1(15698,"Sri 
Ram","9695841573","Vizag",dotnet_backend); 
  Students1 jagadeedsh = new 
Students1(15698,"Jagadeesh","9356892147","Vizag",dataScience); 
  Students1 pavan = new 
Students1(15698,"Pavan","9695841573","Rpk",frontend); 
  /// Storing Students details; 
  Students1 []students = new Students1[] 
{teja,nani,sriram,jagadeedsh,pavan}; 
  for(Students1 std : students) 
  { 
   std.courseDetails(); 
   if(std.getCourses()== fullStack) 
   { 
    System.out.println("Courses Total Price :: 
"+(java.getcoursePrice()+SQL.getcoursePrice()+javaScript.getcoursePrice()+htmlcs
s.getcoursePrice())); 
   } 
   else if(std.getCourses()== java_backend) 
   { 
    System.out.println("Courses Total Price :: 
"+(java.getcoursePrice()+SQL.getcoursePrice())); 
   } 
   else if(std.getCourses() == dotnet_backend) 
   { 
    System.out.println("Courses Total Price :: 
"+(csharp.getcoursePrice()+SQL.getcoursePrice())); 
   }

 }
