Aggregation and Composition: 
What is the difference b/w Composition and Aggregation? 
Aggregation => In case of Aggregation,even if the contained object does not exist still the 
Container object can be reused. 
Compostion => In case of Composition,if the contained object does not exist then container 
Object can't be reused. 
eg: Relationship b/w library and student => Aggregation  
Relationship b/w library and books => Composition 
Relationship b/w Department and Professor => Aggregation 
Relationship b/w University and Department => Composition 
Relationhsip b/w Human and Heart => Composition 
Relationship b/w Mobile and charger => Aggregation 
refer:Composition vs Aggregation.png 
Over –View: 
Container
. 
Libary  
HAS A 
Container Objects 
Books 
If Books does’nt exist issue with 
library.Composition 
HAS A 
Students 
If student does’nt exist no issue with 
the library. Aggregation 
Abstraction: 
Abstraction is one of the fundamental concepts in Java and object-oriented programming 
(OOP) in general. It refers to the process of simplifying complex reality by modeling classes 
based on the essential properties and behaviors of objects, while hiding unnecessary details. 
Abstraction allows you to create a blueprint or template for objects, defining what they can do 
(methods) and what they are (attributes or fields) without specifying the exact implementation. 
In Java, abstraction is achieved primarily through two mechanisms: abstract classes and 
interfaces. 
Abstract Classes: 
 An abstract class is a class that cannot be instantiated (you cannot create 
objects of an abstract class directly). 
 It serves as a blueprint for other classes that extend it. 
 Abstract classes can have both abstract methods (methods without a body) 
and concrete methods (methods with an implementation). 
 Subclasses that extend an abstract class must provide implementations for 
all the abstract methods unless they are also declared as abstract. 
 Abstract can be used only for a class and the methods,we can not use for 
the variables and the class. 
 We can not create Object for Abstarct Class. We can create Referance of 
Abstract class. 
 Abstarct means incomplect. 
Abstract Methods: 
 . Abstract Methods are such methods, which have only Method Signature 
and does not have body. 
 In java – in a Class one Method is abstract the we have make sure that Class 
also should abstract. 
Final Method Can be 
inheritaded. 
package Abstraction; 
import javax.swing.plaf.synth.SynthOptionPaneUI; 
abstract class plane_p 
{ 
 abstract public void fly(); 
 abstract public void takeOFF(); 
} 
class cargo_plane extends plane_p 
{ 
 public void fly() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Cargo planes are fly at low height"); 
 } 
 public void takeOFF() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Cargo planes needs long run Way"); 
 } 
} 
class fighter_plane extends plane_p 
{ 
 public void fly() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Fighter planes are fly at High height"); 
 } 
 public void takeOFF() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Fighter planes needs small run Way"); 
 } 
} 
class passenger_plane extends plane_p 
{ 
 public void fly() 
 { 
  System.out.println("passenger planes are fly at Medium height"); 
 } 
 public void takeOFF() 
 { 
  System.out.println("passenger planes needs small run Way"); 
 } 
} 
class TakeoffLand 
{ 
 public void premits(plane_p pl) 
 { 
  pl.fly(); 
  pl.takeOFF(); 
 } 
} 
public class Abs_code1  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  plane_p cp = new cargo_plane(); 
  plane_p fp = new fighter_plane(); 
  plane_p pp = new passenger_plane(); 
  TakeoffLand tl = new TakeoffLand(); 
  int count=0; 
  plane_p []planes = new plane_p[]{cp,fp,pp}; 
  for(plane_p plane : planes) 
  { 
   count++; 
   System.out.println("-------------------------------"+count); 
   System.out.println(); 
   tl.premits(plane); 
   System.out.println(); 
  } 
 } 
} 
Out put: -------------------------------1 
Cargo planes are fly at low height 
Cargo planes needs long run Way 
 -------------------------------2 
Fighter planes are fly at High height 
Fighter planes needs small run Way 
 -------------------------------3 
passenger planes are fly at Medium height 
passenger planes needs small run Way

package Abstraction; 
import java.util.*; 
abstract class Shapes 
{ 
 float area; 
 abstract void input(); 
 abstract void compute(); 
 public void display() 
 { 
  System.out.println("The area is "+area+" mm^2"); 
 } 
} 
class Rectangle extends Shapes 
{ 
     float len,bre; 
 @Override 
 void input() { 
  System.out.println("Rectangle"); 
  Scanner s = new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.println("Enter the length of the rectangle"); 
   len = s.nextFloat(); 
  System.out.println("Enter the Breadth of the rectangle"); 
   bre = s.nextFloat(); 
 } 
 @Override 
 void compute() { 
  area = len*bre; 
 } 
} 
class Sqaure extends Shapes 
{ 
     float len; 
 @Override 
 void input() { 
  System.out.println("Square"); 
  Scanner s = new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.println("Enter the length of the Square"); 
   len = s.nextFloat(); 
 } 
 @Override 
 void compute() { 
  area = len*len; 
 } 
} 
Conclusion: 
Final Class True 
Abstract Class True 
Final abstract class False  
Final abstract method  False 
Final variable True 
Abstract variable  False  
class Circle extends Shapes 
{ 
     float rad; 
 @Override 
 void input() { 
  System.out.println("Circle"); 
  Scanner s = new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.println("Enter the radius of the Square"); 
   rad = s.nextFloat();  
 } 
 @Override 
 void compute() { 
  area =(3.14f)*rad*rad; 
 } 
} 
class Geomentry 
{ 
 void permists(Shapes s) 
 { 
  s.input(); 
  s.compute(); 
  s.display(); 
 } 
} 
public class Abs_Code2 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Shapes re = new Rectangle(); 
  Shapes sq = new Sqaure(); 
  Shapes ci = new Circle(); 
  Geomentry geo = new Geomentry(); 
  Shapes sp[] = new Shapes[] {re,sq,ci};int count=0; 
  for(int i=0;i<sp.length;i++) 
  { 
   count++; 
   System.out.println("--------Shape---------"+count); 
   geo.permists(sp[i]); 
   System.out.println(); 
  } 
 } 
}

Interface: 
In Java, an interface is a way to define a contract or a set of abstract methods that 
a class must implement. Interfaces provide a way to achieve abstraction and 
define a common API for a group of related classes. Here are the key points to 
understand about interfaces in Java: 
Declaration: 
 An interface is declared using the interface keyword followed by the 
interface name. 
 It can only contain method declarations, constant declarations (implicitly 
public, static, and final), and default methods (introduced in Java 8) with 
method bodies. 
Method Signatures: 
 Interface methods have no method bodies; they are implicitly public and 
abstract. 
 Classes that implement an interface must provide concrete 
implementations (method bodies) for all the methods declared in the 
interface. 
Multiple Inheritance: 
 Java allows a class to implement multiple interfaces. This is a way to 
achieve multiple inheritance of types because a class can inherit the method 
signatures (contract) from multiple interfaces. 
Conclusion: 
 Interface is requirement specification / blue print of a class. 
 100% Abstraction can be achieved by using the Interface/By using abstract 
class we achive (0 to 100%) 
 Mutiple Inheritance can be achived by using Interface concept. 
Key Points: 
1. In a class if we write one method is abstract then we have to change the 
class also abstract.Coming to interface by defineally java will understand 
those methods are abstract Methods. 
2.   
3.  Interface is collection of public abstract methods. 
4. The nature of Interface is defiantly public. 
5. Interface helps to Achive Standardization. 
6. Interface can act blue print of a class. 
7. One interface has Multiple Implementation  
8. Polymorphism can be achived by using interface and Object can’t be 
created to Interface instead of that we can create Reference of the Interface. 
9. One Interface can be Extended to Another Interface that is allowed in java 
interface calculater 
{ 
 void add();  // public abstract void add(); 
 void sub();  //  public abstract void sub(); 
}  // by default those methods are public abstract 
interface  Demo  
{ 
 void add(); 
} 
interface Demo1 extends Demo 
{ 
 void sub(); 
} 
Mutiple Inheritance can be achived by using Interface concept. 
package InterFace; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
interface calculater 
{ 
 void add();  // public abstract void add(); 
 void sub();  //  public abstract void sub(); 
} 
class MyCal_1 implements calculater 
{ 
 public void add() 
 { 
  Scanner scan=new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.println("Please enter 1st number to add"); 
  int a=scan.nextInt(); 
  System.out.println("Please enter 2nd number to add"); 
  int b=scan.nextInt(); 
  int c=a+b; 
  System.out.println("The Sum of Values are :"+c); 
 } 
 public void sub() 
 { 
  Scanner scan=new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.println("Please enter 1st number to Sub"); 
  int a=scan.nextInt(); 
  System.out.println("Please enter 2nd number to Sub"); 
  int b=scan.nextInt(); 
  int c=a-b; 
  System.out.println("The Sub of Values are :"+c); 
 } 
} 
class MyCal_2 implements calculater 
{ 
 public void add() { 
  int a=10; 
  int b=20; 
  int c=a+b; 
  System.out.println("----------------------------------------------"); 
  System.out.println("The Sum of Values are :"+c); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public void sub() { 
  int a=30; 
  int b=20; 
  int c=a-b; 
  System.out.println("----------------------------------------------"); 
  System.out.println("The Sub of Values are :"+c); 
 } 
} 
class Results 
{ 
 public void getResults(calculater res) 
 { 
  res.add(); 
  res.sub(); 
 } 
} 
public class InterFace_exp1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  calculater cal1 = new MyCal_1(); 
  calculater cal2 = new MyCal_2(); 
  Results res = new Results(); 
  calculater []cal = new calculater[] {cal1,cal2}; 
  for(calculater result : cal) 
  { 
   res.getResults(result); 
  } 
 } 
} 
Out put: 
Please enter 1st number to add 
21 
Please enter 2nd number to add 
39 
The Sum of Values are :60 
Please enter 1st number to Sub 
54 
Please enter 2nd number to Sub 
21 
The Sub of Values are :33 ---------------------------------------------- 
The Sum of Values are :30 ---------------------------------------------- 
The Sub of Values are :10

package InterFace; 
interface cal1 
{ 
 void add(int a,int b); 
} 
interface cal2 
{ 
 int sub(int a,int b); 
} 
class myCal implements cal1,cal2 
{ 
 public int sub(int a, int b) { 
  int c=a-b; 
  return c; 
 } 
 public void add(int a, int b) { 
  int c=a+b; 
  System.out.println("After the Sum :"+c); 
 } 
} 
public class InterFace_exp2  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  myCal ca = new myCal(); 
  ca.add(26,34); 
  System.out.println("After the Sub :"+ca.sub(32, 24)); 
 } 
}

After the Sum :60 
After the Sub :8

package InterFace; 
 import java.util.Scanner; 
interface Calcu 
{ 
 void add(); 
} 
class MyCal2  
{ 
 void sub() 
 { 
  int a=60; 
  int b=30; 
  int c=a-b; 
  System.out.println("After performing the Sum : "+c);  
 } 
} 
class MyC extends MyCal2 implements Calcu 
{ 
 public void add() 
 { 
  Scanner scan=new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.println("Please enter 1st number to add"); 
  int a=scan.nextInt(); 
  System.out.println("Please enter 2nd number to add"); 
  int b=scan.nextInt(); 
  int c=a+b; 
  System.out.println("After performing the Sum : "+c); 
  scan.close(); 
 } 
} 
public class InterFace_exp3 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  MyC cp = new MyC(); 
  cp.sub(); 
  cp.add(); 
 } 
}

 Final – we can not change the value.

10th Sept Live Class Functional Interface, Lambda Expression, Package in 
Java: 
Functional Interface: 
In Java, a functional interface is an interface that has exactly one abstract method. Functional 
interfaces are also sometimes referred to as "Single Abstract Method" (SAM) interfaces. These 
interfaces are a key feature of Java's support for functional programming and the use of lambda 
expressions. 
Here are the key characteristics and rules for functional interfaces in Java: 
Single Abstract Method (SAM): 
 A functional interface must have only one abstract method. It can have multiple default 
or static methods, but only one abstract method. 
@FunctionalInterface Annotation: 
 While it's not mandatory, it's a good practice to annotate functional interfaces with the 
@FunctionalInterface annotation. This annotation serves as a compiler directive to 
ensure that the interface meets the requirements of a functional interface. 
 If you annotate an interface with @FunctionalInterface and it has more than one 
abstract method or no abstract methods at all, the compiler will generate an error. 
Functional Interface can be implemented by using thease methods: 
 General Approach – [as Mensioned in above codes] 
 Anonymous Inner Class. 
 Lambads Expression. 
Anonymous Inner class: 
In Java, an anonymous inner class is a class that is defined and instantiated without giving it a 
name. It's typically used for creating small, one-time-use classes that override methods or 
implement interfaces in a concise manner. Anonymous inner classes are often used in event 
handling and for implementing interfaces with a minimal amount of code. 
General Approach : 
 Determine whether you need to create a new functional interface or if an existing one 
already suits your needs. 
 If creating a new one, define it with a single abstract method that matches the desired 
functional behavior. 
Code Example: 
Anonymous Inner Class for an Interface: 
 Anonymous inner classes are commonly used to implement interfaces with a single 
abstract method (functional interfaces). 
 You can create an anonymous inner class by using the new keyword followed by the 
interface name or class name (if implementing an interface) and providing the 
implementation for the abstract method. 
package Functional_Interface; 
@FunctionalInterface 
interface FunC1 
{ 
 void display(); // public abatract void display(); 
   default void show() 
   { 
    System.out.println("This Defalut Method"); 
   } 
} 
class Fun_exc implements FunC1 
{ 
 public void display() 
 { 
  System.out.println("This is abstract over ridden in Fun_exc 
class"); 
 } 
} 
public class Funcational_interface_c1  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  FunC1 fc = new Fun_exc(); 
  fc.display(); 
  fc.show(); 
 } 
} 
Out put: 
This is abstract over 
ridden in Fun_exc class 
This Defalut Method 
Code Exp: 
package Functional_Interface; 
interface Algo 
{ 
 int linearSearch(int arr[],int target); 
} 
class linear_search 
{ 
 Algo algo = new Algo() 
 { 
     @Override 
  public int linearSearch(int[] arr, int target) { 
   for(int i=0;i<arr.length;i++) 
   { 
    if(arr[i]== target) 
    { 
     return i; 
    } 
   } 
      return -1; 
  } 
 }; 
} 
public class Anonymous_InnerClass  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  int arr[] =new int[] {3,2,1,4,5}; 
  int target_num = 1; 
  linear_search LnS = new linear_search(); 
     int res = LnS.algo.linearSearch(arr, target_num); 
  if(res != 1) 
  { 
  System.out.println(target_num+" Element found at index  "+res); 
  } 
  else 
  { 
   System.out.println("Element not found"); 
  } 
 } 
} 
Output: 
1 Element found at index  2 
We can implement Anonymous Inner class with out using the InterFace. 
i.e Class level also we can implement the Anonymous Innerclass. 
Code exp2: 
Lambda Expressions: 
 Functional interfaces are typically used with lambda expressions to provide 
concise and expressive implementations of the single abstract method. 
 If your implementation is straightforward and can be expressed in a concise 
manner, consider using lambda expressions instead of defining a separate 
class. 
 Lambda expressions can make your code more readable and expressive. 
package Functional_Interface; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
abstract class Ano1 
{ 
 abstract public int add(); 
} 
public class Anonymous_inner2  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Ano1 an = new Ano1() 
    { 
         @Override 
         public int add() 
         { 
        Scanner in = new Scanner(System.in); 
 System.out.println("Enter the 1st number to add : "); 
         int a =in.nextInt(); 
     System.out.println("Enter the 2nd number to add : "); 
         int b =in.nextInt(); 
         int c = a+b; 
 System.out.println("The Sum of two numbers are :"+c); 
     return c;  
         } 
   }; 
   an.add(); 
 } 
} 
Out put: 
Enter the 1st number to add :  
23 
Enter the 2nd number to add :

package LamdaExpression; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
interface Shape 
{ 
 float area_of_Traiangle(); 
} 
public class Lamada_C1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Shape s = ()-> 
  { 
   Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
   System.out.print("Enter the Base of Triangle : "); 
   float base = sc.nextFloat(); 
   System.out.print("Enter the height of Triangle : "); 
   float height = sc.nextFloat(); 
   float area = ((1/2f)*base*height); 
   System.out.println("The are of Triangle is :"+ 
area+"mm^2"); 
   return area; 
  }; 
  s.area_of_Traiangle(); 
 } 
}

Enter the height of Triangle : 5

package LamdaExpression; 
@FunctionalInterface 
interface Calculator { 
    int calculate(int a, int b); 
} 
public class Lamada_C2 { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        // Step 2: Implement the Functional Interface 
        // Step 3: Use Lambda Expressions (Optional) 
        Calculator addition = (a, b) -> a + b; 
        Calculator subtraction = (a, b) -> a - b; 
        // Step 4: Instantiate and Use Functional Interface Objects 
        int result1 = addition.calculate(10, 5); // result1 is 15 
        int result2 = subtraction.calculate(10, 5); // result2 is 5 
        System.out.println("Addition result: " + result1); 
        System.out.println("Subtraction result: " + result2); 
    } 
} 
Out put: 
Addition result: 15 
Subtraction result: 5 
Packages : 
It is an encapuslation mechanism to group all the related classes and interface in 
single module 
While using inbuilt classes also, internally sunmicrosystem has used the pacakges 
to keep the classes. 
Objectives of packages 
===================== 
1. It resolves the name conflicts 
2. It imporoves modularity(maintainence) of the application 
3. It provides security 
4. It helps the programmer to debug the application in a easy way be referring to 
the pacakges. 
packages naming convention followed by sunmicrosystem 
Over view: 
In Java, a package is a way to organize related classes and interfaces into a group or 
namespace. Packages provide several benefits, including encapsulation, preventing 
naming conflicts, and making it easier to manage and maintain code in large 
applications. Here are some key points to understand about packages in Java: 
Package Declaration: 
 You declare a package at the top of your Java source file using the package 
keyword, followed by the package name. 
 The package declaration should be the first non-comment statement in the 
source file. 
javaCopy code 
package com.example.myapp; 
Package Structure: 
 Packages are hierarchical, and their names are typically based on a reverse 
domain name, ensuring uniqueness across projects. 
 For example, com.example.myapp is a common package naming convention. 
Directory Structure: 
 Java enforces a directory structure that matches the package hierarchy. Each 
level of the package corresponds to a directory. 
 For the com.example.myapp package, you would organize your source files in 
a directory structure like this: 
Copy code 
myapp 
├── com 
│   
└── example 
│       
└── myapp 
│          
 └── YourClass.java 
Import Statements: 
 To use classes or interfaces from other packages in your code, you need to 
import them using the import statement. 
 The import statement allows you to refer to classes by their simple names 
instead of fully qualified names (package name + class name). 
java 
Copy code 
import java.util.ArrayList; 
Access Modifiers: 
 Classes, interfaces, and members (fields, methods) within a package have 
package-private access by default. 
 Classes and members declared as public are accessible from outside the package. 
Default Package: 
 If you don't specify a package in your Java source file, the classes in that file 
belong to the default package. 
 However, it's considered a best practice to always define a package for your 
classes to avoid naming conflicts and ensure code organization. 
Jar Files: 
 Java Archive (JAR) files are used to bundle compiled classes, resources, and 
packages together for distribution and reuse. 
 You can package your classes into JAR files, making it easier to share your code 
with others. 
Java Standard Libraries: 
 Java provides a standard library organized into packages, such as java.util, 
java.io, and java.lang, which are automatically available to your Java programs. 
Creating Your Own Packages: 
 To create your own package, you need to organize your classes in directories 
matching the package structure and specify the package name in your source 
files. 
 Java packages are a fundamental part of Java development, helping you organize 
code into manageable units, promote code reuse, and avoid naming conflicts. 
They are especially useful in large-scale applications where code organization 
and separation of concerns are crucial. 
 11th Sept Live Class Exception Handling part 1:  
Exception Handling: 
Exception handling is a crucial aspect of programming in Java, allowing you to gracefully 
handle unexpected or exceptional situations that may occur during program execution. Java 
provides a robust mechanism for exception handling using a combination of keywords, try
catch blocks, and the throw and throws keywords. Here's an overview of how exception 
handling works in Java: 
Types of Exceptions: 
Checked Exceptions: 
These are exceptions that are checked at compile-time. You must either catch them using try
catch blocks or declare them using the throws keyword in the method signature. Examples 
include IOException and SQLException. 
Unchecked Exceptions: 
Also known as runtime exceptions, these exceptions are not checked at compile-time. They 
typically result from programming errors and are subclasses of RuntimeException. Examples 
include NullPointerException, ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException, and ArithmeticException. 
try-catch Blocks: 
 Use a try block to enclose the code that might throw an exception. 
 Use one or more catch blocks to catch and handle exceptions. Each catch block can 
handle a specific type of exception. 
 You can have a finally block after catch blocks to specify code that always executes, 
whether or not an exception occurs. 
 Exp_C1:                                          
ArithmeticException 
In Java, an ArithmeticException is a type of unchecked exception that occurs during 
arithmetic operations. This exception is thrown when an exceptional arithmetic condition is 
encountered. The most common arithmetic operations that can throw an ArithmeticException 
include division by zero and integer overflow. 
Integer Overflow: 
Another situation that can lead to an ArithmeticException is when you perform an operation 
that results in an integer overflow. For example, if you try to add two very large integers that 
exceed the maximum value representable by an int, an overflow occurs.

  } 
  catch(Exception e) 
  { 
   System.out.println("Please provide non zero 
denominotor"+e); 
  } 
   System.out.println("Thank you for using our application");   
 } 
}

NullPointerException: 
In Java, a NullPointerException is a common runtime exception that occurs when you attempt to 
access or invoke a method on an object that is currently null. This exception typically results from 
programming errors where you assume that an object reference points to a valid object, but it 
doesn't. 
package Exception_Handeling; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
public class Exception_Handeling_C2  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  //Null Pointer Exception 
  try 
  { 
   Scanner in = new Scanner(System.in); 
   System.out.println("Enter the String :"); 
   String s = null; 
   if(!s .equals(null)) 
   { 
    s.length(); 
    System.out.println(s.length()); 
   } 
   else 
   { 
    in.close(); 
   } 
  } 
  catch(Exception e) 
  { 
   System.out.println("String is Null : "+e); 
  } 
 } 
} 
Out put: 
Enter the String : 
String is Null : java.lang.NullPointerException: Cannot invoke 
"String.equals(Object)" because "s" is null 
NumberFormatException: 
In Java, a NumberFormatException is a runtime exception that occurs when you attempt 
to convert a string into a numeric format (e.g., integer or floating-point) using methods 
like parseInt() or parseDouble(), but the string does not represent a valid numeric value.

ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException 
In Java, an ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException is a runtime exception that occurs when you 
try to access an element of an array using an index that is outside the valid range of indices for 
that array. The valid index range for an array in Java is from 0 to array.length - 1. Attempting 
to access an index less than 0 or greater than or equal to array.length will result in this 
exception. 
package Exception_Handeling; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
public class Exception_HandelingC4  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  //Array Out of Bound Exception 
  try 
  { 
   Scanner in = new Scanner(System.in); 
   System.out.println("Enter the size of the array"); 
   int size = in.nextInt(); 
   int arr[] = new int[size]; 
   System.out.println("Enter the elements in Array"); 
   for(int i=0;i<arr.length+1;i++) 
   { 
    arr[i]= in.nextInt(); 
   } 
   System.out.print(arr); 
   in.close(); 
  } 
  catch(Exception e) 
  { 
   System.out.println("if fails throw the exception"+e); 
  } 
 } 
}

Throw: 
 The throw keyword is used to explicitly throw an exception within your code. You 
can use it to create and throw custom exceptions or propagate existing exceptions 
up the call stack. 
 When you throw an exception using the throw keyword, you are signaling that 
something unexpected or erroneous has occurred, and you want to notify the 
program about it. 
package Throw_and_Throws; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
class ThrowTest  
{ 
 public void throwExp() { 
  try { 
   System.out.println("Welcome to division performing application"); 
   Scanner scan = new Scanner(System.in); 
   System.out.println("Enter the first Number to divide"); 
   int a = scan.nextInt(); 
   System.out.println("Enter the second number"); 
   int b = scan.nextInt(); 
   int res = a / b; 
   scan.close(); 
   System.out.println("The result is " + res); 
  }  
  catch (ArithmeticException e) { 
   System.out.println("This Exception occuren throwExp()" + e); 
      throw e; 
  } 
 } 
} 
public class Throw  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 { 
   ThrowTest exp = new ThrowTest(); 
   exp.throwExp(); 
 } 
}

package Throw_and_Throws; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
class ThrowTest  
{ 
 public void throwExp() throws ArithmeticException{ 
  try { 
 System.out.println("Welcome to division performing application"); 
   Scanner scan = new Scanner(System.in); 
   System.out.println("Enter the first Number to divide"); 
   int a = scan.nextInt(); 
   System.out.println("Enter the second number"); 
   int b = scan.nextInt(); 
   int res = a / b; 
   scan.close(); 
   System.out.println("The result is " + res); 
  }  
  catch (ArithmeticException e) { 
   System.out.println("This Exception occuren throwExp()" + e); 
      throw e; 
  } 
  finally 
  { 
   System.out.println("Thanks For Using this Application "); 
  } 
 } 
} 
public class Throw  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 { 
  try 
  { 
     ThrowTest exp = new ThrowTest(); 
     exp.throwExp(); 
  } 
  catch(Exception e) 
  { 
   System.out.println("This is Handeled in Main Method() "+e); 
  } 
 } 
}

package Throw_and_Throws; 
class Trow 
{ 
 public int someMethod(int value)throws IllegalArgumentException { 
    try  
    { 
  if (value < 0) { 
         throw new IllegalArgumentException("Value cannot be negative");   
     } 
  return 1; 
    }catch(Exception e) 
    { 
     System.out.println(" Failed Exception "+e); 
     return -1; 
    } 
 } 
} 
public class Throw2  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  try 
  { 
  Trow ts = new Trow(); 
  int res =ts.someMethod(-3); 
  System.out.println(res); 
  }catch(Exception e) 
  { 
     System.out.println(" Failed Exception "+e); 
  } 
 } 
}

Throws: 
 The throws keyword is used in a method declaration to indicate that the method 
may throw one or more exceptions. It specifies the exceptions that might be thrown 
by the method but doesn't actually throw them. 
 When a method declares that it throws exceptions, it's a way of signaling to the 
caller that it should be prepared to handle these exceptions or propagate them 
further. 
package Throw_and_Throws; 
import java.util.*; 
public class Throws  
{ 
 @SuppressWarnings("null") 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws 
InterruptedException,NullPointerException { 
  try 
  { 
   Scanner s = new Scanner(System.in); 
   System.out.println("Enter the String"); 
         String str = s.nextLine(); 
         Thread.sleep(2000); 
         System.out.println("the String "+str); 
         String str2 = null; 
         System.out.println(str2.length()); 
         s.close(); 
  } 
  catch(Exception e) 
  { 
   System.out.println(" The Excepection Occured in Main "+e); 
   //Since Null Pointer Exception is Unchecked Exception. 
  } 
 } 
}

Enter the String 
Test 
the String Test 
 The Excepection Occured in Main

because "str2" is null 
let's consider a real-time example involving a simplified banking system where we have an 
account management class. This class manages bank accounts and allows you to withdraw 
money. In this example, we'll use the throws keyword to indicate that our withdraw method can 
throw a custom InsufficientFundsException.Explectily throwing an Exception 
package Throw_and_Throws; 
class InsufficientFundsException extends Exception {  New Exception is created 
 public InsufficientFundsException(String message) { 
        super(message); 
    } 
} 
class BankAccount { 
    private double balance; 
    public BankAccount(double initialBalance) { 
        balance = initialBalance; 
    } 
    // The 'throws' keyword indicates that this method may throw 
InsufficientFundsException 
    public void withdraw(double amount) throws InsufficientFundsException { 
        if (amount > balance) { 
            throw new InsufficientFundsException("Insufficient funds to withdraw " 
+ amount); //.Explectily throwing an Exception 
        } 
        balance -= amount; 
    } 
    public double getBalance() { 
        return balance; 
    } 
} 
public class BankExample { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        BankAccount account = new BankAccount(1000); 
        try { 
            account.withdraw(1500); // This may throw InsufficientFundsException 
        } catch (InsufficientFundsException e) { 
         System.out.println(e); 
            System.out.println("Error: " + e.getMessage()); 
        } 
        System.out.println("Remaining balance: " + account.getBalance()); 
    } 
} 
Out Put: 
Throw_and_Throws.InsufficientFundsException: Insufficient funds to 
withdraw 1500.0 
Error: Insufficient funds to withdraw 1500.0 
Remaining balance: 1000.0 
Let's consider another real-time example involving a college attendance system where we have 
an attendance management class. This class manages to allow you to achieve a minimum 
attendance percentage. In this example, we'll use the throws keyword to indicate that our 
minimum attention required can throw a custom . Explectily throwing an Exception 
InsufficientAttendenceException. 
package Throw_and_Throws; 
class InSufficientAttendenceException extends Exception 
{ 
 public InSufficientAttendenceException(String msg) 
 { 
  super(msg); 
 } 
} 
class AttendencePerctentage 
{ 
 private double attendece; 
 public AttendencePerctentage(double minAttendence) 
 { 
   this.attendece= minAttendence; 
 } 
 public void attendencePercentage(double percent) throws 
InSufficientAttendenceException 
 { 
  if(percent < this.attendece) 
  { 
   throw new InSufficientAttendenceException("your attendence 
percent is very Low " + percent); Explectily throwing an Exception 
  } 
  this.attendece = percent; 
 } 
 public double getattendence() 
 { 
  return this.attendece; 
 } 
} 
public class Ateres { 
  public static void main(String[] args) { 
   AttendencePerctentage AC = new AttendencePerctentage(75); 
   try 
   { 
    AC.attendencePercentage(70.00); 
   } 
   catch(InSufficientAttendenceException e) 
   { 
    System.out.println(e); 
    System.out.println("Error : "+e.getMessage()); 
   } 
   System.out.println("Your required Attendence Percent 
"+AC.getattendence()); 
 } 
} 
Out put: 
Throw_and_Throws.InSufficientAttendenceException: your attendence 
percent is very Low 70.0 
Error : your attendence percent is very Low 70.0 
Your required Attendence Percent 75.0 
Different Between Throw and Throws: 
Finally Key word: 
Finally: 
The finally keyword in Java is used in association with try-catch blocks to define a block of code 
that will be executed regardless of whether an exception is thrown or not. It is often used to ensure 
that certain cleanup or resource management tasks are performed, such as closing files, database 
connections, or releasing other resources, even if an exception occurs within the try block. 
try { 
    // Code that may throw an exception 
} catch (Exception e) { 
    // Code to handle the exception 
} finally { 
    // Code that will always execute, regardless of whether an exception was thrown or not 
}

package Throw_and_Throws; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
class ThrowTest  
{ 
 public void throwExp() throws ArithmeticException{ 
  try { 
   System.out.println("Welcome to division performing application"); 
   Scanner scan = new Scanner(System.in); 
   System.out.println("Enter the first Number to divide"); 
   int a = scan.nextInt(); 
   System.out.println("Enter the second number"); 
   int b = scan.nextInt(); 
   int res = a / b; 
   scan.close(); 
   System.out.println("The result is " + res); 
  }  
  catch (ArithmeticException e) { 
   System.out.println("This Exception occuren throwExp()" + e); 
   System.out.println("*********1********************"); 
   System.out.println(); 
   System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
   System.out.println(); 
   System.out.println("*********2********************"); 
   System.out.println(); 
   System.out.println(e.toString()); 
   System.out.println(); 
   System.out.println("*********3********************"); 
   System.out.println(); 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
      throw e; 
  } 
  finally 
  { 
   System.out.println("Thanks For Using this Application "); 
  } 
 } 
} 
public class Throw  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 { 
  try 
  { 
     ThrowTest exp = new ThrowTest(); 
     exp.throwExp(); 
  } 
  catch(Exception e) 
  { 
   System.out.println("This is Handeled in Main Method() "+e); 
  } 
 } 
}

Custom/User defined Exception: 
In Java, you can create custom exceptions by extending the Exception class or one of its subclasses (such as 
RuntimeException) to create your own exception classes. This allows you to define exceptions specific to your 
application or library. Here's how you can create a custom exception in Java: 
1. Create a new Java class for your custom exception, and have it extend either Exception or one of its 
subclasses (e.g., RuntimeException): 
2. Customize your custom exception class by adding constructors and methods as needed. You can create 
multiple constructors to allow different ways of initializing your exception. 
3. You can also add any additional methods or properties to your custom exception class that are specific to 
your application's needs. 
4. To throw your custom exception, you can use the throw keyword: 
5. To catch and handle your custom exception, you can use a try-catch block: 
package UserDefined_or_Custom_Exceptions; 
class CustomException extends Exception { 
    public CustomException() { 
        super(); 
    } 
    public CustomException(String message) { 
        super(message); 
    } 
    public CustomException(String message, Throwable cause) { 
        super(message, cause); 
    } 
} 
class CustomExceptionExample { 
    public void someMethod() throws CustomException { 
        // Perform some logic 
        // If an error condition occurs, throw your custom exception 
     String str = null; 
        if (str==null) { 
            throw new CustomException("An error occurred"); 
        } 
    } 
} 
public class Def_and_customException  
{ 
  public static void main(String[] args) { 
   CustomExceptionExample cs = new CustomExceptionExample(); 
   try 
   { 
    cs.someMethod(); 
   }catch(CustomException e) 
   { 
    System.out.println(e+e.getMessage()); 
   } 
 } 
}

error occurredAn error occurred 
Example 2 
package UserDefined_or_Custom_Exceptions; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
class InavalidUserException extends Exception { 
 public InavalidUserException() { 
  super("Invalid Input"); 
 } 
 public InavalidUserException(String message) { 
  super(message); 
 } 
} 
class ATM { 
 private int accountNumber = 3333; 
 private int password = 1234; 
 private int accNum; 
 private int pwd; 
 private int Maxattempt = 3; 
 public void input() { 
  Scanner in = new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.println("*******Enter the account Number**********"); 
  accNum = in.nextInt(); 
  System.out.println("*******Enter the Password **********"); 
  pwd = in.nextInt(); 
 } 
  public void verify() throws InavalidUserException  
  { 
      for (int i = 1; i <= Maxattempt; i++) 
      { 
          if (accountNumber == accNum && password == pwd)  
          { 
              System.out.println("-----collect your cash--------"); 
              return; 
          }  
          else  
          { 
              System.out.println("-----Invalid Credentials---- Please try 
again----"); 
              if (i < Maxattempt) { 
                  System.out.println(); 
                  System.out.println(" Your " + i + " attempt failed"); 
                  System.out.println(); 
                  System.out.println("You have " + (Maxattempt - i) + " 
attempts left"); 
                  System.out.println("========================"); 
                  input(); 
              } 
          } 
      } 
      throw new InavalidUserException("******************Your account 
blocked************"); 
  }   
} 
public class ATM_Exception { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  ATM atm = new ATM(); 
  try { 
   atm.input(); 
   atm.verify(); 
  } catch (InavalidUserException e) { 
   System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
   System.exit(0); 
  } 
 } 
}

Exp2: 
Developing a console base project depending on your age cretaria will provide 
you with the information you need to qualify for a driver's license or not.
package UserDefined_or_Custom_Exceptions; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
class UnderAgeException extends Exception { 
   public UnderAgeException(String msg) { 
  super(msg); 
 } 
} 
class OverageException extends Exception { 
 public OverageException(String msg) { 
  super(msg); 
 } 
} 
class LicienceApp { 
 private String name; 
 private int age; 
 public void Input() { 
  System.out.println("Enter the Name :"); 
  try { 
   Scanner in = new Scanner(System.in); 
   name = in.nextLine(); 
   System.out.println("Enter the Age :"); 
   age = in.nextInt(); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   System.out.println("Failed due to Exception" + e); 
  } 
 } 
public void CheckInput() throws InterruptedException, 
UnderAgeException, OverageException { 
  System.out.println("--Wait for 3 Secound we are checking --
"); 
  Thread.sleep(3000); 
  if (age >= 18 && age <= 60) { 
   System.out.println("<---Congratulations---> "+name); 
   System.out.println(" You are Eligible for Driving 
Licience "); 
  } else if (age < 18) { 
   System.out.println(" Sorry "+ name); 
   throw new UnderAgeException("---> Your age is less than 
18 years you are not eligible"); 
  } else if (age > 60) { 
   System.out.println(" Sorry "+ name); 
   throw new OverageException("---> Your age is more than 
60 years you are not eligible"); 
  } 
 } 
} 
class LicienceVerification { 
 public void Eligiblecriteria() throws InterruptedException, 
UnderAgeException, OverageException { 
  LicienceApp lapp = new LicienceApp(); 
  try { 
   lapp.Input(); 
   lapp.CheckInput(); 
  } catch (UnderAgeException une) { 
   System.out.println(" Failed due to Exception " + une); 
   try { 
    System.out.println("========================="); 
    System.out.println("Enter ur Inputs again"); 
    lapp.Input(); 
    lapp.CheckInput(); 
   } catch (UnderAgeException uae) { 
    System.out.println(uae.getMessage()); 
    System.exit(0); 
   } 
  } catch (OverageException one) { 
   System.out.println(" Failed due to Exception " + one); 
   try { 
    System.out.println("========================="); 
    System.out.println("Enter ur Inputs again"); 
    lapp.Input(); 
    lapp.CheckInput(); 
   } catch (OverageException oae) { 
    System.out.println(oae.getMessage()); 
    System.exit(0); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
} 
public class DrivingLicenceAPP { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  try { 
   LicienceVerification licienceverification = new 
LicienceVerification(); 
   licienceverification.Eligiblecriteria(); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   System.out.println("Failed due to Exception" + e); 
  } 
 } 
}

Summary: 
Exception handling 
============= 
1. try catch and finally 
2. throws(best suited for checkedException) 
3. throw(best sutied for uncheckedException and customException) 
In realtime application,we use many resources where all the resource should be 
closed inside finally block. 
resource => In File operations we use 
FileReader,FileWriter,BufferedReader,BufferedWriter 
In JDBC Operations we use 
Connection,Statement,PreapredStatement,CallableStatement,.... 
JDK1.6V for developers 
================== 
eg: BufferedReader br=null; 
FileReader fr =null; 
try{ 
fr = new FileReader("sample.txt"); 
br = new BuffereReader(); 
} 
catch(IOException e) 
{ 
e.printStackTrace(); 
} 
Finally 
{ 
if(br!=null) 
br.close(); 
if(fr!=null) 
fr.close(); 
} 
boilerplate -> the code which is repeated in multiple modules of project with no 
change or with small change. 
whenever boiler plate code comes into pitcutre, we always try 
to avoid it by using 
a. using JDK software higher version(jdk1.0,jdk1.2,......jdk18) 
b. using 3rd party API's 
In JDK1.7 version they made few enhancement in the Excpetion handling area 
======================================================= 
1. try with resource 
2. try with multicatch block 
try with resource 
============ 
Syntax: try(R){ 
use resource as per ur application requirement 
if exception occurs or not occurs and if it is handled or not handled still Resources will be closed 
once the control comes out of  
try{ 
block. 
}catch(XXXX e){ 
} 
eg: without using try with resource 
===================== 
BufferedReader br=null; 
FileReader fr =null; 
try{ 
fr = new FileReader("sample.txt"); 
br = new BuffereReader(); 
} 
catch(IOException e) 
{ 
e.printStackTrace(); 
} 
Finally 
{ 
if(br!=null) 
br.close(); 
if(fr!=null) 
fr.close(); 
} 
eg: try with resource 
try(BufferedReader br= new BufferedReader(new FileReader("sample.txt"))){ 
//use the resource 
} 
catch(IOException e) 
{ 
e.printStatckTrace(); 
} 
Advantage of try with Resource 
====================== 
1. The main advantage of try with resource is the resources which are a part of 
try block gets close automatically. 
once the control comes of out try block automatically that resource will be 
closed. 
while try block is getting executed 
a. exception occured and handled 
b. exception occured and not handled 
In both these cases also jvm will close the resource automatically, if we 
use resource with "try with resource". 
2. Using try with resource increases readabilty and reduces redundant code in our application. 
2.From JDK1.7 for Resource Releasing logic Requirement specification they had 
come with an interface called 
"AutoCloseable" which is added in "java.lang" package. 
interface AutoCloseable{ 
try(BufferedReader br=new BufferedReader(new FileReader("sample.txt"))){ 
//logic of using br 
} 
catch(IOException e){ 
//handling logic 
} 
Note: try(String name =new String("sachin")){ 
//using name object 
}catch(Exception e){} 
output: Compile Time Error 
All java.io classes and java.sql classes has implemented AutoCloseable 
interface. 
3. All resources reference variable are been made as final automatically when they 
are used, so we can't 
re-assign the reference of the Resource Variable. 
CompileTime Error 
============== 
try(BufferedReader br=new BufferedReader(new FileReader("sachin.txt"))){ 
br=new BufferedReader(new FileReader("kohli.txt"))); 
}catch(IOException e){} 
4. Before JDK1.6 
try{ 
}catch(XXXX e){ 
}finally{ 
} 
After JDK1.7, do we need finaly block ? 
Ans. no 
finally block becomes dummy if we use "try with Resource". 
5. JDK1.6V 
try{ 
}finally{ 
} 
a. if exception does not occur => normal termination/smoothfull termination 
still finally executes. 
b. if exception occurs => abnormal termination still finally executes. 
JDK1.7 
try(R){ 
} 
it is possible to write only try also from JDK1.7 version ,but that try 
should be associated with Resource. 
public abstract void close() throws Exception; 
} 
public class BufferedReader implements AutoCloseable{ 
@Override 
public void close(){ 
//logic of closing. 
} 
} 
Wrapper Classes: 
In Java, wrapper classes are used to represent primitive data types as objects. The 
Java programming language provides a set of classes in the java.lang package that 
serve as wrapper classes for each of the primitive data types. These classes are: 
1. Integer: java.lang.Integer - Wraps an int. 
2. Long: java.lang.Long - Wraps a long. 
3. Float: java.lang.Float - Wraps a float. 
4. Double: java.lang.Double - Wraps a double. 
5. Byte: java.lang.Byte - Wraps a byte. 
6. Short: java.lang.Short - Wraps a short. 
7. Character: java.lang.Character - Wraps a char. 
8. Boolean: java.lang.Boolean - Wraps a boolean. 
In this example, you can see how to create instances of wrapper classes, perform 
autoboxing (converting a primitive to its corresponding wrapper class object implicitly), 
and unboxing (converting a wrapper class object to its corresponding primitive type 
implicitly). 
Wrapper classes are useful in situations where you need to treat primitive data types as 
objects, such as when working with collections that require objects, or when using Java 
generics. 
Example: wrap 
package com.WrapperPackages; 
public class WrapperExp1 { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        // Using wrapper classes to convert primitive data types to objects 
        Integer intObj = new Integer(42); 
        Double doubleObj = new Double(3.14); 
        // Autoboxing: converting primitive to object implicitly 
        Integer autoboxedInt = 10; 
        Double autoboxedDouble = 2.5; 
        // Unboxing: converting object to primitive implicitly 
        int unboxedInt = intObj; 
        double unboxedDouble = doubleObj; 
        System.out.println("Integer Object: " + intObj); 
        System.out.println("Double Object: " + doubleObj); 
        System.out.println("Autoboxed Integer: " + autoboxedInt); 
        System.out.println("Autoboxed Double: " + autoboxedDouble); 
        System.out.println("Unboxed Integer: " + unboxedInt); 
        System.out.println("Unboxed Double: " + unboxedDouble); 
    } 
} 
JDK1.5 features 
=========== 
1.Wrapper classes 
2.Var-Args 
Wrapper class 
========== 
1. To wrap primtive into object form so that we can handle primtive also just like objects 
2. To define several utility function which are requried for primitives. 
3. Wrapper classes are a part of "java.lang" package. 
primtive data types 
============== 
1. byte,short,int,long 
2. float,double 
3. char 
4. boolean 
For every primitive type we have equavilent Wrapper class as shown below 
byte -> Byte 
short -> Short 
int -> Integer 
long -> Long 
float -> Float 
double-> Double 
***char -> Character(1 constructor) 
***boolean -> Boolean(2 constructor(String is important)) 
With Respect to wrapper class how is toString() implemented? 
class Object{ 
public String toString(){ 
// returns the reference(address/hashCodeValue) of the object 
} 
} 
public final class Integer extends Object{ 
@Override 
public String toString(){ 
//returns the data present in the Object 
} 
}  
Almost every Wrapper class contains 2 constructors which takes 
a. primtive type as the argument. 
b. String type as the argument. 
eg#1. 
Integer i1 = new Integer(10); 
System.out.println(i1);//jvm calls i1.toString() 
Integer i2 = new Integer("10"); 
System.out.println(i2);//jvm calls i1.toString() 
output

10

Boolean b=new Boolean(True);//CE 
Boolean b=new Boolean(False);//CE 
Note: If we are passing String argument, then case is not important and content is 
important. 
if the content is case insensitive String of true then it is treated as 
true and in all other cases it is false.

String toString() 
JVM will always call toString() when we try to print any reference variable. 
reference varaible can be 
a. inbuilt class 
b. user defined class 
eg#1. 
class Object{ 
public String toString(){ 
// returns the reference(address/hashCodeValue) of the object 
} 
} 
public final class String extends Object{ 
@Override 
public String toString(){ 
//returns the data present in the Object 
} 
} 
String name= new String("sachin"); 
System.out.println(name);// jvm internally calls name.toString() 
eg#2. 
class Object{ 
public String toString(){ 
// returns the reference(address/hashCodeValue) of the object 
} 
} 
public class Student extends Object{ 
String name; 
Student(String name){ 
this.name =name; 
} 
public String toString(){ 
// returns the reference(address/hashCodeValue) of the object 
} 
} 
Student student = new Student("sachin"); 
System.out.println(student);//JVM calls student.toString() 
output: hashCode value of Student object 
eg#3. 
class Object{ 
public String toString(){ 
// returns the reference(address/hashCodeValue) of the object 
} 
} 
public class Student extends Object{ 
String name; 
Student(String name){ 
this.name =name; 
} 
@Override 
public String toString(){ 
return this.name; 
} 
} 
Student student = new Student("sachin"); 
System.out.println(student);//JVM calls student.toString() 
output: sachin 
Note: In all wrapper class toString() is overriden to return the content 
Object class method 
=============== 
public class Object{ 
public String toString() { 
//return the reference of the Object 
} 
public boolean equals(Object o){ 
//compares the reference 
} 
} 
public final class String{ 
@Override 
public String toString(){ 
//returns the content of the Object 
} 
@Override 
public boolean equals(Object o){ 
//compares the content of the String 
} 
} 
Note: equals() method is also overriden in all Wrapper class to compare the 
content. 
public final class Integer{ 
@Override 
public String toString(){ 
//returns the content of the Object 
} 
@Override 
public boolean equals(Object o){ 
//compares the content. 
} 
}

Usage of Wrapper class --------------------------- 
utility method(helper methods/static methods) 
1.valueOf() 
2.XXXXValue() 
3.parseXXX() 
4.toString() 
1.valueOf 
1.valueOf() Method: 
Purpose: The valueOf() method is a utility method used for converting a string 
representation of a primitive type to its wrapper class object. 
Example 1: 
String str = "123"; 
Integer intObj = Integer.valueOf(str); // Converts the string "123" to an Integer object 
signature: public static wrapper valueOf(primtive data) 
public static wrapper valueOf(String data) 
It is used to create wrapper object for the given primtive or String type of 
data. 
It is alternative to constructor,but good practise is to use valueOf() only. 
Example 2: 
//constructor usage of Wrapper class to create Wrapper Object 
Integer i1= new Integer(10); 
Integer i2= new Integer("10"); 
//usage of utility methods to create Wrapper Object 
Integer i3= Integer.valueOf(10); 
Integer i4= Integer.valueOf("10"); 
System.out.println(i1); 
System.out.println(i2); 
System.out.println(); 
System.out.println(i3); 
System.out.println(i4); 
output 
10 
10 
10 
10 
Note: valueOf() is also a part of Character class. 
eg#2. 
Integer i1=Integer.valueOf(10); 
Double d1= Double.valueOf(10.5); 
Boolean b1=Boolean.valueOf("Nitin"); 
Character c1=Character.valueOf('a');

System.out.println(b1);//false  Boolean type 
System.out.println(c1);//a  chareter type

2. XXXXValue() Methods: 
Purpose: These methods are used to extract the primitive value from a wrapper object. The 
"XXXX" in the method name corresponds to the primitive data type. 
Example: 
Integer intObj = 42; 
int primitiveInt = intObj.intValue(); // Extracts the int value from the Integer object 
We can use xxxxValue() to convert wrapper to prmitive type. 
Every Number type wrapper class(Byte,Short,Integer,Long,Float,Double)contains the 
following 6 xxxxValue() method to convert the wrapper object to primitive types. 
Number 
Byte 
Short 
Integer 
Long 
Float 
Double 
Character 
Boolean 
Note: 130 is not in the range of byte so jvm will perform operation in the 
following manner 
range = -128 to 127 
result = -128,-127,-126 ---- > last value will be stored. 
eg#2. 
Character c1=new Character('c'); 
char c2= c1.charValue(); 
System.out.println(c2);//c 
Boolean b1=new Boolean("nitin"); 
Boolean b2=b1.booleanValue(); 
System.out.println(b2);//false 
3. parseXXX() Methods: 
Purpose: These methods are used for parsing a string representation of a primitive type 
directly into its corresponding primitive value. 
Usage: 
Example: 
String str = "123"; 
int primitiveInt = Integer.parseInt(str); // Parses the string "123" to an int 
Every wrapper class except Character class Contains parseXXXX() to 
convert String to Corresponding primtive type. 
signature: public static xxxx parseXXX(String data) 
Example:  
 int i1  = Integer.parseInt("10"); 
System.out.println(i1);//10 
boolean b1=Boolean.parseBoolean("TrUE"); 
System.out.println(b1);//true 
short s1=Short.parseShort("Ten"); 
System.out.println(s1);//NumberFormatException 
String strp = "10"; 
int number = Integer.parseInt(strp); 
System.out.println(number); 
Out put: 
10 
4. toString() Method: 
Purpose: The toString() method is overridden in wrapper classes to return a string 
representation of the object. 
We can use toString() to convert wrapper object/primitve data to String. 
signature: public static String toString(XXXX data) 
public static String toString(xxxx data) 
      Example: 
Over view on for all four methods: 
Integer intObj = 42; 
String str = intObj.toString(); // Converts the Integer object to a string "42" 
Integer i=Integer.valueOf("10"); 
System.out.println(i);//10(in String format) 
System.out.println(i.toString());//10(in String format) 
System.out.println(); 
String s1=Integer.toString(10); 
String s2= Boolean.toString(true); 
String s3= Character.toString('a'); 
System.out.println(s1);//10(in string format) 
System.out.println(s2);//true(in string format) 
System.out.println(s3);//a(in string format)

AutoBoxing and AutoUnBoxing(JDK1.5V) 
================================ 
valueOf() -> To convert String/primitive to Wrapper  
Object 
xxxxValue() -> To convert Wrapper to primitive type. 
Integer i = 10; 
| 
|compiler will make the following change 
| 
Integer i = Integer.valueOf(10); 
Automatic conversion of primitive type to wrapper  
type done by the compiler iscalled "AutoBoxing". 
Integer i1= new Integer(10); 
int i2 = i1; 
| 
|Compiler will do the following change 
| 
int i2= i1.intValue(); 
Automatic conversion of wrapper type to primtive  
type done by the compiler is called "AutoUnBoxing". 
Autoboxing and UnBoxing 
=================== 
eg#1. 
class TestApp 
{ 
static Integer I=10;//AutoBoxing(valueOf()) 
public static void main(String[] args) 
{ 
int i=I;//AutoUnBoxing(intValue()) 
System.out.println(i);//10 
} 
} 
eg#2. 
class TestApp 
{ 
static Integer I=0;//AutoBoxing(valueOf()) 
public static void main(String[] args) 
  { 
int i=I;//AutoUnBoxing(intValue()) 
System.out.println(i);//0 
   } 
} 
eg#3. 
class TestApp 
{ 
static Integer I=null;//AutoBoxing(valueOf()) 
public static void main(String[] args) 
{ 
int i=I;//AutoUnBoxing(intValue())//NullPointer 
Exception 
System.out.println(i);// 
} 
} 
a. null 
b. 0 
c. CE 
d. NumberFormatException 
e. NullPointerException 
f. None of the above

package com.WrapperPackages; 
public class WrapperExp2 { 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
 {  
  //constructor usage of Wrapper class to create Wrapper Object 
  Integer i1= new Integer(10); 
  Integer i2= new Integer("10"); 
  //usage of utility methods to create Wrapper Object 
 // ******** Method value of ********* 
  int i3= Integer.valueOf(10); 
  int i4= Integer.valueOf("10"); 
  System.out.println(" i1 ---> : "+i1); 
  System.out.println(" i2 ---> : "+i2); 
  System.out.println("====================="); 
  System.out.println(" i3 ---> : "+i3); 
  System.out.println(" i4 ---> : "+i4); 
  //String to Wrapper  
  String str = "123"; 
  Integer intObj = Integer.valueOf(str);  
     System.out.println(" intObj :"+ intObj); 
  ///******** xxxxvalue(); 
  System.out.println("===================="); 
  Integer i=new Integer(130); 
  System.out.println("Byte   : "+i.byteValue());//-126 
  System.out.println("Short  : "+i.shortValue());//130 
  System.out.println("Int    : "+i.intValue());//130 
  System.out.println("Long   : "+i.longValue());//130 
  System.out.println("Float  : "+i.floatValue());//130.0 
  System.out.println("Double : "+i.doubleValue());//130.0 
  /// for character type Wrapper to premitive 
  System.out.println("-----------------------"); 
  Character c1 = new Character('A'); 
  char c2 = c1.charValue(); 
  System.out.println("c1 : "+c2); 
  System.out.println("---------------"); 
  Boolean b1 = new Boolean("Teja"); 
  boolean b2 = b1.booleanValue(); 
  System.out.println("B1 : "+b2); 
  //// Parsexxxx(); Exp 1 
  String strp = "10"; 
  int number = Integer.parseInt(strp); 
  System.out.println(number); 
  // Parsexxx(); Exp2 
  boolean b = Boolean.parseBoolean("TruE"); 
  System.out.println("boolean : "+b); 
  int ila  = Integer.parseInt("10"); 
  System.out.println("ila : "+ila);//10 
  boolean ble=Boolean.parseBoolean("TrUE"); 
  System.out.println("ble :"+ble);//true 
  try 
  { 
    short s1=Short.parseShort("Ten"); 
    System.out.println("s1 : "+s1);//NumberFormatException 
  }catch(Exception e) 
  { 
        System.out.println("Failed due to cause of  :"+e); 
  } 
         int ro = 24; 
  String rap = Integer.toString(ro); 
  System.out.println("Rap : "+rap); 
   } 
}

Multithreading in Java: 
 Multithreading allows you to execute multiple threads concurrently, enabling better 
utilization of CPU resources and improved application performance.  
 If some task is executing behind the screen (backed end), there is defaultly one 
thread that is executing the task. 
Thread Class: 
 Java provides the Thread class to create and manage threads. You can create a 
thread by extending the Thread class or implementing the Runnable interface. 
Thread() 
Every time 
thread 
willexecute in 
main stack 
Main Stack() i.e 
in console main 
method 
Runtime Stack 
Thread Lifecycle: 
A thread goes through various states such as NEW, RUNNABLE, BLOCKED, WAITING, 
TIMED_WAITING, and TERMINATED. You can manage thread states using methods like 
sleep()
, 
wait()
Over view: 
, 
notify()
, and 
join()
. 
start()
, 
In Java, the code you compile (execute) runs by default; a thread is given that so that it 
will execute. This kind of thread is called as Main thread();. 
Main thread() : The main thread is the initial thread that is created when a Java program 
starts its execution. It's the thread from which the main() method is invoked, and it serves 
as the entry point for the entire program. 
Main Method: 
The main method is the starting point for Java applications. It has the following signature: 
 Like the thread Execusion Starts from 
Thread Priorities: 
Threads are often assigned priorities to influence scheduling decisions. Higher-priority threads are given 
preference over lower-priority threads. In Java, thread priorities range from Thread.MIN_PRIORITY to 
Thread.MAX_PRIORITY, with Thread.NORM_PRIORITY as the default. 
Example: 
Thread.currentThread().getName() 
Thread.currentThread().getName() method in Java. This method is used to retrieve the 
name of the currently executing thread.

{ 
 Public static void main (String args[]) 
{ 
              ///Main thread() execution starts from Here 
} 
} 
public class Main_Thread  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
   { 
       System.out.println("Hey Focus Here"); 
System.out.print("Current thread Status : "); 
Thread t = Thread.currentThread(); 
System.out.print(t); 
   } 
} 
Out put: 
Hey Focus Here 
Current thread Status : Thread[#1,main,5,main] 
package Multi_threading; 
public class Main_Thread  
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  System.out.println("Hey Focus Here"); 
  System.out.print("Current thread Status : "); 
  Thread t = Thread.currentThread(); 
  System.out.println(t); 
  //Changeing the Thread Name 
  System.out.println(); 
  System.out.println("<-------------Changeing the Thread Name------------------>"); 
  t.setName("<----Teja Thread---->"); 
  t.setPriority(7); 
  System.out.println("Current thread Status :"+t); 
  //Gettring the Thread Name 
  System.out.println(); 
  String cstr =t.getName(); // Gettrig the Current details and Storeing in the String 
  System.out.println("Current thread Name : "+cstr); 
 } 
} 
Out put: 
Hey Focus Here 
Current thread Status : Thread[#1,main,5,main] 
<-------------Changeing the Thread Name------------------> 
Current thread Status :Thread[#1,<----Teja Thread---->,7,main] 
Current thread Name : <----Teja Thread----> 
Thread Scheduler in Java 
A component of Java that decides which thread to run or execute and which thread to wait for 
is called a thread scheduler in Java. In Java, a thread is only chosen by a thread scheduler if 
it is in a runnable state. However, if there is more than one thread in the runnable state, it is up 
to the thread scheduler to pick one of the threads and ignore the other ones. There are some 
criteria that determine which thread will execute first. There are two factors for scheduling a 
thread, i.e., priority and time of arrival. 
Priority: The priority of each thread lies between 1 and 10. If a thread has a higher priority, it 
has a better chance of getting picked up by the thread scheduler. 
Time of Arrival: Suppose two threads of the same priority enter the runnable state, then 
priority cannot be the factor to pick a thread from these two threads. In such a case, the arrival 
time of the thread is considered by the thread scheduler. A thread that arrives first gets 
preference over the other threads. 
How to Create Thread in Java and how many ways we can create multiple threads in Java. ? 
In Java, there are two main ways to create threads: by extending the Thread class or by implementing 
the Runnable interface. Both approaches involve defining a run method where the code to be executed 
in the thread is placed. 
1_Extending the Thread class: 
Extending the Thread class in Java involves creating a new class that directly extends the Thread 
class and overrides its run method to define the code that should be executed in the new thread. 
2_Implementing the Runnable interface: 
Implementing the Runnable interface in Java involves creating a class that implements the Runnable 
interface and providing an implementation for the run method. The run method contains the code that 
should be executed when the thread is started. 
Using the Runnable interface is generally preferred over extending the Thread class because it allows 
for better flexibility(because Muliple inheritance not  allowed). Java supports multiple interfaces, so 
a class can implement Runnable while extending another class. 
Example_:1 IN this, all the executions of methos banking, printing, and calculating are 
executed using the same method, i.e., in a single thread (main()). This is an example of single
threaded programming. 
Example_2: In this, all the execution of methos banking, printing, and calculating are executed 
in different classes and different methods and maintained in different threads. This is an 
example of multi-threading programming. 
Over view:   Creating an Objects as Main Thread T 
For Banking T1,Printing T2 and Calculating T3 
package Multi_threading; 
public class Multi_threading1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException { 
  System.out.println("*********Banking Task **********"); 
  for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
  { 
   Thread.sleep(3000); 
   System.out.println("*********Banking Task Started **********"); 
  } 
  System.out.println("*********Banking Complected **********"); 
  System.out.println("-------------------------------------------------"); 
  System.out.println("*********Printing Task **********"); 
  for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
  { 
   Thread.sleep(3000); 
   System.out.println("*********Printing Task Started **********"); 
  } 
  System.out.println("*********Printing Complected **********"); 
  System.out.println("-------------------------------------------------"); 
  System.out.println("*********Calculation Task **********"); 
  for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
  { 
   Thread.sleep(3000); 
   System.out.println("*********Calculation Task Started **********"); 
  } 
  System.out.println("*********Calculation Complected **********"); 
 } 
}

Example_2 : for Extending the Thread Class: 
package Multi_threading; 
class Banking extends Thread 
{ 
        @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
        try 
        { 
   System.out.println("*********Banking Task **********"); 
   for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(3000); 
    System.out.println("*********Banking Task Started **********"); 
   } 
   System.out.println("*********Banking Complected **********"); 
   System.out.println("-------------------------------------------------"); 
    }catch(InterruptedException e) 
        { 
     System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
        } 
 } 
} 
class Printing extends Thread 
{ 
 @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
  try 
        { 
   System.out.println("*********Printing Task **********"); 
   for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(3000); 
    System.out.println("*********Printing Task Started **********"); 
   } 
   System.out.println("*********Printing Complected **********"); 
   System.out.println("-------------------------------------------------"); 
        } 
  catch(InterruptedException e) 
        { 
     System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
        } 
 } 
} 
class Calculation extends Thread 
{ 
 @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
  try 
        { 
   System.out.println("*********Calculation Task **********"); 
   for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(3000); 
    System.out.println("*********Calculation Task Started **********"); 
   } 
   System.out.println("*********Calculation Complected **********"); 
        } 
  catch(InterruptedException e) 
        { 
     System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
        } 
 } 
} 
public class Multi_threading1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException { 
  Thread bank = new Banking(); 
  Thread print = new Printing(); 
  Thread calculation = new Calculation(); 
  bank.start(); 
  print.start(); 
  calculation.start(); 
 } 
}

In this example, Thread Shedular will execute 
the execution of each task (thread), i.e., which 
thread needs to be executed first. 
Thread.Start() : the start() method is a crucial method provided by the Thread class for initiating the execution of a thread. When you call the start() method on a Thread 
object, it does the 
New Thread Creation: 
Allocates the necessary system resources and initializes the new thread. 
Invocation of run Method: 
Calls the run() method on the thread. The run() method contains the code that will be executed in the new thread. 
Concurrency and Execution: 
Initiates the concurrent execution of the thread. The code specified in the run() method runs in a separate thread of control. 
In the above example_2, Thread Shedular will execute the execution of each task (thread), i.e., which thread needs to be executed first. Due to that, the flow is getting 
mismatched, so to overcome that, the join method();, is used for the extraction of each dependent. 
Example 3: Join Method(); 
package Multi_threading; 
class Banking1 extends Thread 
{ @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
        try 
        { 
   System.out.println("*********Banking Task **********"); 
   for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(3000); 
    System.out.println("*********Banking Task Started **********"); 
   } 
   System.out.println("*********Banking Complected **********"); 
   System.out.println("-------------------------------------------------"); 
    }catch(InterruptedException e) 
        { 
     System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
        } 
 } 
} 
class Printing1 extends Thread 
{ @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
  try 
        { 
   System.out.println("*********Printing Task **********"); 
   for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(3000); 
    System.out.println("*********Printing Task Started **********"); 
   } 
   System.out.println("*********Printing Complected **********"); 
   System.out.println("-------------------------------------------------"); 
        } 
  catch(InterruptedException e) 
        { 
     System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
        } 
 } 
} 
class Calculation1 extends Thread 
{ @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
  try 
        { 
   System.out.println("*********Calculation Task **********"); 
   for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(3000); 
    System.out.println("*********Calculation Task Started **********"); 
   } 
   System.out.println("*********Calculation Complected **********"); 
        } 
  catch(InterruptedException e) 
        { 
     System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
        } 
 } 
} 
public class Multi_threading2 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException { 
 Thread bank = new Banking1(); 
 Thread print = new Printing1(); 
 Thread calculation = new Calculation1(); 
 // Using the Join method we can Execute the depends threads in correct way. 
 bank.start(); 
 bank.join(); 
 print.start(); 
 print.join(); 
 calculation.start(); 
 } 
}

Example_4 : for Implementing the Runnable interface: 
package Multi_threading; 
class Banking2 implements Runnable 
{ 
 @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
        try 
        { 
   System.out.println("*********Banking Task **********"); 
   for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(3000); 
    System.out.println("*********Banking Task Started **********"); 
   } 
   System.out.println("*********Banking Complected **********"); 
   System.out.println("-------------------------------------------------"); 
    }catch(InterruptedException e) 
        { 
     System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
        } 
 } 
} 
class Printing2 implements Runnable 
{ 
 @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
  try 
        { 
   System.out.println("*********Printing Task **********"); 
   for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(3000); 
    System.out.println("*********Printing Task Started **********"); 
   } 
   System.out.println("*********Printing Complected **********"); 
   System.out.println("-------------------------------------------------"); 
        } 
  catch(InterruptedException e) 
        { 
     System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
        } 
 } 
} 
class Calculation2 implements Runnable 
{ 
 @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
  try 
        { 
   System.out.println("*********Calculation Task **********"); 
   for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(3000); 
    System.out.println("*********Calculation Task Started **********"); 
   } 
   System.out.println("*********Calculation Complected **********"); 
        } 
  catch(InterruptedException e) 
        { 
     System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
        } 
 } 
} 
public class Multi_threading3 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException { 
  Banking2 bank = new Banking2(); 
  Printing2 print = new Printing2(); 
  Calculation2 calculation = new Calculation2(); 
  // Using the Join method we can Execute the depends threads in correct way. 
  Thread t1 = new Thread(bank); 
  Thread t2 = new Thread(print); 
  Thread t3 = new Thread(calculation); 
  t1.start(); 
  t1.join(); 
  t2.start(); 
  t2.join(); 
  t3.start(); 
 } 
}

Example_5 : By Using Single Run Method Executing Multiple threads. 
package Multi_threading; 
class Alpha extends Thread 
{ 
 @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
  String thread = Thread.currentThread().getName(); 
  if(thread.equals("BANKING")) 
  { 
   banking(); 
  } 
  else if(thread.equals("PRINTING")) 
  { 
   printing(); 
  } 
  else 
  { 
   calculation(); 
  } 
 } 
 public void banking() 
 { 
  try 
        { 
   System.out.println("*********Banking Task **********"); 
   for(int i=0;i<3;i++) 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(3000); 
    System.out.println("*********Banking Task Started **********"); 
   } 
   System.out.println("*********Banking Complected **********"); 
   System.out.println("-------------------------------------------------"); 
    }catch(InterruptedException e) 
        { 
     System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
        } 
 }

public class Multi_threading4 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException { 
  Thread alp1 = new Alpha(); 
  Thread alp2 = new Alpha(); 
  Thread alp3 = new Alpha(); 
  // Setting the thread Name 
  alp1.setName("BANKING"); 
  alp2.setName("PRINTING"); 
  alp3.setName("CALCULATE"); 
  // Starting execution of the thread 
  alp1.start(); 
  alp1.join(); 
  alp2.start(); 
  alp2.join(); 
  alp3.start(); 
 } 
}

public class Multi_threading5 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException { 
  lambda l1 = new lambda(); 
  lambda l2 = new lambda(); 
  lambda l3 = new lambda(); 
  Thread t1 = new Thread(l1); 
  Thread t2 = new Thread(l2); 
  Thread t3 = new Thread(l3); 
  // Setting the thread Name 
  t1.setName("BANKING"); 
  t2.setName("PRINTING"); 
  t3.setName("CALCULATE"); 
  t1.start(); 
  t1.join(); 
  t2.start(); 
  t2.join(); 
  t3.start();  
 } 
}

How to check thread is alive…? 
In Java, you can use the isAlive() method to check whether a thread is alive or not. The isAlive() 
method is a part of the Thread class, and it returns true if the thread upon which it is called is still 
running, and false otherwise. 
Example: 
package Multi_threading; 
class MyThread extends Thread { 
    public void run() { 
        for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) { 
            System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName() + ": " + i); 
            try { 
                Thread.sleep(500); // Sleep for 500 milliseconds 
            } catch (InterruptedException e) { 
                e.printStackTrace(); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
} 
public class Multi_threading6 { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        MyThread myThread = new MyThread(); 
        myThread.start(); 
        // Checking if the thread is alive 
        while (myThread.isAlive()) { 
            try { 
                Thread.sleep(100); // Sleep for 100 milliseconds 
            } catch (InterruptedException e) { 
                e.printStackTrace(); 
            } 
            System.out.println("Main thread: MyThread is still alive."); 
        } 
        System.out.println("Main thread: MyThread has completed its execution."); 
    } 
}
