Synchronized: 
In Java, the synchronized keyword is used to control access to critical sections of code, preventing 
multiple threads from executing them concurrently and potentially causing data corruption or 
inconsistency. It is a mechanism for implementing thread safety and ensuring that shared resources 
are accessed in a controlled manner. 
It's important to use synchronization cautiously to avoid performance issues and deadlocks. While 
synchronization is effective in preventing race conditions, it can also introduce contention, 
impacting the performance of your multithreaded application. Use it only where necessary and 
consider other concurrency mechanisms provided by the java.util.concurrent package for more fine
grained control. 
A code Example before using the Synchronized and After Using the Syncornized:  
1.Before using the Synchornized Key word: 
package Multi_threading; 
class TrailRoom extends Thread 
{ 
 Runnable rn = ()-> 
 { 
  try 
  { 
  System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" Has entered to 
the Trail Room ......."); 
  Thread.sleep(3000); 
  System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" Has Using the 
Trail Room -------"); 
  Thread.sleep(3000); 
  System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" Has Existing the 
Trail Room <<<------>>>"); 
  }catch (InterruptedException e) { 
   System.out.println("Failed due to Casue of "+e.getMessage()); 
  } 
 }; 
 @Override  
 public void run() 
 { 
    rn.run();  
 } 
} 
public class Multi_threading7{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  TrailRoom tr = new TrailRoom(); 
  Thread t1 = new Thread(tr); 
  Thread t2 = new Thread(tr); 
  Thread t3 = new Thread(tr); 
  Thread[] thread = {t1,t2,t3}; 
  t1.setName("Boy"); 
  t2.setName("Girl"); 
  t3.setName("Kid"); 
  for(Thread th : thread) 
  { 
   th.start(); 
  } 
 } 
}

Difference between Join(); --Method and Syncronized key Word 
 Join Method Synchornized Key word 
1. The join method is a method available in the 
Thread class. 
2. It is used to wait for a thread to complete its 
execution before moving forward in the 
program. 
3. When a thread calls join on another thread, it 
waits for that thread to finish before 
continuing its own execution. 
4. It's useful when you want to ensure that 
certain threads complete their work before the 
main thread or another thread continues. 
1. The synchronized keyword is used to control 
access to critical sections of code by allowing 
only one thread at a time to execute that 
section. 
2. It is applied to methods or blocks of code to 
ensure that only one thread can execute the 
synchronized portion at a time. 
3. It helps prevent race conditions and ensures 
data consistency when multiple threads are 
accessing shared resources.

 Runnable  rn = ()-> 
 { 
  try  
  {

   System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName() + " Has entered to the 
Trail Room ......."); 
   Thread.sleep(3000); 
   System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName() + " Has Using the Trail 
Room -------"); 
   Thread.sleep(3000); 
   System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName() + " Has Exiting the Trail 
Room <<<------>>>"); 
   System.out.println(); 
  } catch (InterruptedException e) { 
   System.out.println("Failed due to Casue of " + e.getMessage()); 
  } 
 };

 public synchronized void run() 
 { 
    rn.run();  
 } 
}

Dead Lock In Multithreading: 
A deadlock in multithreading occurs when two or more threads are blocked forever, each waiting for the other to 
release a lock. It's a situation where a set of threads are unable to proceed because each is waiting for the other to 
release a resource. Deadlocks are a common issue in concurrent programming and can lead to the application 
becoming unresponsive. Here are the key conditions that must be met for a deadlock to occur, often referred to as the 
"deadlock conditions": 
package Multi_threading; 
class ITRS implements Runnable 
{ 
 @Override 
 public void run() 
 { 
  try 
  { 
   int arr[] = { 6, 7, 8, 4, 3 }; 
   for (int i = 0; i < arr.length; i++)  
   { 
    for (int j = i; j < arr.length; j++)  
    { 
     if (arr[i] > arr[j]) { 
      int temp = arr[i]; 
      arr[i] = arr[j]; 
      arr[j] = temp; 
     } 
    } 
   } 
   synchronized (this) { 
    for (int i = 0; i < arr.length; i++)  
    { 
     Thread.sleep(500); 
     System.out.print(" " + arr[i]); 
    } 
   } 
    }catch(InterruptedException e) 
  { 
     System.out.println("Failed "+e.getMessage()); 
  } 
 } 
} 
public class Multi_threading8 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  ITRS yu = new ITRS(); 
  Thread t1 = new Thread(yu); 
  Thread t2 = new Thread(yu); 
  Thread t3 = new Thread(yu); 
  Thread[] thread = {t1,t2,t3}; 
  for(Thread thr :thread) 
  { 
   thr.start(); 
  } 
 } 
}

1. Mutual Exclusion: 
o At least one resource must be held in a non-shareable mode, meaning only one thread can use it at a time. 
2. Hold and wait: 
o A thread must be holding at least one resource and waiting to acquire additional resources held by other threads. 
3. No Preemption: 
o Resources cannot be forcibly taken away from a thread; they can only be released voluntarily by the thread holding 
them. 
4. Circular Wait: 
o There must exist a circular chain of two or more threads, each holding a resource that the next thread in the chain is 
waiting for. 
Example Code for Dead Lock: 
package Multi_threading; 
class Immortal implements Runnable 
{ 
 public String Resource1 = new String("Brhmasthra"); 
 public String Resource2 = new String("PashuPatastra"); 
 public String Resource3 = new String("Sarpastra"); 
 @Override 
 public void run() { 
  try 
  { 
    String str = Thread.currentThread().getName(); 
    if(str.equals("RAMA")) 
    { 
     ram_Acquires(); 
    } 
    else 
    { 
    ravan_Acquires(); 
    } 
  }catch(Exception e) 
  { 
   System.out.println(" Failed Due to"+e.getMessage()); 
  } 
 } 
 public void ram_Acquires() 
 { 
    try 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(4000); 
    synchronized(Resource1) 
    { 
     System.out.println("Rama has acquired "+ Resource1); 
     Thread.sleep(4000); 
     synchronized(Resource2) 
     { 
      System.out.println("Rama has aquired "+ Resource2); 
      Thread.sleep(4000); 
      synchronized(Resource3) 
      { 
       System.out.println("Rama has aquired "+ Resource3); 
      } 
     } 
    } 
   } 
   catch(Exception e) 
   { 
    e.printStackTrace(); 
   } 
 } 
 public void ravan_Acquires() 
 { 
   try 
   { 
    Thread.sleep(4000); 
    synchronized(Resource3) 
    { 
     System.out.println("Ravan has acquired "+ Resource3); 
     Thread.sleep(4000); 
     synchronized(Resource2) 
     { 
      System.out.println("Ravan has aquired "+ Resource2); 
      Thread.sleep(4000); 
      synchronized(Resource1) 
      { 
       System.out.println("Ravan has aquired "+ Resource1); 
      } 
     } 
    } 
   } 
   catch(Exception e) 
   { 
    e.printStackTrace(); 
   }  
 } 
}

Thread.Group(): 
In Java, a ThreadGroup is a way to group multiple threads together. It provides a convenient 
mechanism for managing and controlling a set of threads as a single unit. Thread groups are 
instances of the ThreadGroup class, and they have several purposes: 
1. Organizing Threads: 
o Thread groups provide a way to organize and categorize threads. 
o Threads can be added to a thread group when they are created, or they can be moved into a 
thread group later. 
2. Controlling Threads: 
o Thread groups allow you to perform operations on all threads within the group 
simultaneously. 
o For example, you can interrupt all threads in a group or set the priority of all threads in a 
group. 
3. Defining Exception Handling: 
o Thread groups can have an uncaught exception handler, which is called when any thread in 
the group terminates due to an uncaught exception. 
4. Active Count: 
o You can obtain the number of active threads in a thread group, which can be useful for 
monitoring and management. 
Example: 
Demon Thread: In Java, a demon thread is a type of thread that runs in the background and does not prevent the 
Java Virtual Machine (JVM) from exiting when all non-demon threads have completed. In other words, demon 
threads are considered "service" threads that are not essential for the application to keep running. 
Here are some key characteristics of demon threads: 
1. Background Execution: 
o Demon threads execute in the background, performing tasks such as garbage collection, housekeeping, or 
other maintenance activities. 
2. Termination Behavior: 
o If all non-demon threads finish their execution, the JVM terminates, regardless of whether there are demon 
threads still running. 
o If there are only demon threads left, the JVM considers its work as done and terminates. 
3. Created using setDaemon: 
o You can set a thread as a demon thread by calling the setDaemon(true) method before starting the 
thread. 
o By default, threads are non-demon threads. 
Note : We should not make a demo thread the main thread. And if we allocate any thread as a demon thread behind 
the seen JVM, it doesn’t give priority to that thread.  
package Multi_threading; 
public class Multi_threading10 { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        ThreadGroup group = new ThreadGroup("MyThreadGroup"); 
        Thread thread1 = new Thread(group, () -> { 
            for(int i=0;i<3;i++) { 
                System.out.println("Thread 1 is running"); 
                try { 
                    Thread.sleep(1000); 
                } catch (InterruptedException e) { 
                    e.printStackTrace(); 
                } 
            } 
        }); 
        Thread thread2 = new Thread(group, () -> { 
           for(int i=0;i<3;i++) { 
                System.out.println("Thread 2 is running"); 
                try { 
                    Thread.sleep(1000); 
                } catch (InterruptedException e) { 
                    e.printStackTrace(); 
                } 
            } 
        }); 
        thread1.start(); 
        thread2.start(); 
        group.list(); 
    } 
}

public class Demon_threading { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  // TODO Auto-generated method stub 
  Thread t=Thread.currentThread(); 
  System.out.println(t.isDaemon()); 
  //t.setDaemon(true); 
  //System.out.println(t.isDaemon()); 
  Ineuron i=new Ineuron(); 
  Thread t1=new Thread(i); 
  System.out.println(t1.isDaemon()); 
  t1.start(); 
  try 
  { 
    t1.setDaemon(true);  
    System.out.println(t1.isDaemon()); 
  }catch(Exception e) 
  { 
   System.out.println(e+" Occured Due to "+e.getMessage()); 
  } 
 } 
}

InterThread Communication -------------------------------------- 
Two threads should interact with each other, how? 
eg: Producer Consumer Problem 
ProducerEnd 
=> Producer duty is to produce the data and once the data is produced update 
the variable 
called "DataProvider" to true 
=> This action should be done by "Producer Thread"

Producer – Produces the Data Consumer --- consumes the data 
package Multi_threading; 
//producer thread operations 
class Producer extends Thread 
{  //Producer producing the Data in StringBuffer 
 StringBuffer sb; 
 // variable used by thread for Communication 
 boolean dataprovider = false; 
 public Producer() { 
  // StringBuffer object is created with a default capacity 16 
  sb = new StringBuffer(); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public void run() { 
  for(int i=0;i<10;i++) 
  { 
   try 
   { 
    sb.append(i+" : "); 
    Thread.sleep(100); 
    System.out.println("appending"); 
   }catch(InterruptedException e) 
   { 
    System.out.println("Failed :"+e.getMessage()); 
   } 
  } 
  // informing the consumer that data is produced 
  dataprovider = true; 
 } 
} 
//Consumer thread operations 
class Consumer extends Thread 
{ 
    //Creating the producer object to get the producer from the StringBuffer 
 Producer producer; 
  // Injecting the Producer object in to consumer 
 public Consumer(Producer producer) { 
  this.producer = producer; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public void run() { 
  while(producer.dataprovider == false) 
  { 
   try { 
    Thread.sleep(10); 
   } catch (InterruptedException e) { 
    System.out.println("Failed :"+e.getMessage()); 
   } 
  } 
  //consume the data produced by the producer 
  System.out.println(producer.sb); 
 } 
} 
public class Thread_communication { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Producer obj = new Producer(); 
  Consumer obj1= new Consumer(obj); 
  Thread t1 = new Thread(obj);//producer thread 
  Thread t2 = new Thread(obj1);//consumer thread 
  t2.start();//consumer should wait 
  t1.start();//producer should start 
 } 
}

1.In the above code when the interaction happens b/w 2 threads, always the consumer thread is ready for consumption,but the 
consumer thread will get the data only when the dataProvider value is set to true. 
2.This increases the waiting time of a thread and makes the cpu time idle,through which communication b/w 
2 threads wont be efficient. 
3.To reduce the effieciency problem we use the methods given by Object class 
a.wait() 
b.notify() 
c.notifyAll() 
Note: 
wait(),notify(),notifyAll() methods are present in Object class not in Threadclass. 
If any thread has to call wait(),notify(),notifyAll() then that thread should be the owner of the thread.We say the thread as 
owner iff the thread has the lock of the object. 
If the thread calls notify(),notifyAll() and wait() and the thread is not a owner then it would result in 
RE: "IllegalMonitorStateException". 
wait() -> Whichever thread is excpecting the updated result from the object thatthread should call wait method.Whenever 
wait() is called automatically that thread will release the lock of the Object to the other thread to use that lock. 
notify() -> Which ever thread wants to update the Object, that thread should 
call notify() to the Other thread(one). 
notifyAll() ->Which ever thread wants to update the Object, that thread should call 
notifyAll() to the Other 
waiting threads(many) 
Wait():The wait() method is a part of the Object class in Java and is used for interthread communication. It is typically used 
within synchronized blocks to make a thread wait until another thread signals that a certain condition has been met. 
Usage: 
The wait() method is called on an object. 
It must be called from within a synchronized block to avoid IllegalMonitorStateException. 
It releases the lock held by the current thread, allowing other threads to acquire the lock. 
Waiting for Notification: 
When a thread calls wait(), it enters a "waiting" state until another thread calls notify() or notifyAll() on the same object. 
Interrupted Exception: 
The wait() method can throw an InterruptedException if the thread is interrupted while waiting. 
Timeout Variant: 
There is an overloaded version of wait(long timeout) that allows the thread to wait for a specified amount of time. If the 
specified time elapses or the thread is interrupted, it will resume execution. 
Important Questions: 
Why wait(),notify(),notifyAll() methods are part of Object class, why not Thread class? 
ans. These methods will be used by the thread on different types of Objects like StringBuffer,Student,Customer,Account,For 
every object the parent class is Object,so these methods comes from 
object class. 
=>methods like join,yield,sleep will be applied only on Threads, so only 
these methods are part of Thread class not Object class. 
What is the difference b/w notify() and notifyAll()? 
notify() -> It will give notification only to one thread which needs the lock 
of that object 
notifyAll() -> It will give notification to mulitple threads which needs the 
lock of that object. 
Summary: 
Interthread communication is a mechanism in Java that allows threads to communicate with each 
other, synchronize their actions, and coordinate their execution. This is crucial in scenarios where 
multiple threads are working concurrently and need to share information or coordinate their 
activities. The primary methods for interthread communication in Java are: 
wait(), notify(), and notifyAll(): 
These methods are part of the Object class and are used for low-level interthread communication. 
wait(): Causes the current thread to wait until another thread invokes the notify() or notifyAll() 
methods for this object. 
notify(): Wakes up one of the threads that are currently waiting in the wait() method,for single 
thread. 
notifyAll(): Wakes up all the threads that are currently waiting in the wait() method,for multiple 
threads.

package Multi_threading; 
//producer thread operations 
class Producer extends Thread 
{ 
 //Producer producing the Data in StringBuffer 
 StringBuffer sb; 
 // variable used by thread for Communication 
 boolean dataprovider = false; 
 public Producer() { 
  // StringBuffer object is created with a default capacity 16 
  sb = new StringBuffer(); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public void run() { 
  synchronized (sb) { 
   for(int i=0;i<10;i++) 
   { 
    try 
    { 
     sb.append(i+" : "); 
     Thread.sleep(100); 
     System.out.println("appending"); 
    }catch(InterruptedException e) 
    { 
     System.out.println("Failed :"+e.getMessage()); 
    } 
   } 
   // send the notification to the waiting thread 
   sb.notify(); 
  } 
 } 
} 
//Consumer thread operations 
class Consumer extends Thread 
{ 
  //Creating the producer object to get the producer from the StringBuffer 
 Producer producer; 
 /** 
  * Injecting the Producer object in to consumer 
  */ 
 public Consumer(Producer producer) { 
  this.producer = producer; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public void run() { 
  synchronized (producer.sb) { 
   try 
   {   //wait till the notification is sent by producer 
    producer.sb.wait(); 
    // consume the data produced by the producer 
    System.out.println(producer.sb); 
   }catch(InterruptedException e) 
   { 
    System.out.println("Failed "+e.getMessage()); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
} 
//Effecient way of interthread communication  using wait() and notify() 
public class Thread_comminication1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Producer obj = new Producer(); 
  Consumer obj1= new Consumer(obj); 
  Thread t1 = new Thread(obj);//producer thread 
  Thread t2 = new Thread(obj1);//consumer thread 
  t2.start();//consumer should wait 
  t1.start();//producer should start 
 } 
}

Var args[]: 
Varargs, short for variable-length argument lists, is a feature introduced in Java 5 that allows a 
method to accept a variable number of arguments. This feature simplifies the syntax for methods 
that need to handle a variable number of parameters. Varargs is denoted by an ellipsis (...) followed 
by the argument type. 
package Multi_threading; 
public class Lambda_threading extends Thread{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  ////This is For Annomous inner Class 
   Thread ths = new Thread(new Runnable() { 
   @Override 
    public void run() { 
     for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) { 
      try { 
       System.out.println("child Thread"); 
       Thread.sleep(1000); 
      } catch (InterruptedException e) { 
       // TODO Auto-generated catch block 
       e.printStackTrace(); 
      } 
     } 
    } 
   }); 
   ths.start(); 
  ////This is For Lambda Expression 
  Thread th = new Thread(()-> { 
   for(int i=0;i<5;i++) 
   { 
    try{ 
      System.out.println("child Thread"); 
     Thread.sleep(1000); 
    } catch (InterruptedException e) { 
     // TODO Auto-generated catch block 
     e.printStackTrace(); 
    } 
   } 
  }); 
   th.start(); 
   for(int i=0;i<5;i++) 
   { 
    try{ 
     System.out.println("Main Thread"); 
    Thread.sleep(1000); 
   } catch (InterruptedException e) { 
    // TODO Auto-generated catch block 
    e.printStackTrace(); 
   } 
   } 
 } 
}

Declaration: 
Varargs are declared by specifying three dots (...) after the argument type in the method parameter 
list. 
The varargs parameter must be the last parameter in the parameter list. 
Example 2: 
Advatage : We can pass different size of parameters; 
In the printValues method, String... values allows you to pass a variable number of String 
arguments. This is a convenient feature for methods that need to handle a flexible number of 
parameters. 
package Var_args; 
public class varArgs { 
    public void printValues(String... values) { 
        for (String value : values) { 
            System.out.println(value); 
        } 
    } 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        varArgs obj = new varArgs(); 
        obj.printValues("One", "Two", "Three"); 
        obj.printValues("Hello", "World"); 
        obj.printValues(); // No arguments 
    } 
} 
Out put: 
One 
Two 
Three 
Hello 
World 
package Var_args; 
package Var_args; 
class calculation 
{ 
 public int add(int...nums) 
 {  
  int sum=0; 
  for(int i : nums) 
  { 
   sum = sum + i; 
  } 
    return sum; 
 } 
} 
public class Var_args2 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  calculation calc = new calculation(); 
  int res =calc.add(1,2,3,4,5); 
  int tras = calc.add(1,2,3); 
  System.out.println("Final Result:"); 
  System.out.println(res); 
  System.out.println(tras); 
 } 
}

Q> 
when we have sb.notify() how will will waiting thread know from which point of code 
to start? 
sb.notify() and sb.wait() both are under synchronized and they share the 
common communication channel. 
sb.wait() -> release the lock and enter into waiting state 
| 
sb.notify() -> use the lock update the object and send the notification 
to sb.wait() 
can you please tell the difference between join and yield? 
join() -> stop ur execution and wait for another thread to execute later join 
yield() -> pause ur execution for sometime and check whether there are any 
threads of same priority available or 
not, if not continue ur execution, if available give the other 
thread a chance. 
so how we are assuming consumer will take the lock , it is like lock will not be 
given to producer and given to 
consumer first? 
Producer ->produce the item and sent the notification to the consumer[notify()] 
Consumer -> consume the item if avaialble otherwise wait as long as the 
producer produces the item 
and gets the notification.[wait] 
consumer.start();//no enter into waiting state by releasing the lock 
producer.start()// get the lock and update the data and finally relase the 
lock.

Collections: 
Java Collections provide a framework of classes and interfaces in the Java programming language to represent and manipulate 
groups of objects. These collections are part of the java.util package and provide a wide range of functionality for working with 
groups of objects, such as lists, sets, maps, and queue 
Here are some key interfaces and classes in the Java Collections framework: 
Interfaces: 
1. Collection: 
o The root interface for all collection classes. It defines basic operations like add, remove, contains, etc. 
2. List: 
o Extends Collection and represents an ordered collection. Common implementations include ArrayList and 
LinkedList. 
3. Set: 
o Extends Collection and represents an unordered collection that does not allow duplicate elements. Common 
implementations include HashSet and TreeSet. 
4. Map: 
o Represents a collection of key-value pairs. Common implementations include HashMap and TreeMap. 
5. Queue: 
o Extends Collection and represents a collection designed for holding elements before processing. Common 
implementations include LinkedList and PriorityQueue. 
.Developers can choose the appropriate collection type based on their specific requirements and performance 
considerations. 
Classes: 
1. ArrayList: 
o Implements the List interface and provides a dynamic array to store elements. 
2. LinkedList: 
o Implements the List interface and provides a doubly-linked list implementation. 
3. HashSet: 
o Implements the Set interface and uses a hash table to store elements. It does not allow duplicate elements. 
4. TreeSet: 
o Implements the Set interface and stores elements in a sorted tree structure. It does not allow duplicate 
elements. 
5. HashMap: 
o Implements the Map interface and uses a hash table to store key-value pairs. It does not allow duplicate 
keys. 
6. TreeMap: 
o Implements the Map interface and stores key-value pairs in a sorted tree structure. It does not allow 
duplicate keys. 
7. PriorityQueue: 
o Implements the Queue interface and stores elements based on their natural order or a specified 
comparator. 
Utility Classes: 
1. Collections: 
o Provides static methods for operations on collections, such as sorting, shuffling, and finding the 
minimum/maximum element. 
2. Arrays: 
o Provides static methods for working with arrays, such as sorting and searching. 
These classes and interfaces make it easier to work with collections of objects in Java, providing a high level of 
abstraction and flexibility 
=================================================================================== 
Array list: Certainly! ArrayList is a part of the Java Collections Framework and is implemented in the 
java.util package. It provides dynamic arrays in Java, which can grow or shrink as needed. Here are 
some key points about ArrayList: 
1. Dynamic Resizing: 
o ArrayList internally uses an array to store elements. When the number of elements exceeds 
the capacity of the array, it automatically increases its size to accommodate more elements. 
2. Type-Safe: 
o ArrayList is a generic class, which means you can specify the type of elements it will store. 
This helps with type safety and avoids runtime type errors. 
3. Ordered Collection: 
o ArrayList maintains the order of elements in which they are inserted. You can access 
elements by their index, and the order is preserved when iterating through the list. 
4. Random Access: 
o ArrayList provides constant-time access to elements using their index. This makes it 
efficient for scenarios where random access is important. 
5. Methods for Modification: 
o add(E element): Appends the specified element to the end of the list. 
o add(int index, E element): Inserts the specified element at the specified position. 
o remove(int index): Removes the element at the specified position. 
o set(int index, E element): Replaces the element at the specified position with the specified element. 
6. Search and Retrieval: 
o get(int index): Returns the element at the specified position. 
o indexOf(Object o): Returns the index of the first occurrence of the specified element. 
o isEmpty(): Returns true if the list is empty. 
o contains (Object o): Returns true if the list contains the specified element. 
7. Size and capacity: 
o size(): Returns the number of elements in the list. 
o ensureCapacity(int minCapacity): Increases the capacity of the ArrayList to ensure that it can hold at 
least the specified number of elements. 
8. Iteration: 
o iterator(): Returns an iterator over the elements in the list. 
o forEach(Consumer<? super E> action): Performs the given action for each element of the ArrayList.                         
9.Search and comparison: 
o contains (Object o): Returns true if the list contains the specified element. 
o indexOf(Object o): Returns the index of the first occurrence of the specified element in the list. 
o lastIndexOf(Object o): Returns the index of the last occurrence of the specified element in the list. 
o equals (Object o): compares the specified object with the ArrayList for equality. 
10.Bulk Operations: 
o addAll(Collection<? extends E> c): Appends all of the elements in the specified collection to the end 
of the list. 
o removeAll(Collection<?> c): Removes all of the elements in the specified collection from the list. 
o retainAll(Collection<?> c): Retains only the elements in the list that are contained in the specified 
collection. 
11.Conversion: 
o toArray(): Returns an array containing all of the elements in the list. 
o toArray(T[] a): Returns an array containing all of the elements in the list; the runtime type of the 
returned array is that of the specified array. 
Note: In the case of an array list, we can add both homogenous data (the same data type) and hytriogenousdata 
(different data types). 
Index base adding example al3.add(2,15); It is allowed but not recommended.the consept of link list comes in 
to picture. 
Code Example: 
Disadvantages of an array list: 
1. Dynamic Resizing Overhead: 
o When an ArrayList needs to grow beyond its current capacity, it creates a new array and copies all elements 
from the old array to the new one. This process incurs overhead and can be inefficient for large lists. 
package Array_List; 
import java.util.*; 
public class Array_list { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  //Creating the Array list with name list and Storeing the hytriogenous data 
  ArrayList list = new ArrayList(); 
  list.add(55); 
  list.add("Teja"); 
  list.add('A'); 
  list.add(5.10); 
  list.add(true); 
  list.add("$$$"); 
  System.out.println(list); 
  System.out.println("-------------------------------------"); 
  //removeing the last element $$$ 
  list.remove(5); 
  //Adding one element 
  list.add(5, "Naruto"); 
  System.out.println(list); 
  //Creating the Array list with name list and Storeing the homogenous data  
  ArrayList<Integer> list2 = new ArrayList<Integer>(); 
  for(int i=1;i<=5;i++) 
  { 
   list2.add(i); 
  } 
  // adding dublicate element 
  list2.add(5); 
  System.out.println("----------List2-------------"); 
  System.out.println(list2); 
  System.out.println("-------------------------------------------------"); 
  //meriging the Array list list with list2 
  list2.addAll(list); 
  System.out.println(list2);  
  //checking list 2 is empty or not 
  System.out.println(list2.isEmpty()); 
  System.out.println(); 
  ArrayList al3 = new ArrayList<>(); 
  al3.ensureCapacity(4); 
  al3.add("Bengaluru"); 
  al3.add("India"); 
  al3.add(15); 
  al3.add(20.5); 
      al3.add(1, 50); 
      System.out.println(al3.size()); 
  System.out.println(al3); 
 } 
}

[1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 5, 55, Teja, A, 5.1, true, Naruto]

2. Memory Overhead: 
o ArrayList uses an array internally, which can result in memory waste. The array needs to be 
allocated with a certain initial capacity, and if that capacity is not utilized, it leads to inefficient 
memory usage. 
3. Slower than Arrays for Random Access: 
o While ArrayList provides constant-time access for retrieving elements by index, it can be slower 
than arrays for this operation due to the need for bounds checking and the indirect reference through 
the array. 
4. Not Thread-Safe: 
o ArrayList is not thread-safe. If multiple threads modify an ArrayList concurrently without proper 
synchronization, it can lead to unpredictable behavior. If thread safety is required, alternatives like 
Vector or using Collections.synchronizedList() can be considered. 
5. No Support for Primitive Types: 
o ArrayList can only store objects, not primitive types. If you need to work with primitive types, you 
have to use their corresponding wrapper classes, like Integer for int, which adds some overhead. 
6. Limited Performance for Insertions and Deletions: 
o Inserting or deleting elements in the middle of an ArrayList requires shifting elements, which can be 
inefficient for large lists. If frequent insertions or deletions are anticipated, a LinkedList might be a 
more suitable choice. 
7. Fixed Capacity Arrays: 
o While ArrayList can dynamically resize, it starts with a fixed capacity, and if the initial capacity is 
not well-chosen, it might lead to frequent resizing, impacting performance. 
8. Lack of compact storage: 
o Unlike arrays, ArrayList does not store elements in a contiguous memory block. This non
contiguous storage may result in less cache-friendly behavior, affecting performance in certain 
scenarios.  
When should I use an array over an array list? 
1. Fixed Size:  
o The size is known and fixed.i.e when ever size we know we can prefier over array list. 
o Required when data is homgenious data.  
2. Memory Efficiency:  
o Memory efficiency is crucial. 
3. Random Access:  
o Frequent random access by index is a priority. 
4. Primitive Types:  
o Dealing with primitive data types directly. 
=================================================================================== 
Linked List: 
LinkedList in Java is suitable for scenarios where dynamic size and efficient insertions and deletions 
are critical, but it may not be the best choice for situations requiring frequent random access or when 
memory efficiency is a top concern. The appropriate choice depends on the specific requirements of 
the application. 
Singly Linked list in Java: 
A singly Linked List in Java is a collection of nodes that are connected in a chained sequence. Where each node has the following – 
 Data Value 
 Next Reference – Reference to the next node in the sequence 
Unlike Arrays with are contiguously stored, Linked List is not contiguous and are scattered all over the memory but connected with one 
another using the next references.Also, array size can not be dynamically increased however, in Linked List the size can be increased and 
decreased at any time dynamically. 
Code Example: 
package Linked_list; 
class Node 
{ 
 // intilizaing the data 
 int data; 
 Node next; 
 //creating the data with constructor 
 public Node(int data) { 
  this.data = data; 
  this.next = null; 
 } 
} 
class Single_Linked_list 
{ 
  Node head; // Points to the first node in the list 
     // Constructor 
     public Single_Linked_list() { 
         this.head = null; 
     } 
     // Method to insert a new node at the end of the list 
  public void append(int data)  
  { 
   Node newNode = new Node(data); 
   if (head == null) { 
    head = newNode; 
    return; 
   }  
   else  
   { 
    Node last = head; 
    while (last.next != null)  
    { 
     last = last.next; 
    } 
    last.next = newNode; 
   } 
  } 
  // Method to display the elements of the list 
  public void display() { 
   Node current = head; 
   while (current != null) { 
    System.out.print(current.data + " "); 
    current = current.next; 
   } 
   System.out.println(); 
  } 
} 
public class Linked_list1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Single_Linked_list linkedList = new Single_Linked_list(); 
        // Appending elements to the linked list 
        linkedList.append(1); 
        linkedList.append(2); 
        linkedList.append(3); 
        // Displaying the elements of the linked list 
        System.out.print("Linked List: "); 
        linkedList.display(); 
    } 
} 
Out put: 
Linked List: 1 2 3  
 Doubly linked List: 
A doubly linked list is a type of linked list where each node contains a data element and two pointers 
or references, one pointing to the next node in the sequence (similar to a singly linked list) and 
another pointing to the previous node in the sequence. This allows for traversal in both directions. 
1.The Node class now has a prev pointer in addition to the next pointer. 
2.TheDoublyLinkedList class has methods for appending elements and displaying the list in both 
forward and backward directions. 
3. This allows you to traverse the doubly linked list in both directions, making it useful in scenarios 
where bidirectional traversal is needed. 
Code Example: 
package Linked_list; 
class Nodes { 
    int data; 
    Nodes next; 
    Nodes prev; 
    public Nodes(int data) { 
        this.data = data; 
        this.next = null; 
        this.prev = null; 
    } 
} 
class DoublyLinkedList { 
    Nodes head; 
    public DoublyLinkedList() { 
        this.head = null; 
    } 
    public void append(int data) { 
        Nodes newNode = new Nodes(data); 
        if (head == null) { 
            head = newNode; 
        } else { 
            Nodes last = head; 
            while (last.next != null) { 
                last = last.next; 
            } 
            last.next = newNode; 
            newNode.prev = last; 
        } 
    } 
    public void displayForward() { 
        Nodes current = head; 
        System.out.print("Forward: "); 
        while (current != null) { 
            System.out.print(current.data + " "); 
            current = current.next; 
        } 
        System.out.println(); 
    } 
    public void displayBackward() { 
        Nodes last = head; 
        while (last.next != null) { 
            last = last.next; 
        } 
        System.out.print("Backward: "); 
        while (last != null) { 
            System.out.print(last.data + " "); 
            last = last.prev; 
        } 
        System.out.println(); 
    } 
} 
public class Doubly_linked_list { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        DoublyLinkedList doublyLinkedList = new DoublyLinkedList(); 
        doublyLinkedList.append(1); 
        doublyLinkedList.append(2); 
        doublyLinkedList.append(3); 
        doublyLinkedList.displayForward(); 
        doublyLinkedList.displayBackward(); 
    } 
} 
Out put: 
Forward: 1 2 3  
Backward: 3 2 1  
Important points on linked list 
 A linked list in Java follows a doubly linked-list data structure. 
 It can also store homogeneous and heterogeneous data. 
 Here, we can add one collection to another. 
 Disbursed memory allocation 
 The order of insertation is maintained. 
 Index-based access is allowed. 
 Positioning of element in between the element –is also Recommended 
 We can add directly elements at front end and rare end as well. 
 Fast deletion and dublicate elements are permitted. 
 No demand of contigious memory allocation. 
 Both the add and offer methods add elements to a queue. 
 add throws an exception if it fails, while offer returns false on failure. 
 Use add when you want exceptions for failure handling. 
 Use offer when you prefer a boolean result for failure indication.

Array deque: 
ArrayDeque in Java is a resizable, array-based double-ended queue implementation provided in the 
java.util package. It is a part of the Java Collections Framework and implements the Deque 
interface. 
Here are some key points about ArrayDeque: 
1. Double-Ended Queue: 
ArrayDeque allows elements to be added or removed from both ends (front and rear) of the      
queue. 
2. Resizable Array:Internally, it uses a dynamically resizable array to store elements. 
3. No Capacity Restrictions:Unlike arrays, ArrayDeque does not have a fixed size. It can 
dynamically grow or shrink as needed. 
4. Not Thread-Safe:ArrayDeque is not synchronized, so if multiple threads access a ArrayDeque 
concurrently, it must be synchronized externally. 
5. Null Elements:ArrayDeque allows null elements. 
Important points: 
 It is implementing Queue  Interface  
 We can add elements (data) both front end and rare end 
 Index based accessing is not allowed. 
 Dublicates are allowed. 
package ArrayDeque; 
import java.util.*; 
public class Array_deque1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  ArrayDeque arraydeq = new ArrayDeque(); 
  arraydeq.add(10); 
  arraydeq.add(20); 
  arraydeq.add("iNeuron"); 
  arraydeq.add("Bengaluru"); 
  System.out.println(arraydeq); 
  arraydeq.addFirst(100); 
  arraydeq.addLast(200); 
  arraydeq.add(10); 
  System.out.println(arraydeq); 
 } 
}

functionality of a regular queue. In a priority queue, elements are assigned priorities, and the element 
with the highest priority is served before others. Priority queues are often implemented using heaps, 
such as heaps i.e (Min – heap Datastructure). 
The Swaping will Happen in Parent Level , sibling level  it wont happen.dublicates are allowed.

TreeSet: 
TreeSet is a class in Java that implements the SortedSet interface and extends AbstractSet. It is part of the Java 
Collections Framework and represents a set sorted in ascending order. Elements in a TreeSet are ordered based on 
their natural ordering or a specified comparator.Internally it follows Binary Search Tree Algoritham. 
Here are some key characteristics of TreeSet: 
1. Sorted Order: 
o Elements are stored in sorted order (ascending by default). 
2. No Duplicate Elements: 
o TreeSet does not allow duplicate elements. If you attempt to add a duplicate, it will not be added, and 
the existing value will remain. 
3. Red-Black Tree Implementation: 
o Internally, TreeSet uses a red-black tree, which is a self-balancing binary search tree. 
4. Efficient for Range Operations: 
o TreeSet provides efficient operations for finding the smallest and largest elements, as well as 
subsetting based on a range. 
5. Not Thread-Safe: 
o Like many other collection classes in Java, TreeSet is not synchronized. If multiple threads access a 
TreeSet concurrently, it should be synchronized externally. 
 Back – end Over view

Marker Interface 
An interface which does not contain any abstract methods that interface is 
called "Marker Interface". 
If an class implements Marker interface, then that class "object" will get 
additional funcitionality at the runtime by the 
JVM. 
eg: RandomAccess(searching is fast in the Collection object), 
Serializable(makes the object transportable),......

package TreeSet; 
import java.util.TreeSet; 
public class Tree_set1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  TreeSet ts=new TreeSet(); 
  ts.add(100); 
  ts.add(50); 
  ts.add(150); 
  ts.add(25); 
  ts.add(75); 
  ts.add(125); 
  ts.add(175); 
  ts.add(25); 
  System.out.println(ts); 
  TreeSet ts1 = new TreeSet(); 
  ts1.add(35); 
  ts1.add(40); 
  ts1.add(42); 
  ts1.add(20); 
  ts1.add(15); 
  ts1.add(75); 
  System.out.println("<------TreeSet 1-------->"); 
  System.out.println(ts1.higher(20)); 
  System.out.println(ts1.ceiling(20)); 
  System.out.println("----Least vaues-----"); 
  System.out.println(ts1.floor(18)); 
  System.out.println(ts1.lower(20)); 
 } 
} 
higher() method: The higher() method in a TreeSet is used to retrieve the least element in this set 
strictly greater than the given element, or null if there is no such element. In other words, it returns 
the smallest element that is greater than the specified element. 
ceiling() method: The ceiling() method is a method in the TreeSet class in Java, and it is used to 
return the least element in the set that is greater than or equal to the given element, or null if there is 
no such element. 
floor() method: The floor() method in the TreeSet class is used to return the greatest element in the 
set that is less than or equal to the given element, or null if there is no such element. 
lower() method:The lower() method in the TreeSet class is used to return the greatest element in 
the set that is strictly less than the given element, or null if there is no such element.

HashSet: In Java, HashSet is a class that implements the Set interface, and it is part of the Java Collections Framework. It 
represents a collection of unique elements, and it does not allow duplicate elements. HashSet uses a hash table for storage and 
provides constant-time performance for basic operations like add, remove, contain, and size. 
Here are some key characteristics of HashSet: 
1.No Duplicate Elements: 
HashSet does not allow duplicate elements. If you try to add an element that is already present, the operation will have no effect. 
And Searching ablitity is fast in Hashset 
2.Unordered Collection: 
The order of elements in a hash set is not guaranteed. It does not maintain the order in which elements are inserted. 
3.Null Elements: 
HashSet allows a single null element. 
4.Backed by HashMap: 
Internally, a HashSet is backed by a HashMap, where the elements are stored as keys and the values are constant dummy values. 
5.Not Thread-Safe: 
HashSet is not synchronized. If multiple threads access a HashSet concurrently, it must be synchronized externally. 
LinkedHashSet: 
LinkedHashSet is a class in Java that extends HashSet and implements the Set interface. It is part of the Java Collections Framework. 
Like HashSet, it stores elements in a hash table, ensuring uniqueness. However, LinkedHashSet maintains the order of elements based 
on their insertion order.   Here are some key characteristics of LinkedHashSet: 
Order Maintained: 
LinkedHashSet maintains the order of elements based on their insertion order. This order is predictable and consistent. 
Null Elements: 
LinkedHashSet allows a single null element. 
Backed by LinkedHashMap: 
Internally, a LinkedHashSet is backed by a LinkedHashMap, where the elements are stored as keys and the values are constant dummy 
values. 
Not Thread-Safe: 
LinkedHashSet is not synchronized. If multiple threads access a LinkedHashSet concurrently, it must be synchronized externally. 
package Hashset; 
import java.util.*; 
public class Hash_set1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  HashSet hs = new HashSet(); 
  hs.add(23); 
  hs.add(33); 
  hs.add(13); 
  hs.add(53); 
  hs.add(43); 
  hs.add(63); 
  if(hs.contains(33)) 
  { 
   System.out.println("In Hashset 33 is present"); 
  } 
  if(!hs.contains(24)) 
  { 
   System.out.println("In Hashset 24 is not present"); 
  } 
 } 
}

Iterator: 
In Java, an iterator is an interface provided by the java.util package that allows iterating over the elements of a collection, such as 
a list, set, or map. The iterator provides methods to sequentially access the elements in the collection. 
The main methods in the iterator interface are: 
boolean hasNext(): 
Returns true if the iteration has more elements. 
E next(): 
Returns the next element in the iteration. 
void remove(): 
Removes the last element returned by the iterator. This method is optional and may not be supported by all iterators. 
ListIterator 
A ListIterator in Java is an interface provided by the java.util package that extends the basic functionality of the Iterator interface. 
It is specifically designed for iterating over elements in a list bidirectionally. In addition to the methods provided by the Iterator 
interface, ListIterator adds methods to navigate the list in both forward and backward directions, as well as to modify the list 
during iteration. 
Key methods in the ListIterator interface include: 
boolean hasNext(): 
Returns true if there are more elements when traversing in the forward direction. 
E next(): 
Returns the next element in the list when traversing in the forward direction. 
boolean hasPrevious(): 
Returns true if there are more elements when traversing in the reverse direction. 
E previous(): 
Returns the previous element in the list when traversing in the reverse direction. 
int nextIndex(): 
Returns the index of the next element to be returned by next(). 
package Iterator; 
import java.util.*; 
public class Iterator1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  LinkedList dd = new LinkedList(); 
  dd.add(301); 
  dd.add("Teja"); 
  dd.add("Section"+'A'); 
  dd.add(3000+"$"); 
  dd.add("Rjy"); 
  System.out.println("<---For Loop--->"); 
  for(int i=0; i<=dd.size()-1;i++) 
  { 
   System.out.println(dd.get(i)); 
  } 
  System.out.println("<----For Each---->"); 
  for (Object o : dd) { 
   System.out.println(o); 
  } 
  System.out.println("<-----Iterator----->"); 
  Iterator iter = dd.iterator(); 
  while (iter.hasNext()) 
  { 
   System.out.println(iter.next()); 
  } 
 } 
}

Rjy 
int previousIndex(): 
Returns the index of the element that would be returned by previous(). 
void add(E e): 
Inserts the specified element into the list. 
void remove(): 
Removes the last element returned by either next() or previous(). 
void set(E e): 
Replaces the last element returned by next() or previous() with the specified element. 
Fail-Safe: 
In a fail-safe collection, iterators are designed to operate on a copy of the collection's data 
rather than the actual data structure. This means that modifications to the collection do not 
throw concurrent modification exceptions during iteration. 
The advantage of fail-safe iterators is that they don't compromise the integrity of the 
collection, even if it's modified while being iterated. However, this comes at the cost of 
potentially working with stale data. 
Java's CopyOnWriteArrayList is an example of a fail-safe collection. It creates a new copy 
of the underlying array whenever a modification is made, allowing concurrent reads without 
interference. 
package Iterator; 
import java.util.*; 
public class Iterator1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  LinkedList dd = new LinkedList(); 
  dd.add(301); 
  dd.add("Teja"); 
  dd.add("Section"+'A'); 
  dd.add(3000+"$"); 
  dd.add("Rjy"); 
  System.out.println("<-------ListIterator-------->"); 
  ListIterator list =dd.listIterator(dd.size()); 
  while(list.hasPrevious()) // printing reverse direction 
  { 
   System.out.println(list.previous()); 
  } 
  System.out.println("<-----Decending Iterator ---->"); 
  Iterator iters = dd.descendingIterator(); 
  while(iters.hasNext()) 
  { 
   System.out.println(iters.next()); 
  } 
 } 
}

Fail-Fast: 
In a fail-fast collection, iterators are designed to throw a ConcurrentModificationException if the 
collection is modified while an iterator is in progress. This ensures that any concurrent modifications 
are immediately detected. 
The advantage of fail-fast behavior is that it helps catch potential issues early during development, 
making it easier to identify and fix problems. However, it might cause the iteration to fail if 
modifications are made concurrently. 
Most of the standard Java collections (like ArrayList, HashSet, etc.) are fail-fast. 
Code Example: 
package Iterator; 
import java.util.ArrayList; 
import java.util.Iterator; 
import java.util.concurrent.CopyOnWriteArrayList; 
public class Fail_Safe { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  ArrayList list = new ArrayList (); 
  list.add(25); 
  list.add(75); 
  list.add(35); 
  list.add(45); 
  list.add(55); 
  /** for(int i=0;i<=list.size();i++)  
              { System.out.println(list.get(i)); 
   * list.add(99); } 
   */ 
 CopyOnWriteArrayList cpl = new CopyOnWriteArrayList(); 
  cpl.add(75); 
  cpl.add(35); 
  cpl.add(45); 
  cpl.add(55); 
  Iterator iter = cpl.iterator(); 
  while(iter.hasNext())  
  { 
   System.out.println(iter.next()); 
   cpl.add(65); 
   cpl.add(105); 
   cpl.add(205); 
  } 
 } 
} 
It is a Structural Modification and never 
ending loop: 
for(int i=0;i<=list.size();i++) 
{ 
System.out.println(list.get(i)); 
list.add(99); 
} 
package Iterator;

public class Fail_Fast { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  ArrayList list = new ArrayList (); 
  list.add(25); 
  list.add(75); 
  list.add(35); 
  list.add(45); 
  list.add(55); 
  Iterator irt = list.iterator(); 
  while(irt.hasNext()) 
  { 
   System.out.println(irt.next()); 
   list.add(95); 
  } 
 } 
}

Enumeration: 
Enumeration is an interface in Java that is part of the legacy java.util package. It was the original 
interface for iterating over collections, introduced in Java 1.0. The Enumeration interface is 
considered less powerful than the more modern Iterator interface and is largely superseded by it. 
However, it is still used in some older classes and methods. 
boolean hasMoreElements(): 
Returns true if the enumeration contains more elements; otherwise, it returns false. 
E nextElement(): 
Returns the next element in the enumeration. 
Final Over view: 
package Iterator; 
import java.util.*; 
public class Enumeratione { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Vector ves = new Vector(); 
  ves.add(43); 
  ves.add(77); 
  ves.add(44); 
  ves.add(92); 
  System.out.println("This an Enumeration"); 
  Enumeration en = ves.elements(); 
  while(en.hasMoreElements()) 
  { 
   System.out.println(en.nextElement()); 
  } 
 } 
}

Maps: 
In Java, you can work with maps using the Map interface and its various implementations. The Map 
interface is part of the Java Collections Framework and provides a way to store key-value pairs. 
Some common implementations of the Map interface include HashMap, TreeMap, LinkedHashMap, 
and Hashtable.  
Here's a brief overview and example of using HashMap: 
How the Data Elements  are Storeing in the map: 
Map methods ------------------- 
1.It contains 12 methods which is common for all the 
implementation Map Objects 
a. Object put(Object key,Object value) // To add key,value pair 
b. void putAll(Map m) // To add another map 
c. Object get(Object key) // To get the value based on key 
d. Object remove(Object key) //To remove an entry based on key 
e. boolean containsKey(Object key) //Check whether it contains  
key or not 
f. boolean containsValue(Object 
value)//Check whether it contains value or 
not 
g. boolean isEmpty() //To check wheter the 
Map is empty or not 
h. int size() //To get the size of a Map 
i. void clear() //To remove all Entry from a 
map 
views of a Map 
j.Set keySet() //Convert the key's of Map into Set for reading purpose 
k.Collection values() //Convert the values of Map into Collection for reading 
purpose 
l.Set entrySet() // Convert whole Entry of Map into Set for reading purpose. 
Entry(I) 
======= 
1. Each key-value pair is called Entry. 
2. Without existence of Map,there can't be existence of Entry Object. 
3. Interface entry is defined inside Map interface. 
interface Map 
{ 
 interface Entry 
 { 
  Object getKey(); //To get the key using Map.Entry Object 
  Object getValue();//To get the value using Map.Entry Object 
  Object setValue(Object newValue);//To update the value Using Map.Entry 
  Object 
 } 
} 
package Hash_MAP; 
import java.util.*; 
import java.util.Map.Entry; 
public class Hash_map1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  HashMap hmap  = new HashMap(); 
  hmap.put(10,"Sachin"); 
  hmap.put(18,"Kohli"); 
  hmap.put(07,"Dhoni"); 
  hmap.put(37,"Raina"); 
  hmap.put(95,"Dhawan"); 
  hmap.put(42,"Rohit Sharama"); 
  System.out.println(hmap);//hmap.toString() will be Called 
  System.out.println("****************************"); 
  System.out.println("-----TO Call Individual----"); 
  System.out.println(hmap.get(18)); 
  //Method Get Executed and the Object is created at the Run Time. 
  System.out.println("-----SET-----"); 
  Set set = hmap.keySet(); // To Get the Key From Entry Set... 
  System.out.println(set); 
  System.out.println(set.getClass().getName()); 
  System.out.println("---To Get Values----"); 
  Collection c = hmap.values(); // To Get Values From the Map 
  System.out.println(c); 
  System.out.println(c.getClass().getName()); 
  System.out.println("---TO GET MAP ENTRY SET----"); 
  Set mapData = hmap.entrySet(); 
  System.out.println(mapData); 
  System.out.println(mapData.getClass().getName()); 
  System.out.println("--USING ITERATOR --While Loop Starts--"); 
  Iterator itr = set.iterator(); 
  while(itr.hasNext()) 
  { 
   System.out.println(hmap.get(itr.next())); 
  } 
  System.out.println("*****Iterating By USING MAPDATA******"); 
  Iterator map_DATA = mapData.iterator(); 
  while(map_DATA.hasNext()) 
  { 
   Map.Entry data = (Entry) map_DATA.next(); 
   System.out.println(data.getKey()+" : "+data.getValue()); 
   if (data.getKey().equals(10))  
   { 
    data.setValue("Arjun"); 
    System.out.println("---Sucessfully Element Update ---"); 
    System.out.println(data.getKey()+" : "+data.getValue()); 
   } 
  } 
  System.out.println("---UPDATED MAP-----"); 
  System.out.println(hmap); 
 } 
} 
*****Out put*****

7=Dhoni, 10=Sachin,

95=Dhawan}

LinkedHashMap :  
LinkedHashMap is another implementation of the Map interface in Java, and it extends HashMap. It 
maintains a doubly-linked list of the entries in the order in which they were inserted into the map. This 
means that when you iterate over the entries, they are returned in the order in which they were added. 
HashMap 
======= 
Underlying DataStructure: Hashtable 
insertion order : not preserved 
duplicate keys : not allowed 
duplicate values : allowed 
Heterogenous objects : allowed 
null insertion : for keys allowed only once,but for values can be any no. 
implementation interface: Serializable,Cloneable. 
HashMap HashTable 
 All the methods are not synchronized. 
 At a time multiple threads can operate on 
a Object, so it is not ThreadSafe. 
 Pefromance is high. 
 null is allowed for both keys and values. 
 Introduced in 1.2v 
 All the methods are synchronzied. 
 At a time only one Thread can operate on 
a Object, so it is ThreadSafe. 
 Performance is low. 
 null is not allowed for both keys and 
values,it would result in 
NullPointerException. 
 Introduced in 1.0v 
Constructors 
============ 
1. HashMap hm=new HashMap() 
//default capacity => 16, loadfactor => 0.75(upon increase of data by  75% automatically size of 
HashMap will be doubled) 
2. Hashmap hm=new HashMap(int capacity); 
3. HashMap hm=new HashMap(int capacity,float fillration); 
4. HashMap hm=new HashMap(Map m); 
HashMap LinkedHashMap 
 underlying datastructure is hashtable. 
 insertion order not preserved. 
 introduced in 1.2v 
 Generally has better performance for 
basic operations like insertion, deletion, 
and retrieval. It has constant-time average 
complexity for these operations. 
 It is the child class of HashMap. 
 underlying datastructure is LinkedList + 
hashtable. 
 insertion order preserved. 
 introduced in 1.4v 
 May have slightly lower performance 
compared to HashMap due to the 
additional overhead of maintaining the 
linked list. 
Code Example: 
IdentityHashMap: 
IdentityHashMap is another implementation of the Map interface in Java, but it differs from 
HashMap and LinkedHashMap in terms of how it compares keys. Instead of using the equals() 
method to check for equality, IdentityHashMap uses reference equality (i.e., it compares the memory 
addresses of the key objects) to determine if two keys are the same. 
package Hash_MAP; 
import java.util.Collection; 
import java.util.HashMap; 
import java.util.Iterator; 
import java.util.LinkedHashMap; 
import java.util.LinkedHashSet; 
import java.util.Map; 
import java.util.Set; 
import java.util.Map.Entry; 
public class Linked_hashMap { 
 public static void main(String args[]) 
 { 
  LinkedHashMap lhamp = new LinkedHashMap(); 
  lhamp.put(10,"Sachin"); 
  lhamp.put(18,"Kohli"); 
  lhamp.put(07,"Dhoni"); 
  lhamp.put(37,"Raina"); 
  lhamp.put(95,"Dhawan"); 
  lhamp.put(42,"Rohit Sharama"); 
  Set set = lhamp.keySet(); // To Get the Key From Entry Set... 
  System.out.println(set); 
  System.out.println(set.getClass().getName()); 
  System.out.println("---To Get Values----"); 
  Collection c = lhamp.values(); // To Get Values From the Map 
  System.out.println(c); 
  System.out.println(c.getClass().getName()); 
  System.out.println("*****Iterating By USING MAPDATA******"); 
  Set mapData = lhamp.entrySet(); 
  Iterator map_DATA = mapData.iterator(); 
  while(map_DATA.hasNext()) 
  { 
   Map.Entry data = (Entry) map_DATA.next(); 
   System.out.println(data.getKey()+" : "+data.getValue()); 
  } 
 } 
}

import java.util.*; 
public class HashManDUP { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  HashMap dub = new HashMap(); 
  // Creating the Key 
  Integer i1 = new Integer(21); 
  Integer i2 = new Integer(21); 
  //Adding data to hashMap 
  dub.put(i1,"Sachin"); 
  dub.put(i2, "Kohli"); 
  System.out.println(dub); 
 } 
}

With Using Identity HashMap: 
package Hash_MAP; 
import java.util.HashMap; 
import java.util.IdentityHashMap; 
public class Identity_hashMap { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  IdentityHashMap identmap = new IdentityHashMap(); 
  // Creating the Key 
  Integer i1 = new Integer(21); 
  Integer i2 = new Integer(21); 
  //Adding data to hashMap 
  identmap.put(i1,"Sachin"); 
  identmap.put(i2, "Kohli"); 
  System.out.println(identmap); 
 } 
} 
Out Put: 
{21=Sachin, 21=Kohli} 
 i1==i2(false) 
IdentityHashMap 
=============== 
It is same as HashMap, with the following differences 
a. In case of HashMap,jvm will use equals() to check whether the keys are 
duplicated or not. 
equals() => meant for ContentComparison. 
b. In case of IdentityHashMap,jvm wil use == operator to identify whether the keys 
are duplicated.

Garbage collector actions 
package Hash_MAP; 
import java.util.*; 
class Test { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception { 
  Employee e = new Employee(); 
  e = null;// Garbage object 
     System.gc();// Informing JVM to active GC thread to clean garbage object 
  Thread.sleep(5000); 
 } 
} 
class Employee { 
 @Override 
 public void finalize() { 
  System.out.println("Cleaning the object"); 
 } 
} 
public class Garbage_collector_Action 
{ 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception { 
  Test ts = new Test(); 
  ts.main(args); 
 } 
} 
Out put: 
Cleaning the object 
package Hash_MAP; 
import java.util.*; 
public class GC2 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception { 
  HashMap hm = new HashMap(); 
  Temp t = new Temp(); 
  hm.put(t, "shri"); 
  System.out.println(hm);// {temp=shri} 
  t = null;// Making eligible for Garbage Collection 
  System.gc();// Triggering garbage collector thread to clean 't' 
  Thread.sleep(5000); 
  System.out.println(hm);// {temp=shri} 
 } 
} 
class Temp { 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "temp"; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public void finalize() { 
  System.out.println("cleaning temp object"); 
 } 
} 
Out Put:  
{temp=shri} 
{temp=shri} 
 InThis Example Garbage collector is Not Cleaning the 
Object Hash map is Not allowing It 
TO Over Come this Weak Hash Map Comes Into 
Picture. 
Weak Hash Map: 
It is exactly same as HashMap, with the following differences. 
1. HashMap will always dominate Garbage Collector, that is if the Object is a part of HashMap and 
if the Object is Garbage Object, still Garbage Collector won't remove that Object from heap since it 
is a part of HashMap. HashMap dominates GarbageCollector. 
2. Garbage Collector will dominate WeakHashMap, that is if the Object is part of WeakHashMap 
and if that Object is Garbage Object, then immediately Garbage Collector will remove that Object 
from heap even though it is a part of WeakHashMap, so we say Garbage Collector 
dominates"WeakHashMap". 
Code Example: 
package Hash_MAP; 
import java.util.*; 
public class Weak_hash_Map { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception { 
  WeakHashMap  hm = new  WeakHashMap(); 
  Temp t = new Temp(); 
  hm.put(t, "shri"); 
  System.out.println(hm);// {temp=shri} 
  t = null;// Making eligible for Garbage Collection 
  System.gc();// Triggering garbage collector thread to clean 't' 
  Thread.sleep(5000); 
  System.out.println(hm);// {temp=shri} 
 } 
} 
class Temp2 { 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "temp"; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public void finalize() { 
  System.out.println("cleaning temp object"); 
 } 
} 
Out Put: 
{temp=shri} 
cleaning temp object

OverView: 
Hashtable: 
=> The Underlying Data Structure for Hashtable is Hashtable Only. 
=> Duplicate Keys are Not Allowed. But Values can be Duplicated. 
=> Insertion Order is Not Preserved and it is Based on Hashcode of the Keys. 
=> Heterogeneous Objects are Allowed for Both Keys and Values. 
=> null Insertion is Not Possible for Both Key and Values. Otherwise we will get Runtime 
Exception    Saying NullPointerException. 
=> It implements Serializable and Cloneable,but not RandomAccess. 
=> Every Method Present in Hashtable is Synchronized and Hence Hashtable Object is Thread Safe. 
Constructors: 
1) Hashtable h = new Hashtable(); 
Creates an Empty Hashtable Object with Default Initial Capacity 11 and 
Default Fill Ratio 0.75. 
2) Hashtable h = new Hashtable(intinitialcapacity); 
3) Hashtable h = new Hashtable(intinitialcapacity, float fillRatio); 
4) Hashtable h = new Hashtable(Map m); 
package Hash_MAP; 
import java.util.*; 
public class HashCode { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Hashtable hm = new Hashtable();// Default capacity is 11 
  hm.put(new Temps(5), "A"); 
  hm.put(new Temps(2), "B"); 
  hm.put(new Temps(6), "C"); 
  hm.put(new Temps(15), "D"); 
  hm.put(new Temps(23), "E"); 
  hm.put(new Temps(16), "f"); 
  System.out.println(hm); 
  HashCode hc = new HashCode(); 
  System.out.println(hc.getClass().getName()+"@"+Integer.toHexString(hc.hashCode())); 
 } 
} 
class Temps { 
 int i; 
 Temps(int i) { 
  this.i = i; 
 } 
 public int hashCode() { 
  return i; 
 } 
 public String toString() { 
  return i + " "; 
 } 
} 
OUT Put: 
{6 =C, 16 =f, 5 =A, 15 =D, 2 =B, 23 =E} 
Hash_MAP.HashCode@2c7b84de 
Properties: 
In Java, the Properties class is a subclass of Hashtable. It is used to maintain lists of key-value pairs, where 
both the keys and values are strings. Properties is often used to manage application configuration settings, 
such as database connection parameters, system properties, or application-specific settings. 
Here are some key points about Properties: 
Key-Value Pairs: 
Like Hashtable, Properties also stores key-value pairs. 
Both the keys and values in a Properties object must be strings. 
Loading and Saving: 
Properties provides methods to load properties from an input stream (load() method) and save properties to 
an output stream (store() method). 
This makes it easy to read properties from a file and write properties back to a file. 
Default Values: 
Properties can have default values, which are used if no value is associated with a particular key. 
You can set default values using the setProperty() method. 
Concurrency: 
Like Hashtable, Properties is synchronized, which means it is thread-safe for use in multi-threaded 
environments. 
However, it's worth noting that for newer applications, ConcurrentHashMap might be preferred for better 
concurrency performance. 
System Properties: 
Properties can also be used to manage system properties. The System.getProperties() method returns a 
Properties object containing all the system properties. 
package Hash_MAP; 
import java.util.*; 
import java.io.*; 
public class JavaProperties { 
 FileInputStream inputStream; 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException { 
  Properties propertiesfile = new Properties(); // Properties Object is created 
  //Creating a FileInputStream to read the data from a file called 
"database.properties" 
  FileInputStream inputStream = new FileInputStream("D://Java notes and INEURON 
Daily live classes//JAVA Pdfs/database.properties"); 
  //Data loaded into properties object throug inputStream 
  propertiesfile.load(inputStream); 
  System.out.println(propertiesfile); 
  System.out.println("---Get the data from file---"); 
  System.out.println("================================"); 
  System.out.println("URL is :: "+propertiesfile.getProperty("Url")); 
  System.out.println("USER is :: "+propertiesfile.getProperty("User")); 
  System.out.println("PASSWORD is :: "+propertiesfile.getProperty("password")); 
  System.out.println(); 
  System.out.println("---Updateing the data from file---"); 
  System.out.println("================================"); 
  // Setting new Propertity i.e adding the new Data to the file 
  propertiesfile.setProperty("Student", "Sai Teja"); 
  propertiesfile.setProperty("Sports", "Table Tennis"); 
  FileOutputStream outputStream = new FileOutputStream("D://Java notes and INEURON 
Daily live classes//JAVA Pdfs/database.properties"); 
  propertiesfile.store(outputStream,"Map Got Concluded"); 
  System.out.println(propertiesfile); 
  System.out.println("URL is :: "+propertiesfile.getProperty("Url")); 
  System.out.println("USER is :: "+propertiesfile.getProperty("User")); 
  System.out.println("PASSWORD is :: "+propertiesfile.getProperty("password")); 
  System.out.println("Student is :: "+propertiesfile.getProperty("Student")); 
  System.out.println("Sports is :: "+propertiesfile.getProperty("Sports")); 
 } 
}

Type safety 
Type safety in Java refers to the compiler's ability to detect and prevent type-related errors at compile 
time, thus reducing the likelihood of runtime errors such as type casting exceptions. Java's type system 
provides. 
Case 1: Type-Safety 
 Arrays are always type safe that is we can give the guarantee for the type ofelements present 
inside array. 
 For example if our programming requirement is to hold String type of objects it is 
recommended to use String array. 
 In the case of string array we can add only string type of objects by mistake if we are trying to 
add any other type we will get compile time error. 
example 
String name[] =new String[500]; 
name[0] = "Navin Reddy"; 
name[1] = "Haider"; 
name[2] = new Integer(100); //CE: incompatbile types found: java.lang.Integer and Type Casting is 
not Required. 
required: java.lang.String 
That is we can always provide guarantee for the type of elements present inside array and hence 
arrays are safe to use with respect to type that is arrays are type safe. 
But collections are not type safe that is we can't provide any guarantee for the type of elements present 
inside collection. 
For example if our programming requirement is to hold only string type of objects it is never 
recommended to go for ArrayList. 
By mistake if we are trying to add any other type we won't get any compile time error but the program 
may fail at runtime. 
Example: 
ArrayList al =new ArrayList(); 
al.add("NavinReddy"); 
al.add("Haider"); 
al.add(new Integer(10)); 
String name1 = (String)al.get(0); 
String name2 = (String)al.get(1); 
String name3 = (String)al.get(2);//Exception in thread "main" :: java.lang.ClassCastException  
java.lang.Integer cannot be cast to java.lang.String 
Hence we can't provide guarantee for the type of elements present inside. 
That is in collections type casting is bigger headache. 
To overcome the above problems of collections(type-safety, type casting)sun people 
introduced generics concept in 1.5v 
hence the main objectives of generics are: 
1. To provide type safety to the collections. 
2. To resolve type casting problems. 
Generics: 
Type safety in Java refers to the compiler's ability to detect and prevent type-related errors at compile 
time, thus reducing the likelihood of runtime errors such as type casting exceptions. Java's type system 
provides several features to ensure type safety:Generics in Java provide a way to create classes, 
interfaces, and methods that can work with any type while providing compile-time type safety. They 
allow you to abstract over types, making your code more reusable and flexible. 
Example: 
To hold only string type of objects we can create a generic version of ArrayList as 
follows. 
ArrayList<String> al =new ArrayList<String>(); 
al.add("NavinReddy"); 
al.add(10);//Compiletime Error : can't find symbol 
incompatible type: required java.lang.String found:int 
That is through generic syntax we can resolve type casting problems. 
For this ArrayList we can add only string type of objects by mistake if we are trying to add any other type we will get 
compile time error that is through generics we are getting type safety.At the time of retrieval it is not required to 
perform any type casting we can assign elements directly to string type variables. 
package Generics; 
import java.util.*; 
public class Genrics_syntax { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  //Generics Syntax 
  ArrayList<String> gen=new ArrayList<String>(); 
  gen.add("Kohli"); 
  gen.add("Raina"); 
  gen.add("Dhoni"); 
  System.out.println(gen); 
  //Type Casting is Not Required 
  String firstname = gen.get(0); 
  String lastname = gen.get(2); 
  System.out.println(firstname + " "+lastname); 
 } 
} 
Out Put: 
[Kohli, Raina, Dhoni] 
Kohli Dhoni 
Conclusions: 
1. Polymorphism concept is applicable only for the base type but not for parameter type[usage of parent 
reference to hold child object is called polymorphism]. 
|-> basetype 
eg: ArrayList<String> al =new ArrayList<String>(); 
|=> parameter type 
List<String> al =new ArrayList<String>(); 
Collection<String> al =new ArrayList<String>(); 
Collection<Object> al =new ArrayList<String>();//CE: incompatible types 
2.Collections concept applicable only for objects , Hence for the parameter type we can use any class or 
interface name but not primitive value(type).Otherwise we will get compile time error. 
eg: ArrayList<int> al =new ArrayList<int>();//CE: unexcpected type found:primitive required:reference. 
 Generic classes: 
Until 1.4v a non-generic version of ArrayList class is declared as follows. 
Example: 
class ArrayList{ 
 add(Object o); 
 Object get(int index); 
} 
add() method can take object as the argument and hence we can add any type of 
object to the ArrayList. 
Due to this we are not getting type safety. 
The return type of get() method is object hence at the time of retrieval compulsory 
we should perform type casting. 
But in 1.5v a generic version of ArrayList class is declared as follows. 
|=> Type parameter 
class ArrayList<T>{ 
 add(T t); 
 T get(int index) 
} 
Based on our requirement T will be replaced with our provided type. 
For Example to hold only string type of objects we can create ArrayList object as 
follows. 
Example: 
ArrayList<String> l=new ArrayList<String>();

 T obj;

  this.obj = obj; 
 } 
 public void show() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Type of an Object : "+obj.getClass().getName()); 
 } 
 public T getObj() 
 { 
  return obj; 
 } 
}

  Gen<Integer> gens =new Gen <Integer>(10); 
  gens.show(); 
  System.out.println(gens.getObj()); 
  System.out.println();

 }

Bounded types 
We can bound the type parameter for a particular range by using extends keyword 
such types are called bounded types. 
Example 1: 
class Test<T> 
{} 
Test <Integer> t1=new Test< Integer>();//valid 
Test <String> t2=new Test < String>();//valid 
Here as the type parameter we can pass any type and there are no restrictions hence 
it is unbounded type. 
Example 2: 
class Test<T extends X> 
{} 
If x is a class then as the type parameter we can pass either x or its child 
classes. 
If x is an interface then as the type parameter we can pass either x or its 
implementation classes. 
eg#1. 
class Test <T extends Number>{} 
class Demo{ 
 public static void main(String[] args){ 
 Test<Integer> t1 = new Test<Integer>(); 
 Test<String> t2 = new Test<String>(); //CE 
 } 
} 
eg#2. 
class Test <T extends Runnable>{} 
class Demo{ 
 public static void main(String[] args){ 
 Test<Thread> t1 = new Test<Thread>(); 
 Test<String> t2 = new Test<String>(); //CE 
 } 
} 
package Generics; 
//valid 
class Demo<T extends Number> 
{ 
} 
/* In-valid 
 * class sample<T implements new Runnable() { 
 *  
 * } 
 */ 
class Trail<T extends Runnable >{  //Valid 
} 
public class Generics2 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  //Demo<String> d6 = new Demo<String>();Invalid 
  Demo<Integer> d1 = new Demo<Integer>(); // valid 
  //Demo<Double> d3 = new Demo<Double>();Invalid 
  Demo<Number> d2 = new Demo<Number>(); 
  //Trail<String> t0 = new Trail<String>(); //Invalid 
  Trail<Runnable> t1 = new Trail<Runnable>(); //valid 
  Trail<Thread> t2 = new Trail<Thread>(); //valid 
 } 
} 
Keypoints about bounded types: ------------------------------------------ 
=> We can't define bounded types by using implements and super keyword 
=> But implements keyword purpose we can replace with extends keyword. 
eg: class Test<T implements Runnable>{}//invalid 
class Test<T super String>{}//invalid 
=> As the type parameter we can use any valid java identifier but it convention to 
use T always. 
eg: class Test<T>{} 
class Test<iNeuron>{} 
=> We can pass any no of type parameters need not be one. 
eg: class HashMap<K,V>{} 
HashMap<Integer,String> h=new HashMap<Integer,String>(); 
Which of the following are valid? 
class Test <T extends Number&Runnable> {}//valid(first class and then interface) 
class Test<T extends Number&Runnable&Comparable> {} //valid(first class and then multiple 
interfaces) 
class Test<T extends Number&String> {} //invalid(both are classes becoz multiple 
inheritance through class is not supported) 
class Test<T extends Runnable&Comparable> {}//valid (both are interfaces) 
class Test<T extends Runnable&Number> {}//invalid(first class then interface)
