Serialization: (1.1 v) 
=> The process of saving (or) writing state of an object to a file is called serialization but strictly 
speaking it is the process of converting an object from java supported form to either network supported 
form (or) file supported form. 
=> By using FileOutputStream and ObjectOutputStream classes we can achieve serialization process. 
|=> writeObject(Object obj) 
 Ex: using flipkart booking an iPhone and iPhone reaching to the user. -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- 
In Java, sterilization is not a common term. However, if you're referring to serialization, I can explain 
that! Serialization in Java is the process of converting an object into a byte stream, which allows the 
object to be saved to a file, sent over a network, or stored in a database. This byte stream can later be 
deserialized to recreate the original object. 
De-Serialization: 
=> The process of reading state of an object from a file is called DeSerialization but strictly speaking 
it is the process of converting an object from file supported form (or) network supported form to java 
supported form. 
=> By using FileInputStream and ObjectInputStream classes we can achieve DeSerialization. 
       |=> readObject() 
Deserialization in Java is the reverse of serialization. It involves converting a byte stream back into a 
Java object. Deserialization allows you to reconstruct an object that was previously serialized (saved 
as a byte stream), either from a file, database, or over a network. 
Here's how deserialization works in Java: 
Steps to Perform Deserialization 
 Read the byte stream (from a file or other source) containing the serialized object. 
 Convert the byte stream back into the original object. 
Serlization Code Example: 
package Serialization; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.FileOutputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectInputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectOutputStream; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
class Dog implements Serializable 
{ 
 int a=35; 
 int b=25; 
} 
public class Serialization1 { 
 public static void main(String[] args)throws Exception { 
  //Serialiation.... 
  Dog dog1 = new Dog(); 
  System.out.println("Serialization Started........."); 
  FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream("D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live 
classes\\IMP PDFS\\13th Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\Serlizationtest.ser"); 
  ObjectOutputStream ops = new ObjectOutputStream(fos); 
  ops.writeObject(dog1); 
  ops.close(); 
  System.out.println("......Serlization Ended"); 
  //DeSerialization.... 
  System.out.println("Deserlization Started........."); 
  FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live 
classes\\IMP PDFS\\13th Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\Serlizationtest.ser"); 
  ObjectInputStream ois = new ObjectInputStream(fis); 
  Dog dog2=(Dog)ois.readObject(); 
  ois.close(); 
  System.out.println("....DeSelization ended"); 
  System.out.println("Dog object data......."); 
  System.out.println(dog2.a+"\t"+dog2.b); 
  int c = dog2.a+dog2.b; 
  System.out.println("Value of c.... "+ c); 
 } 
} 
Out put: 
Serialization Started......... 
......Serlization Ended 
Deserlization Started......... 
....DeSelization ended 
Dog object data....... 
35 25 
Value of c.... 60 
.SerFile: 
 package Serialization; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.FileOutputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectInputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectOutputStream; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
class Nums implements Serializable{ 
 int a=35;int b=25; 
 Nums(){System.out.println("Nums Constructor called.....");} 
} 
class Cat implements Serializable{ 
 String animal = "Cat";String sound = "Moueee"; 
 Cat(){ System.out.println("Cat Constructor called....");} 
} 
public class Serialization2 { 
 public static void main(String[] args)throws Exception { 
  //Serialiation.... 
  Nums Nums1 = new Nums();Cat cat1 = new Cat(); 
  System.out.println("Serialization Started........."); 
  FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream("D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live classes\\IMP 
PDFS\\13th Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\Serlizationtest.ser"); 
  ObjectOutputStream ops = new ObjectOutputStream(fos); 
  ops.writeObject(Nums1); 
  ops.writeObject(cat1); 
  ops.close(); 
  System.out.println("......Serlization Ended"); 
  //DeSerialization.... 
  System.out.println("Deserlization Started........."); 
  FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live classes\\IMP 
PDFS\\13th Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\Serlizationtest.ser"); 
  ObjectInputStream ois = new ObjectInputStream(fis); 
  Nums Nums2=(Nums)ois.readObject();Cat cat2 = (Cat)ois.readObject(); 
  ois.close(); 
  System.out.println("....DeSelization ended"); 
  System.out.println("Nums object data......."); 
  System.out.println(Nums2.a+"\t"+Nums2.b); 
  int c = Nums2.a+Nums2.b; 
  String animal = cat2.animal+" makes Sound "+cat2.sound; 
  System.out.println("Value of c.... "+ c); 
  System.out.println(animal); 
 } 
} 
Out put: 
Nums Constructor called..... 
Cat Constructor called.... 
Serialization Started......... 
......Serlization Ended 
Deserlization Started......... 
....DeSelization ended 
Nums object data....... 
35 25 
Value of c.... 60 
Cat makes Sound Moueee 
.serFile: 
Note: if we are trying to serialize multiple classes, the order of serialization of the class should follow 
the order of deserialization. Example: If class A{ is serialized first and class B is serialized, the 
deserialization should follow the same way... or else if we are deserialization first for class B and then 
class A, it will cause the below error. Exception in thread "main" java.lang. ClassCastException: class 
Serialization. Nums cannot be cast to class Serialization.Cat (Serialization. Nums and Serialization. 
Cats are in the unnamed module of loader 'app'. 
    at Serialization.Serialization2.main(Serialization2.java:42) 
Key points 
1. We can perform serialization only for serializable objects. 
2. An object is said to be serializable if and only if the corresponding class implements a serializable 
interface. 
3. A serializable interface is present in the Java.io package and does not contain any methods.   It is a 
marker interface. The required ability will be provided automatically by JVM. 
4. We can add any number . of objects to the file and we can read all those objects fromthe file, but in 
which order we wrote objects in the same order, only the objects will come back. That is, order is 
important. if There is a mismatch in order; it would result in "ClassCastException". 
5. If we are trying to serialize a non-serializable object, then we will get RuntimeException saying 
"NotSerializableException"

Transient keyword: 
The transient keyword in Java is used to indicate that a field should not be serialized when an object 
is being serialized. When an object is serialized, all of its fields are converted into a byte stream 
except for those marked as transient. Fields marked as transient will not be part of the serialization 
process and will not be saved in the serialized object. When the object is deserialized, the transient 
fields are set to their default values (i.e., null for objects, 0 for integers, false for booleans, etc.). 
Why Use transient? 
There are several reasons to use the transient keyword: 
Security: You might have sensitive information, such as passwords, that you don't want to serialize 
and expose when saving or transmitting the object. 
Non-Serializable Fields: If a class contains a field that references an object which is not serializable 
(e.g., a Thread, Socket, or other system resources), you can mark those fields as transient to avoid 
issues during serialization. 
Transient keyword: 
1. transient is the modifier applicable only for variables,but not for classes and methods. 
2. While performing serialization if we don't want to save the value of a particular variable to meet 
security constant such type of variable ,then we should declare that variable with "transient" keyword. 
3. At the time of serialization JVM ignores the original value of transient variable and save default 
value to the file . 
4. That is transient means "not to serialize". 
package Serialization; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.FileOutputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectInputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectOutputStream; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
class Numbers implements Serializable 
{ 
 int a=35; 
 transient int b=25; 
} 
public class TransientKeyWord { 
 public static void main(String[] args)throws Exception { 
  //Serialiation.... 
  Numbers Numbers1 = new Numbers(); 
  System.out.println("Serialization Started........."); 
  FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream("D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live classes\\IMP 
PDFS\\13th Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\Serlizationtest.ser"); 
  ObjectOutputStream ops = new ObjectOutputStream(fos); 
  ops.writeObject(Numbers1); 
  ops.close(); 
  System.out.println("......Serlization Ended"); 
  //DeSerialization.... 
  System.out.println("Deserlization Started........."); 
  FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live classes\\IMP 
PDFS\\13th Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\Serlizationtest.ser"); 
  ObjectInputStream ois = new ObjectInputStream(fis); 
  Numbers Numbers2=(Numbers)ois.readObject(); 
  ois.close(); 
  System.out.println("....DeSelization ended"); 
  System.out.println("Numbers object data......."); 
  System.out.println(Numbers2.a+"\t"+Numbers2.b); 
  int c = Numbers2.a+Numbers2.b; 
  System.out.println("Value of c.... "+ c); 
 } 
}

1. static variable is not part of object state hence they won't participate in serialization because of this declaring a static variable as transient there is 
no use.

Transient Vs Final: 
1. final variables will be participated into serialization directly by their values.Hence declaring a final variable as transient there is no use.  
 //the compiler assign the value to final variable 
eg: final int x= 10; 
int y = 20; 
System.out.println(x);// compiler will replace this as System.out.println(20) 
becoz x is final. 
System.out.println(y);

If we don't know the order of Serialization then we need to use the following code 
FileInputStream fis =new FileInputStream("abc.ser"); 
ObjectInputStream ois=new ObjectInputStream(fis); 
Object obj=ois.readObject();/runtime object can be Dog,Cat,Rat 
if(obj instanceof Dog){ 
Dog d=(Dog)obj;// parent type type casting 
//perform operation related to Dog 
} 
if(obj instanceof Cat){ 
Cat C=(Cat)obj; 
 //perform operation related to Cat 
} 
if(obj instanceof Rat){ 
 Rat r=(Rat)obj;

Object graph in serialization: 
1. Whenever we are serializing an object the set of all objects which are reachabl from that object will be serialized automatically. 
This group of objects is nothing but object graph in serialization. 
2. In object graph every object should be Serializable otherwise we will get runtime exception saying "NotSerializableException". 
Code Example:- 
package Serialization; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.FileOutputStream; 
import java.io.IOException; 
import java.io.ObjectInputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectOutputStream; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
class Wolf implements Serializable { 
 Goat c = new Goat(); 
} 
class Goat implements Serializable { 
 Tree r = new Tree(); 
} 
class Tree implements Serializable { 
 int i = 10; 
} 
public class ObjectGraphSerialization { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException, ClassNotFoundException { 
  Wolf d = new Wolf(); 
  System.out.println("Serialization Started"); 
  FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream("D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live 
classes\\IMP PDFS\\13th Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\Serlizationtest.ser"); 
  ObjectOutputStream oos = new ObjectOutputStream(fos); 
  oos.writeObject(d); 
  System.out.println("Serialization ended"); 
  System.out.println("***********************************"); 
  System.out.println("DeSerialization Started"); 
  FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live 
classes\\IMP PDFS\\13th Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\Serlizationtest.ser"); 
  ObjectInputStream ois = new ObjectInputStream(fis); 
  Wolf d1 = (Wolf) ois.readObject(); 
  System.out.println(d1.c.r.i); 
  System.out.println("DeSerialization ended"); 
 } 
}

package Serialization; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.FileOutputStream; 
import java.io.IOException; 
import java.io.ObjectInputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectOutputStream; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
class AccountHolder implements Serializable { 
    private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L;    
    private String name; 
    private transient String password; // 'transient' means this field won't be serialized    
    public AccountHolder(String name, String password) { 
        this.name = name; 
        this.password = password; 
    } 
    public String getName() { 
        return name; 
    } 
    public String getPassword() { 
        return password; 
    } 
} 
public class AccountandPassWord { 
    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception { 
        System.out.println("Serialization Started............");         
        // Creating an AccountHolder object 
        AccountHolder acp = new AccountHolder("Teja", "123456"); 
        AccountHolder acp2 = new AccountHolder("Surya","2657"); 
        // Serialization process - Saving the object to "account.ser" 
        try (FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream("D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live classes\\IMP PDFS\\13th 
Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\account.ser"); 
             ObjectOutputStream oos = new ObjectOutputStream(fos)) { 
            oos.writeObject(acp); 
            oos.writeObject(acp2); 
        } 
        System.out.println("....Serialization Ended");     
        System.out.println("DeSerialization Started........"); 
        // Deserialization process - Reading the object from "account.ser" 
        try (FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live classes\\IMP PDFS\\13th 
Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\account.ser"); 
             ObjectInputStream ois = new ObjectInputStream(fis)) { 
            AccountHolder ah = (AccountHolder) ois.readObject(); 
            AccountHolder ah2 = (AccountHolder) ois.readObject(); 
            System.out.println("....DeSerialization ended");        
            // Output the deserialized data 
            System.out.println("Account Holder name : " + ah.getName()); 
            System.out.println("Account Holder password : " + ah.getPassword());  // Will be null because 'password' is 
transient 
            System.out.println("Account Holder name : " + ah2.getName()); 
            System.out.println("Account Holder password : " + ah2.getPassword()); 
        } 
    } 
} 
Output: 
Serialization Started............ 
....Serialization Ended 
DeSerialization Started........ 
....DeSerialization ended 
Account Holder name : Teja 
Account Holder password : null 
Account Holder name : Surya 
Account Holder password : null 
* In the above example before serialization Account object can provide proper  
username and password. But after Deserialization Account object can provide only username but not 
password. This is due to declaring password as transient. Hence doing default serialization there may 
be a chance of loss of information due to transient keyword. 
* We can recover this loss of information by using customized serialization.We can implements 
customized serialization by using the following two methods. 
1. private void writeObject(ObjectOutputStream os) throws Exception.  
 * This method will be executed automatically by jvm at the time of serialization. 
 * It is a callback method. Hence at the time of serialization if we want to perform any extra work we 
have to define that in this  
 method only. (prepare encrypted password and write encrypted password seperate to the file )  
2. private void readObject(ObjectInputStream is) throws Exception.  
 * This method will be executed automatically by JVM at the time of Deserialization. Hence at the time 
of Deserialization if we want to perform any extra activity 
we have to define that in this method only. (read encrypted password , perform decryption and assign 
decrypted password  to the current object password variable ) 
This is code Example: 
class AccountHolder implements Serializable { 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 private String name; 
 private transient String password; // 'transient' means this field won't be serialized 
 public AccountHolder(String name, String password) { 
  this.name = name; 
  this.password = password; 
 } 
 public String getName() { 
  return name; 
 } 
 public String getPassword() { 
  return password; 
 } 
 private void writeObject(ObjectOutputStream oos) throws Exception { 
  oos.defaultWriteObject();// performing default Serialization 
  String epwd = "***" + password;// performing encryption 
  oos.writeObject(epwd);// write the encrypted data to file(abc.ser) 
 } 
 private void readObject(ObjectInputStream ois) throws Exception { 
  ois.defaultReadObject();// performing default Serialization 
  String epwd = (String) ois.readObject();// performing decryption 
  password = epwd.substring(3);// writing the extra data to Object 
 } 
} // Using this class in above class main method... 
Out put: 
Serialization Started............ 
....Serialization Ended 
DeSerialization Started........ 
....DeSerialization ended 
Account Holder name : Teja 
Account Holder password : 123456 
Account Holder name : Surya 
Account Holder password : 2657 
* At the time of Account object serialization JVM will check is there any writeObject() method in Account class or 
not. 
* If it is not available then JVM is responsible to perform serialization(default serialization). 
* If Account class contains writeObject() method then JVM feels very happy and executes that Account class 
writeObject() method. The same rule is applicable for readObject() method also. 
Adding Encripting pin: 
class AccountHolder implements Serializable { 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 private String name; 
 private transient String password; // 'transient' means this field won't be serialized 
 transient int pin=4444; 
 public AccountHolder(String name, String password) { 
  this.name = name; 
  this.password = password; 
 } 
 public String getName() { 
  return name; 
 } 
 public String getPassword() { 
  return password; 
 } 
 private void writeObject(ObjectOutputStream oos) throws Exception { 
  oos.defaultWriteObject();// performing default Serialization 
  String epwd = "***" + password;// performing encryption 
  int epin=1234+pin;//performing encryption 
  oos.writeObject(epwd);// write the encrypted data to file(abc.ser) 
  oos.writeInt(epin);//write the encrypted data to file(abc.ser 
 } 
 private void readObject(ObjectInputStream ois) throws Exception { 
  ois.defaultReadObject();// performing default Serialization 
  String epwd = (String) ois.readObject();// performing decryption 
  int epin=ois.readInt();//performing decryption 
  password = epwd.substring(3);// writing the extra data to Object 
  pin=epin-1234;//writing the extra data to Object 
 } 
}

Account Holder password : 123456 
Account Holder name : Surya 
Account Holder password : 2657 
Serialization with respective to Inheritance 
=============================== 
Case 1:  
If parent class implements Serializable then automatically every child class by default implements 
Serializable. That is Serializable nature is inheriting from parent to child.Hence even though child 
class doesn't implements Serializable , we can serialize child class object if parent class implements 
serializable interface. 
package Serialization;import java.io.FileInputStream;import java.io.FileOutputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectInputStream;import java.io.ObjectOutputStream;import java.io.Serializable; 
class Animal implements Serializable { 
    private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; // corrected serialVersionUID 
    public String animalType; 
    public String breed; 
    final int registrationFee = 50; // fixed spelling of registrationFee 
    public Animal(String animalType, String breed) { 
        this.animalType = animalType; 
        this.breed = breed; 
    } 
    public String getAnimalType() { 
        return animalType; 
    } 
    public String getBreedType() { 
        return breed; 
    } 
} 
class Cow extends Animal { // fixed "extends" 
    private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; // corrected serialVersionUID 
    String description; // added to store description 
    public Cow(String animalType, String breed) { 
        super( animalType,  breed); // by default it will take this.animalType = breed; 
        this.description = "This is a domestic Cow."; 
    } 
    int price = 200; 
} 
class Cats extends Animal { 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 String description; // added to store description 
    public Cats(String animalType, String breed) { 
     super( animalType,  breed);  // by default it will take this.animalType = breed; 
        this.description = "This is a domestic Cats."; 
    } 
    int price = 100; 
} 
public class SerializationWithInheritance { 
    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception { 
        String filepath = "D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live classes\\IMP PDFS\\13th Nov(Serialization and 
DeSerialization)\\animal.ser"; 
        Cow cow = new Cow("Cow","Jersey"); 
        Cats Cats = new Cats("Cat","British Shorthair"); 
        System.out.println("Serialization started....."); 
        FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream(filepath); 
        ObjectOutputStream oos = new ObjectOutputStream(fos); 
        oos.writeObject(cow); 
        oos.writeObject(Cats); 
        System.out.println("Serialization ended."); 
        oos.close(); 
        System.out.println("--------------------------------"); 
        System.out.println("Deserialization Started........"); 
        FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream(filepath); 
        ObjectInputStream ois = new ObjectInputStream(fis); 
        Cow cow1 = (Cow) ois.readObject(); 
        Cats Cats1 = (Cats) ois.readObject(); 
        ois.close(); 
        System.out.println("Deserialization ended."); 
        System.out.println(); 
        System.out.println("------Cow Details------"); 
        System.out.println("Regestration fee : "+cow1.registrationFee); 
        System.out.println("Animal Type: " + cow1.getAnimalType()); 
        System.out.println("Animal Breed: "+cow1.getBreedType()); 
        System.out.println("Description: " + cow1.description); 
        System.out.println("Price: " + cow1.price); 
        System.out.println("Total price : "+(cow1.registrationFee+cow1.price)+" $"); 
        System.out.println("------Cats Details------"); 
        System.out.println("Regestration fee : "+Cats1.registrationFee); 
        System.out.println("Animal Type: " + Cats1.getAnimalType()); 
        System.out.println("Animal Breed: "+Cats1.getBreedType()); 
        System.out.println("Description: " + Cats1.description); 
        System.out.println("Price: " + Cats1.price); 
        System.out.println("Total price : "+(Cats1.registrationFee+Cats1.price)+" $"); 
    } 
}

Case 2: 
1. Even though parent class does not implements Serializable we can serialize child object if child class 
implements Serializable interface. 
2. At the time of serialization JVM ignores the values of instance variables which are coming from non 
Serializable parent then instead of original value JVM saves default values for those variables to the file. 
3. At the time of Deserialization JVM checks whether any parent class is non Serializable or not.If any 
parent class is nonSerializable JVM creates a separate object for every  
non Serializable parent and shares its instance variables to the current object. 
4. To create an object for non-serializable parent JVM always calls no arg  
constructor(default constructor) of that non Serializable parent hence every non Serializable parent 
should compulsory 
contain no arg constructor otherwise we will get runtime exception "InvalidClassException". 
5. If case of non-serializable parent class then just instance control flow will be performed and share it's 
instance variable to the current object. 
package Serialization; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import java.io.FileOutputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectOutputStream; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectInputStream; 
import java.io.IOException; 
class Vehical { 
 int i = 10; 
 Vehical() { 
  System.out.println("No arg Vehical constructor"); 
 } 
} 
class Car extends Vehical implements Serializable { 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 int j = 20; 
 Car() { 
  System.out.println("No arg Car constructor"); 
 } 
} 
public class Testvehical { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException, ClassNotFoundException { 
  String filePath ="D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live classes\\IMP PDFS\\13th 
Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\Car.ser"; 
  Car d = new Car(); 
  d.i = 888; 
  d.j = 999; 
  System.out.println("Serialization started"); 
  FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream(filePath); 
  ObjectOutputStream oos = new ObjectOutputStream(fos); 
  oos.writeObject(d); 
  oos.close(); 
  System.out.println("Serialization ended"); 
  System.out.println("******************************"); 
  System.out.println("DeSerialization started"); 
  FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream(filePath); 
  ObjectInputStream ois = new ObjectInputStream(fis); 
  Car d1 = (Car) ois.readObject(); 
  ois.close(); 
  System.out.println(d1.i + "====> " + d1.j); 
  System.out.println("DeSerialization ended"); 
 } 
}

Externalization : ( 1.1 v ) 
1. In default serialization every thing takes care by JVM and programmer doesn't have any control. 
2. In serialization total object will be saved always and it is not possible to save part of the object , which creates performance problems at 
certain point. 
3. To overcome these problems we should go for externalization where every thing takes care by programmer and JVM doesn't have any 
control. 
4. The main advantage of externalization over serialization is we can save either total object or part of the object based on our requirement. 
5. To provide Externalizable ability for any object compulsory the corresponding class should implements externalizable interface. 
6. Externalizable interface is child interface of serializable interface. 
Externalizable interface defines 2 methods : 
1. writeExternal(ObjectOutput out ) throws IOException 
2. readExternal(ObjectInput in) throws IOException,ClassNotFoundException 
public void writeExternal(ObjectOutput out) throws IOException 
This method will be executed automaticcay at the time of Serialization with in this method , we have to write code to save required variables 
to the file . 
public void readExternal(ObjectInput in) throws IOException,ClassNotFoundException 
This method will be executed automatically at the time of deserialization with in this method , we have to write code to save read required 
variable from file and assign to the current object.At the time of deserialization JVM will create a seperate new object by executing  
public no-arg constructor on that object JVM will call  
readExternal() method. 
Every Externalizable class should compusory contains public no-arg constructor otherwise we will get RuntimeExcepion saying 
"InvaidClassException" . 
package Externalization; 
import java.io.Externalizable;import java.io.FileInputStream;import java.io.FileOutputStream;import 
java.io.IOException; 
import java.io.ObjectInput;import java.io.ObjectInputStream;import java.io.ObjectOutput;import 
java.io.ObjectOutputStream; 
class ExternalizableDemo implements Externalizable { 
 String i; 
 int j; 
 int k; 
 ExternalizableDemo(String i, int j, int k) { 
  this.i = i; 
  this.j = j; 
  this.k = k; 
 } 
 public ExternalizableDemo() { 
  System.out.println("Zero arg constructor"); 
 } 
//Performing Serialization as per our requirement 
 public void writeExternal(ObjectOutput out) throws IOException { 
  System.out.println("call back method used while Serialization"); 
  out.writeObject(i); 
  out.writeInt(j); 
  out.writeInt(k); 
 } 
//Performing DeSerialization as per our requirement 
 public void readExternal(ObjectInput in) throws IOException, ClassNotFoundException { 
  System.out.println("call back method used while DeSerialization"); 
  i = (String) in.readObject(); 
  j = in.readInt(); 
  k = in.readInt(); 
 } 
} 
public class Test { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException, ClassNotFoundException { 
  String filePath = "D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live classes\\IMP PDFS\\13th 
Nov(Serialization and DeSerialization)\\ExternalizationTest.ser"; 
  ExternalizableDemo d = new ExternalizableDemo("nitin", 100, 200); 
  System.out.println("Serialization started"); 
  FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream(filePath); 
  ObjectOutputStream oos = new ObjectOutputStream(fos); 
  oos.writeObject(d); 
  System.out.println("Serialization ended"); 
  System.out.println("******************************"); 
  System.out.println("DeSerialization started"); 
  FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream(filePath); 
  ObjectInputStream ois = new ObjectInputStream(fis); 
  d = (ExternalizableDemo) ois.readObject(); 
  System.out.println(d.i + "======>" + d.j + "======>" + d.k); 
  System.out.println("DeSerialization ended"); 
 } 
}

call back method used while 
Serialization

Zero arg constructor

DeSerialization 
nitin======>100======>200

Serialization Externalization 
1. It is meant for default Serialization  
2. Here every thing takes care by JVM and programmer 
doesn't have any control doesn't have any control. 
3. Here total object will be saved always and it is not 
possible to save part of the object. 
4. Serialization is the best choice if we want to save total 
object to the file. 
5. relatively performence is low. 
6. Serializable interface doesn't contain any method  
7. It is a marker interface. 
8. Serializable class not required to contains public no
arg constructor. 
9. transient keyword play role in serialization 
1. It is meant for Customized Serialization 
2. Here every thing takes care by programmer and JVM 
does not have any control. 
3. Here based on our requirement we can save either total 
object or part of the object. 
4. Externalization is the best choice if we want to save 
part of the object. 
5. relatively performence is high 
6. Externalizable interface contains 2 methods : 
 1. writeExternal()  
 2. readExternal() 
7. It is not a marker interface. 
8.Externalizable class should compulsory contains public 
no-arg constructor  
otherwise we will get  
 RuntimeException saying "InvalidClassException" 
9.transient keyword don't play any role in 
Externalization. 
Difference Between Serialization and Externalization 
SerialVersionUID :- 
================ 
* To perform Serialization & Deserialization internally JVM will use a unique identifier,which is nothing 
but serialVersionUID . 
* At the time of serialization JVM will save serialVersionUID with object. 
* At the time of Deserialization JVM will compare serialVersionUID and if it is matched then only object 
will be Deserialized otherwise we will get RuntimeException saying "InvalidClassException". 
The process in depending on default serialVersionUID are : 
1. After Serializing object if we change the .class file then we can't perform deserialization because of 
mismatch in serialVersionUID of local class and serialized object in this case at the time of Deserialization 
we will get RuntimeException saying in "InvalidClassException". 
2. Both sender and receiver should use the same version of JVM if there any incompatability in JVM 
versions then receive anable to deserializable because of different serialVersionUID , in this case receiver 
will get RuntimeException saying "InvalidClassException". 
3. To generate serialVersionUID internally JVM will use complexAlgorithm which may 
create performence problems. 
Serialization 
========== 
class Dog implements Serializable{ 
 public static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 int i=10; 
 int j=20; 
} 
FileOutputStream fos= new FileOutputStream("abc.ser"); 
ObjectOutputStream oos=new ObjectOutputStream(fos); 
oos.writeObject(d1); 
System.out.println("Serialization ended"); 
DeSerialization 
============= 
class Dog implements Serializable{ 
 public static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 int i=10; 
 int j=20; 
} 
System.out.println("Deserialization started"); 
FileInputStream fis=new FileInputStream("abc.ser"); 
ObjectInputStream ois=new ObjectInputStream(fis); 
Dog d2=(Dog) ois.readObject(); 
System.out.println("Deserialization ended"); 
We can solve above problems by configuring our own serialVersionUID . 
A real-time example of serialization and deserialization can be seen in distributed systems or applications where objects need to 
be transmitted over a network, stored on disk, or sent to a remote service for processing. 
Example: Session Management in Web Applications 
Scenario: 
When users log in to a website, their session data (like user ID, preferences, cart items, etc.) needs to be temporarily stored, so it 
can be retrieved later when they revisit the site or perform actions in their session. 
Since the web server may not always be the same (due to load balancing, cloud infrastructure, or restarts), user session data can 
be serialized and stored (in-memory, on disk, or in a database) and then deserialized when needed. This ensures that even if the 
server changes, the user session remains consistent. 
Example Code: Serialization and Deserialization of Session Data 
Let’s assume a scenario where we serialize a user session object and save it to a file, and then deserialize it when the user revisits 
the site to restore their session. 
package Serialization; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import java.io.FileOutputStream; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectOutputStream; 
import java.io.ObjectInputStream; 
import java.io.IOException; 
// UserSession class represents a user's session information 
class UserSession implements Serializable { 
    private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
    String userId; 
    String userName; 
    String preferences; 
    public UserSession(String userId, String userName, String preferences) { 
        this.userId = userId; 
        this.userName = userName; 
        this.preferences = preferences; 
    } 
    @Override 
    public String toString() { 
     System.out.println("Session serialVersionUID : "+serialVersionUID); 
        return "UserSession [userId=" + userId + ", userName=" + userName + ", preferences=" + preferences + "]"; 
    } 
} 
public class SessionManagementExample { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        // Simulating user session data 
        UserSession session = new UserSession("U12345", "John Doe", "Dark Mode, English"); 
        // Serialize the session data (saving it to disk or memory) 
        String sessionFile = "D:\\Java notes and INEURON Daily live classes\\IMP PDFS\\13th Nov(Serialization and 
DeSerialization)\\userSession.ser"; 
        try (FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream(sessionFile); 
             ObjectOutputStream oos = new ObjectOutputStream(fos)) { 
            System.out.println("Serializing user session data..."); 
            oos.writeObject(session); 
            System.out.println("User session serialized successfully."); 
        } catch (IOException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } 
        System.out.println("--------------------------------"); 
        // Deserialize the session data (retrieving it when the user returns) 
        try (FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream(sessionFile); 
             ObjectInputStream ois = new ObjectInputStream(fis)) { 
            System.out.println("Deserializing user session data..."); 
            UserSession deserializedSession = (UserSession) ois.readObject(); 
            System.out.println("Deserialized User Session: " + deserializedSession); 
        } catch (IOException | ClassNotFoundException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } 
    } 
} 
Out put: 
Serializing user session data... 
User session serialized successfully. -------------------------------- 
Deserializing user session data... 
Session serialVersionUID : 1 
Deserialized User Session: UserSession 
[userId=U12345, userName=John Doe, 
preferences=Dark Mode, English] 
Note : In the above program after serialization even though if we perform any change 
to UserSession.class file we can deserialize object. 
=> We can configure our own serialVersionUID both sender and receiver not required 
to maintain the same JVM versions. 
Note : some IDE's generate explicit serialVersionUID 
Cloning in Java refers to creating a copy of an object. Java provides two primary ways to achieve this: 
Clone () method: 
1. The process of creating exactly duplicate object is called cloning. 
2. The main objective of cloning is to maintain backup purposes.(i.e., if something goes wrong we can 
recover the situation by using backup copy.) 
3. We can perform cloning by using clone() method of Object class. 
Signature 
protected native object clone() throws CloneNotSupportedException; 
1. Shallow Copy 
A shallow copy of an object duplicates as much of the object as possible but does not create copies of the 
objects referenced by the original object’s fields (i.e., it copies the references). 
To create a shallow copy, an object should: 
Implement the Cloneable interface. 
Override the clone() method from the Object class. 
2. Deep Copy Cloneing: 
A deep copy involves copying all objects referenced by the fields of the original object, recursively. 
Each referenced object is also cloned.To create a deep copy, you may need to explicitly clone each 
object within the object being cloned. 
package com.Cloneing; 
class Employee implements Cloneable { 
    int id; 
    String name; 
    Employee(int id, String name) { 
        this.id = id; 
        this.name = name; 
    } 
    // Overriding the clone method to create a shallow copy 
    @Override 
    protected Object clone() throws CloneNotSupportedException { 
        return super.clone(); 
    } 
} 
public class Main { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        try { 
            Employee emp1 = new Employee(101, "John Doe"); 
            Employee emp2 = (Employee) emp1.clone(); // Shallow copy of emp1 
            emp2.id = 305; 
            emp2.name = "Jack lee"; 
            System.out.println("---Before Cloned Values----"); 
            System.out.println(emp1.id + " " + emp1.name);  
            System.out.println("---After Cloned Values----"); 
            System.out.println(emp2.id + " " + emp2.name);   
        } catch (CloneNotSupportedException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } 
    } 
} 
 ---Before Cloned Values---- 
101 John Doe ---After Cloned Values---- 
305 Jack lee 
package com.Cloneing; 
class Address implements Cloneable { 
    String city; 
    String country; 
    Address(String city, String country) { 
        this.city = city; 
        this.country = country; 
    } 
    @Override 
    protected Object clone() throws CloneNotSupportedException { 
        return super.clone(); 
    } 
} 
class Employees implements Cloneable { 
    int id; 
    String name; 
    Address address; 
    Employees(int id, String name, Address address) { 
        this.id = id; 
        this.name = name; 
        this.address = address; 
    } 
    // Deep copy by cloning the address object as well 
    @Override 
    protected Employees clone() throws CloneNotSupportedException { 
        Employees cloned = (Employees) super.clone(); 
        cloned.address = (Address) address.clone(); // Cloning the address object 
        return cloned; 
    } 
} 
public class DeepCopyCloning { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        try { 
            Address address = new Address("New York", "USA"); 
            Employees emp1 = new Employees(101, "John Doe", address); 
            Employees emp2 = emp1.clone(); // Deep copy of emp1 
            // Changing emp2's address 
            emp2.address.city = "Sydeny"; 
            emp2.address.country = "AUS"; 
            System.out.println("---Before Cloned Values----"); 
            System.out.println("emp1's Name : " + emp1.name); 
            System.out.println("emp1's ID : " + emp1.id); 
            System.out.println("emp1's City: " + emp1.address.city); 
            System.out.println("emp1's Country : " + emp1.address.country); 
            System.out.println("---After Cloned Values----"); 
            System.out.println("emp1's Name : " + emp2.name); 
            System.out.println("emp1's ID : " + emp2.id); 
            System.out.println("emp1's City: " + emp2.address.city); 
            System.out.println("emp1's Country : " + emp2.address.country); 
        } catch (CloneNotSupportedException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } 
    } 
} 
Out put: ---Before Cloned Values---- 
emp1's Name : John Doe 
emp1's ID : 101 
emp1's City: New York 
emp1's Country : USA ---After Cloned Values---- 
emp1's Name : John Doe 
emp1's ID : 101 
emp1's City: Sydeny 
emp1's Country : AUS 
KeyPoints about Cloneable interface: 
* We can perform cloning only for Cloneable objects. 
* An object is said to be Cloneable if and only if the corresponding class 
implements Cloneable interface. 
* Cloneable interface present in java.lang package and does not contain 
any methods.It is a marker interface where the required ability will be 
provided automatically by the JVM. 
* If we are trying to perform cloning on non-clonable objects then we will 
get RuntimeException saying "CloneNotSupportedException". 
The Singleton Design Pattern ensures that a class has only one instance throughout the application and 
provides a global point of access to that instance. Using factory methods, the creation of this instance 
can be controlled and customized. 
Steps to Implement Singleton Pattern using a Factory Method: 
Private Constructor: Restrict instantiation of the class from outside by making the constructor private. 
Private Static Instance: Hold the single instance in a private static variable. 
Public Static Factory Method: Provide a public method to return the instance, ensuring that only one 
instance is created. 
Example1: 
package SingleTonClass; 
class Sea { 
    private String sea; 
    private String fish; 
    // Step 2: Private static instance of Sea 
    private static Sea seaInstance = null; 
    // Step 1: Private constructor to enforce Singleton pattern 
    private Sea() { 
    } 
    // Optional: A constructor to set the sea and fish values 
    private Sea(String sea, String fish) { 
        this.sea = sea; 
        this.fish = fish; 
    } 
    // Getter methods 
    public String getSea() { //Test(){}//to avoid object creation by the user using new keyword 
        return sea; 
    } 
    public String getFish() { 
        return fish; 
    } 
    // Step 3: Public static factory method to provide the Singleton instance 
    public static Sea getSeaInstance(String sea, String fish) { 
        if (seaInstance == null) { 
            seaInstance = new Sea(sea, fish);  // Creates the instance only if it's null 
        } 
        return seaInstance; 
    } 
} 
public class SingleTonClass { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        // Getting the singleton instance of Sea 
        Sea seaInstance1 = Sea.getSeaInstance("Pacific", "Salmon"); 
        System.out.println("Sea: " + seaInstance1.getSea() + ", Fish: " + 
seaInstance1.getFish()); 
        // Attempting to get another instance with different values 
        Sea seaInstance2 = Sea.getSeaInstance("Atlantic", "Tuna"); 
        System.out.println("Sea: " + seaInstance2.getSea() + ", Fish: " + 
seaInstance2.getFish()); 
        // Both instances should point to the same object 
        System.out.println("Are both instances the same? " + (seaInstance1 == seaInstance2));  
// Output: true 
        // Checking Hash Code 
        System.out.println(seaInstance1.hashCode()); 
        System.out.println(seaInstance2.hashCode()); 
    } 
} 
Out put: 
Sea: Pacific, Fish: Salmon 
Sea: Pacific, Fish: Salmon 
Are both instances the same? true 
1995265320 
1995265320 
Different ways of Creating an Object 
1. using new Operator 
Test t=new Test(); 
2. using newInstance() 
Class.forName("com.abc.main.Test").newInstance() 
3. using clone() 
Test t2=(Test)t1.clone(); 
4. using factorymethods 
Runtime r=Runtime.getRuntime(); 
DateFormat df=DataFormat.getInstance(); 
5. using Serialization and DeSerialization 
FileInputStream fis=new FileInputStream("abc.ser"); 
ObjectInputStream ois=new ObjectInputStream(fis); 
Test t=(Test)ois.readObject(); 
Factory method: 
By using class name if we are calling a method and that method returns the same 
class object such type of method is called factory method. 
Example: 
Runtime r=Runtime.getRuntime();//getRuntime is a factory method. 
DateFormat df=DateFormat.getInstance(); 
If object creation required under some constraints then we can implement by using 
factory method. 
Calendar calendar = Calendar.getInstance();//static factory methods 
String result = "name".toUpperCase();//instance factory methods 
If the corresponding .class file not available at Runtime then we will get 
RuntimeException saying NoClassDefFoundError , It is unchecked. 
To used new operator the corresponding class not required to contain no argument 
constructor 
newInstance( ) 
============ 
newInstance( ) is a method , present in class Class , which can be used to create 
an object . 
We can use the newInstance( ) method , If we don't class name at the beginning and 
available dynamically Runtime. 
Object o=Class.forName(arg[0]).newInstance( ); 
If the corresponding .class file not available at Runtime then we will get 
RuntimeException saying ClassNotFoundException , It is checked. 
To used newInstance( ) method the corresponding class should compulsory contain no 
argument constructor , Other wise we will get 
RuntimeException saying InstantiationException. 
Difference between ClassNotFoundException & NoClassDefFoundError : 
1. For hard coded class names at Runtime in the corresponding .class files not 
available we will get NoClassDefFoundError , 
which is unchecked 
Test t = new Test( ); 
In Runtime Test.class file is not available then we will get "NoClassDefFoundError" 
2. For Dynamically provided class names at Runtime , If the corresponding .class 
files is not available then we will get the 
RuntimeException saying "ClassNotFoundException". 
Ex : Object o=Class.forname("Test").newInstance( ); 
At Runtime if Test.class file not available then we will get the 
"ClassNotFoundException" , which is checked exception. 
Difference between instanceof and isInstance( ) : 
instanceof 
instanceof an operator which can be used to check whether the given object is 
particular type or not We know at the type at 
beginning it is available. 
eg: String s = new String("sachin"); 
System.out.println(s instanceof Object );//true 
//If we know the type at the beginning only. 
isInstance( ) 
isInstance( ) is a method , present in class Class , we can use isInstance( ) 
method to checked whether the given object is particular type or 
not We don't know at the type at beginning it is available Dynamically at 
Runtime. 
class Test { 
public static void main(String[] args) { 
 Test t = new Test( ) ; 
 System.out.println(Class.forName(args[0]).isInstance(t));////arg[0] --- We 
 don't know the type at beginning 
 } 
} 
java Test Test //true 
java Test String //false 
java Test Object //true 
Design Patterns: 
In Java (and in general software development), Design Patterns are standard solutions to common 
problems in software design. They represent best practices that experienced developers use to design 
flexible, reusable, and maintainable code. 
�
� What is a Design Pattern? 
A Design Pattern is a general, reusable solution to a commonly occurring problem within a given 
context in software design. It is not code, but a template or description of how to solve a problem that 
can be used in many different situations. 
✅ Benefits of Using Design Patterns 
Reusability 
Better code readability and maintenance 
Standard terminology for developers 
Easier refactoring and enhancements 
Reduced complexity 
Types of Design Patterns in Java 
Design Patterns are mainly classified into three categories: 
1. Creational Design Patterns 
These patterns deal with object creation mechanisms, trying to create objects in a manner 
suitable to the situation. 
Pattern -  Description 
Singleton - Ensures a class has only one instance and provides a global point of access to it. 
Factory Method - Creates objects without specifying the exact class of object to create. 
Abstract Factory - Produces families of related objects without specifying their concrete 
classes. 
Builder - Builds a complex object step-by-step. 
Prototype     - Clones existing objects without creating new ones from scratch. 
2. Structural Design Patterns 
These patterns focus on how classes and objects are composed to form larger structures. 
Pattern   -   Description 
Adapter - Allows incompatible interfaces to work together. 
Bridge - Separates an object’s abstraction from its implementation. 
Composite - 
Composes objects into tree structures to represent part-whole hierarchies. 
Decorator - 
Facade 
Adds behavior to objects dynamically. - Provides a simplified interface to a complex system. 
Flyweight - Reduces memory usage by sharing common parts of objects. 
Proxy - A placeholder object to control access to another object. 
3. Behavioral  - Design Patterns 
These patterns focus on communication between objects. 
Pattern - Description 
Observer - Allows a subject to notify observers when its state changes. 
Strategy - Enables selecting an algorithm at runtime. 
Command - Encapsulates a request as an object. 
Chain of Responsibility  - Passes request along a chain of handlers. 
Iterator - Provides a way to access elements of a collection sequentially. 
Mediator - Centralizes communication between objects. 
Memento - Captures and restores an object’s internal state. 
State -  Allows an object to change its behavior when its internal state changes. 
Template Method - Defines the skeleton of an algorithm, deferring some steps to 
subclasses. 
Visitor - Separates an algorithm from an object structure on which it operates. 
Interpreter - Provides a way to evaluate language grammar or expressions. 
1. Singleton Pattern 
�
� Purpose: 
Ensure a class has only one instance, and provide a global point of access to it. 
✅ Use Cases: 
Logger classes 
Configuration classes 
Database connections. 
Code Example 1 :- 
package com.SingletonDesignPattern; 
public class Singleton { 
    // Step 1: Create a private static instance of the class 
    private static Singleton instance; 
    // Step 2: Private constructor prevents instantiation from other classes 
    private Singleton() { 
        System.out.println("Singleton instance created"); 
    } 
    // Step 3: Public method to provide access to the instance 
    public static Singleton getInstance() { 
        if (instance == null) { 
            instance = new Singleton(); 
        } 
        return instance; 
    } 
} 
package com.SingletonDesignPattern; 
public class SingletonMain { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Singleton obj1 = Singleton.getInstance(); 
        Singleton obj2 = Singleton.getInstance(); 
        System.out.println("Single Ton Design Class Started...!"); 
        System.out.println(obj1 == obj2); // Output: true (both point to 
the same object) 
    } 
} 
Out Put: 
Singleton instance created 
True 
s 
Example 2: 
package com.SingletonDesignPattern; 
public class Logger { 
    private static Logger instance; 
    private Logger() {} // Prevent instantiation 
    public static Logger getInstance() { 
        if (instance == null) { 
            instance = new Logger(); 
        } 
        return instance; 
    } 
    public void log(String message) { 
        System.out.println("[LOG] " + message); 
    } 
} 
package com.SingletonDesignPattern; 
public class App { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Logger logger1 = Logger.getInstance(); 
        Logger logger2 = Logger.getInstance(); 
        logger1.log("Application started."); 
        logger1.log("This is Single ton Class "+logger1); 
        System.out.println("---------------"); 
        logger2.log("Application started."); 
        logger1.log("This is Single ton Class "+logger2); 
        System.out.println(logger1==logger2); 
    } 
} 
Out Put:-- 
[LOG] Application started. 
[LOG] This is Single ton Class com.SingletonDesignPattern.Logger@2a84aee7 --------------- 
[LOG] Application started. 
[LOG] This is Single ton Class com.SingletonDesignPattern.Logger@2a84aee7 
True 
2. Factory Method Pattern 
�
� Purpose: 
Defines an interface for creating an object, but lets subclasses 
decide which class to instantiate. 
✅ Use Cases: 
When the type of object isn't known until runtime 
UI toolkits (buttons for Windows, Mac, Linux, etc.) 
Code Example: 
package FactoryMethodPattern; 
// Product interface 
public interface Animal { 
    void speak(); 
} 
// Concrete classes 
class Dog implements Animal { 
    public void speak() { 
        System.out.println("Woof!"); 
    } 
} 
class Cat implements Animal { 
    public void speak() { 
        System.out.println("Meow!"); 
    } 
} 
// Factory 
class AnimalFactory { 
    public static Animal getAnimal(String type) { 
        if ("dog".equalsIgnoreCase(type)) { 
            return new Dog(); 
        } else if ("cat".equalsIgnoreCase(type)) { 
            return new Cat(); 
        } 
        return null; 
    } 
} 
package FactoryMethodPattern; 
public class FactoryMain { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Animal a1 = AnimalFactory.getAnimal("dog"); 
        System.out.print("Animal Type : " );  // Output: Woof! 
        a1.speak(); 
        System.out.println(); 
        Animal a2 = AnimalFactory.getAnimal("cat"); 
        System.out.print("Animal Type : " ); 
        a2.speak();  // Output: Meow! 
    } 
} 
Out Put: 
Animal Type : Woof! 
Animal Type : Meow! 
2. Factory Pattern – Real-time Example: Shape Drawing App or 
Payment Gateway Integration 
�
� Use Case: 
In a drawing app, users can choose to draw a circle, square, or 
rectangle. You use a factory to generate the right shape based on user 
input. 
package FactoryMethodPattern; 
public interface Shape { 
    void draw(); 
} 
class Circle implements Shape { 
    public void draw() { 
        System.out.println("Drawing Circle..."); 
    } 
} 
class Rectangle implements Shape { 
    public void draw() { 
        System.out.println("Drawing Rectangle..."); 
    } 
} 
class ShapeFactory { 
    public static Shape getShape(String type) { 
        switch (type.toLowerCase()) { 
            case "circle": return new Circle(); 
            case "rectangle": return new Rectangle(); 
            default: return null; 
        } 
    } 
} 
package FactoryMethodPattern; 
public class DrawingApp { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Shape shape1 = ShapeFactory.getShape("circle"); 
        System.out.print("Shape Type : " ); 
        shape1.draw(); // Output: Drawing Circle... 
        Shape shape2 = ShapeFactory.getShape("rectangle"); 
        System.out.print("Shape Type : " ); 
        shape2.draw(); // Output: Drawing Rectangle... 
    } 
} 
Out put: 
Shape Type : Drawing Circle... 
Shape Type : Drawing Rectangle... 
3. Builder Pattern – Real-time Example: Building 
Complex Objects like User, Config, or HTTP 
Request 
�
� Use Case: 
Use this when you need to create an object with lots 
of optional fields (like creating a complex User or 
HTTP request). 
package BuilderPattern; 
public class User { 
    private String name; 
    private int age; 
    private String address; 
    private String phone; 
    private User(Builder builder) { 
        this.name = builder.name; 
        this.age = builder.age; 
        this.address = builder.address; 
        this.phone = builder.phone; 
    } 
    @Override 
    public String toString() { 
        return "User{name='" + name + "', age=" + age + ", address='" + address + "', phone='" + 
phone + "'}"; 
    } 
    public static class Builder { 
        private String name; 
        private int age; 
        private String address; 
        private String phone; 
        public Builder(String name) { 
            this.name = name; 
        } 
        public Builder age(int age) { 
            this.age = age; 
            return this; 
        } 
        public Builder address(String address) { 
            this.address = address; 
            return this; 
        } 
        public Builder phone(String phone) { 
            this.phone = phone; 
            return this; 
        } 
        public User build() { 
            return new User(this); 
        } 
    } 
} 
package BuilderPattern; 
public class Buildermain { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        User user = new User.Builder("John Doe") 
                        .age(30) 
                        .address("New York") 
                        .phone("123456789") 
                        .build(); 
        System.out.println("User created: " + user); 
    } 
} 
Out Put: 
User created: User{name='John Doe', 
age=30, address='New York', 
phone='123456789'} 
4. Strategy Pattern – Real-time Example: Payment Methods / Sorting Algorithms 
�
� Use Case: 
You want to dynamically switch between different algorithms or behaviors at runtime (like choosing 
between PayPal, Credit Card, UPI for payment). 
package StrategyPatterns; 
public interface PaymentStrategy { 
    void pay(int amount); 
} 
class CreditCardPayment implements PaymentStrategy { 
    public void pay(int amount) { 
        System.out.println("Paid " + amount + " using Credit Card."); 
    } 
} 
class PayPalPayment implements PaymentStrategy { 
    public void pay(int amount) { 
        System.out.println("Paid " + amount + " using PayPal."); 
    } 
} 
class ShoppingCart { 
    private PaymentStrategy paymentStrategy; 
    public void setPaymentStrategy(PaymentStrategy strategy) { 
        this.paymentStrategy = strategy; 
    } 
    public void checkout(int amount) { 
        paymentStrategy.pay(amount); 
    } 
} 
package StrategyPatterns; 
public class Main { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        ShoppingCart cart = new ShoppingCart(); 
        cart.setPaymentStrategy(new CreditCardPayment()); 
        cart.checkout(500); 
        cart.setPaymentStrategy(new PayPalPayment()); 
        cart.checkout(300); 
    } 
}
